Multi-user auth accepts the committed default SECRET_KEY, making session cookies forgeable

config.py:85 · reviewer: data-handling
What it is
config.py ships a hardcoded fallback signing key: `SECRET_KEY: str = os.environ.get("SECRET_KEY", "dev-insecure-change-me").strip()`. app.py passes it straight into `auth.install_auth(dash_app.server, users, secret_key=secret_key or config.SECRET_KEY)` (app.py ~137-141), and install_auth simply does `server.secret_key = secret_key` (auth.py:106) with no check that the value is not the public default. The gate itself only checks `session.get(_SESSION_KEY) in users` (auth.py:115), so anyone who can sign a Flask session cookie is fully authenticated. The docstrings say the key 'MUST be set to a stable, secret value in production' but nothing in code enforces or even warns about it, and fly.toml's [env] block does not set SECRET_KEY, so a deploy where the operator forgot `fly secrets set SECRET_KEY=...` runs multi-user auth on a key committed to a public GitHub repo.
Why it matters
The whole point of the gate (per auth.py's own docstring) is that the dashboard 'surfaces a coach's private third-party material' plus real opponent names and USCF records. With the known default key, an attacker can mint a valid `session["user"] = "<any configured username>"` cookie offline with itsdangerous/Flask and bypass login entirely — a user-isolation breach guarded only by an unenforced deployment convention.
How to fix
In build_app (or install_auth), when `users` is non-empty and the effective secret key equals the shipped default, refuse to start with a clear error (mirroring how parse_users fails loudly on a plaintext password). Optionally fall back to `secrets.token_hex(32)` per boot for the single-user dev case only.
Expected improvement
A misconfigured multi-user deployment fails loudly at boot instead of silently running with forgeable authentication over private coach material and opponent PII.
Evidence
config.py:85 `SECRET_KEY: str = os.environ.get("SECRET_KEY", "dev-insecure-change-me").strip()`; auth.py:106 `server.secret_key = secret_key`; auth.py:115 `if session.get(_SESSION_KEY) in users: return None`
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed against current code. config.py:85 has the exact hardcoded fallback "dev-insecure-change-me"; app.py:140 (inside the `if users and not demo_mode` block starting at 137) passes `secret_key or config.SECRET_KEY` into auth.install_auth, and the module-level boot at app.py:188 passes config.SECRET_KEY; auth.py:106 does `server.secret_key = secret_key` with no default-key check; auth.py:115 authenticates purely on `session.get(_SESSION_KEY) in users`, so anyone who can sign a session cookie with the committed key is fully logged in as any configured user. grep shows "dev-insecure" appears only in config.py — no code path, warning, or test enforces a real key when USERS is non-empty. fly.toml [env] (lines 6-19) indeed does not set SECRET_KEY (correct practice would be `fly secrets set`, but nothing enforces it). All cited line numbers accurate. Not fixed by PRs #82-#86 and not a duplicate of issues #80/#40. Severity high is appropriate: it only bites multi-user deployments (single-user runs ungated by design), but in that mode it is a complete auth bypass via a key committed to a public repo, guarding exactly the private coach material the gate exists to protect. Proposed fix (refuse to start when users is non-empty and key equals the default, mirroring parse_users' loud failure) is sound.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read config.py:70-99, app.py:120-160 and 188, auth.py:1-140, fly.toml, and grepped the repo for any enforcement of SECRET_KEY. All cited facts check out at the cited lines: config.py:85 has the committed fallback "dev-insecure-change-me"; app.py:140 passes `secret_key or config.SECRET_KEY` into install_auth (app.py:188 does the same on the serve path); auth.py's install_auth sets `server.secret_key = secret_key` with no default-key check, and the gate is just `session.get("user") in users`. No code anywhere warns or refuses on the default key — the only mitigations are prose: the config.py comment, install_auth's docstring, and README:151/205 telling operators to use `fly secrets set`. fly.toml's [env] indeed omits SECRET_KEY (correctly, since it's a secret), so a forgotten `fly secrets set SECRET_KEY` silently runs multi-user auth on the public key. Attack works as described: with the key known, itsdangerous can mint session={"user": "<configured username>"} offline; attacker needs a valid username, but usernames aren't secrets. The proposed fix is sound and consistent with the codebase's own pattern (parse_users in user_config raises loudly on a plaintext password, so a fail-fast on default-key + non-empty users mirrors existing style); the per-boot random-key fallback for the ungated single-user case is also fine since no gate exists then. Mitigating context (why one could argue medium): exploitation requires a multi-user production deploy whose operator ignored explicit README instructions, and demo mode / single-user mode has no gate at all so the key is irrelevant there. But because the gate exists precisely to protect a coach's private material and the failure is silent, high is defensible; keeping severity unchanged. No line/description corrections needed.

_safe_dirname collisions and '.'/'..' passthrough silently share per-user cache files between tenants

data.py:498-520, 549-553 · reviewer: multiuser-tenant-isolation
What it is
register_users() derives each user's private cache directory as os.path.join(base, _safe_dirname(username)), and _safe_dirname only maps disallowed characters to '_': re.sub(r"[^A-Za-z0-9_.-]", "_", username). Distinct configured usernames therefore collapse to the same directory: 'user a' and 'user_a' both become 'user_a'; 'a/b' and 'a b' both become 'a_b'. Nothing rejects the collision — parse_users (user_config.py:104-109) only rejects *exact* duplicate usernames, and register_users has no post-sanitization uniqueness check. Colliding users silently share games.pgn, uscf_cache.json, coach.pgn, and analysis_cache.json. Two aggravators: (1) '.' and '..' survive sanitization unchanged because dots are in the allowed class, so username '..' yields cache_path '.user-data/../games.pgn' — writing outside DATA_DIR into the app working directory, where it collides with the single-user default cache 'games.pgn'; username '.' collapses the user dir onto the base dir. (2) The duplicate check is case-sensitive while macOS dev filesystems are case-insensitive, so 'Daniel' and 'daniel' collide on a local multi-user run.
Why it matters
This is a silent tenant-isolation breach in the exact seam ADR 0005 promises to protect ('one user's accessors never return another user's data'). Concretely: if Lichess is unreachable at Sync time, _boot_from_cache (data.py:396-411) loads whatever games.pgn is at store.cache_path — with a collision that is the *other* user's full game history, served under this user's login. The shared uscf_cache.json is worse because it is read-write in normal operation, not just on outage: dismiss_reconciliation_entry (data.py:694) writes dismissals one user makes into the file the other user reads back at next Sync (data.py:301), and _detect_new_achievements (data.py:366-383) cross-pollutes seen-achievement state, suppressing or mislabeling the other tenant's celebrations. Failure is completely silent — no log, no error, no Reconciliation entry. Severity is high rather than critical only because usernames are operator-controlled config, not attacker-controlled input; but 'john smith' vs 'john_smith' is a plausible real config, and nothing warns the operator.
How to fix
Reject the problem at config parse or registration time, where the module already 'fails loudly rather than silently serving the wrong data' (user_config.py docstring). Two small changes: (a) in parse_users, validate usernames against a strict pattern (e.g. ^[A-Za-z0-9_.-]+$ excluding '.' and '..', optionally case-folded for uniqueness) so sanitization becomes a no-op; (b) in register_users, track {safe_dirname: username} and raise (or refuse to register the second user) on a post-sanitization collision as a hard error. Either alone closes the sharing hole; both together also document the invariant.
Expected improvement
A config whose usernames would share or escape a cache directory fails loudly at boot instead of silently cross-serving one tenant's games, dismissals, and achievement state to another.
Evidence
data.py:552 `safe = re.sub(r"[^A-Za-z0-9_.-]", "_", username)`; data.py:500 `user_dir = os.path.join(base, _safe_dirname(username))` then `cache_path=os.path.join(user_dir, "games.pgn")`; user_config.py:104-105 only `if record.username in users: raise UserConfigError(f"Duplicate username...")` — no post-sanitization or path check anywhere.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed against current code. data.py:552 has exactly `re.sub(r"[^A-Za-z0-9_.-]", "_", username)`; dots allowed so '.' and '..' pass through, and 'user a'/'user_a' collide. data.py:500 joins base with _safe_dirname(username) and derives all four per-user cache files from it; register_users (483-520) has no post-sanitization uniqueness check. user_config.py parse_users only rejects exact duplicate usernames; _require_str only strips whitespace — no format validation. Aggravators verified: dismiss_reconciliation_entry writes to the shared uscf_cache.json and dismissals are re-read at Sync; _detect_new_achievements reads/writes seen-achievement state in the same file; _boot_from_cache loads whatever PGN is at cache_path on outage. Cited line numbers are accurate. Not covered by excluded issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86 (those touched docs/CI/dead code, not data.py registration). Severity high is right: real tenant-isolation gap, but requires operator-configured colliding usernames, which the finding already prices in.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current code. data.py:552 _safe_dirname allows dots and maps everything else to '_' with no post-sanitization uniqueness check in register_users (data.py:499-520); user_config.py:104-109 only rejects exact duplicate usernames. Verified: 'user a'/'user_a' collide; '..' yields cache_path '.user-data/../games.pgn' (CWD, colliding with the single-user default cache); '.' collapses onto the base dir. All impact paths check out: _boot_from_cache (396-411) would serve the colliding user's games.pgn; uscf_cache.json is read-write in normal operation (dismissal write at 694, read-back at 301; achievement seen-state at 366-383). ADR 0005 explicitly promises per-user cache subdirectories 'so they never collide', so this violates a documented invariant, not an intentional design. No test or guard exists; not covered by excluded issues #40/#80 or PRs #82-#86. Line refs in the finding are all accurate. Severity: I suggest medium rather than high — usernames are exclusively operator-set config (USCF_DASHBOARD_USERS env), there is no attacker-controlled input or signup, and the deployment is effectively single-real-user; the realistic trigger is an operator misconfig ('john smith' vs 'john_smith'), which is plausible but narrow. High is defensible on the silent-tenant-isolation-breach framing if the reviewer weights the ADR promise heavily. Proposed fix (validate usernames in parse_users, collision check in register_users) is correct and cheap.

Session cookie lacks Secure/SameSite hardening and never expires

auth.py:106-125 · reviewer: auth-security
What it is
install_auth sets only server.secret_key and writes session[_SESSION_KEY] = username on login (auth.py:106, 125). No Flask session cookie config is set anywhere in the repo (grep for SESSION_COOKIE/PERMANENT finds nothing in product code), so the deploy runs on Flask defaults: SESSION_COOKIE_SECURE=False, SESSION_COOKIE_SAMESITE unset. The session is also non-permanent with no server-side notion of expiry: because Flask sessions are stateless signed cookies, a captured cookie value remains replayable indefinitely (logout at auth.py:137 only pops the key from the current client's cookie; the old signed value stays valid until SECRET_KEY rotates).
Why it matters
Fly's force_https=true redirects HTTP requests, but without the Secure flag the browser still attaches the session cookie to the initial plaintext http://chess-dashboard.fly.dev request before the redirect, exposing it to on-path capture. Missing SameSite leaves the gated Dash POST callbacks relying on browser default-Lax behavior rather than an explicit policy. And with no expiry, any leaked cookie (logs, shared machine, network capture) grants permanent access with no revocation mechanism short of rotating SECRET_KEY for all users.
How to fix
In install_auth, alongside setting secret_key: server.config.update(SESSION_COOKIE_SECURE=True, SESSION_COOKIE_HTTPONLY=True, SESSION_COOKIE_SAMESITE='Lax', PERMANENT_SESSION_LIFETIME=timedelta(days=N)); set session.permanent = True on successful login so the lifetime applies. Gate SESSION_COOKIE_SECURE on non-debug/production if local HTTP dev must keep working.
Expected improvement
Session cookies stop being transmittable over plaintext HTTP, carry an explicit SameSite policy, and expire after a bounded window instead of being valid forever once captured.
Evidence
server.secret_key = secret_key  …  session[_SESSION_KEY] = username  (no server.config.update of any SESSION_COOKIE_* setting anywhere in the repo)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read auth.py in full plus repo-wide grep and fly.toml. Confirmed: secret_key set at auth.py:106, session write at :125, logout pop at :137; no SESSION_COOKIE_*, PERMANENT_SESSION_LIFETIME, or session.permanent anywhere in product code; fly.toml:24 has force_https=true. Line cites are accurate. Corrections: (1) SESSION_COOKIE_HTTPONLY=True is Flask's default, so that part of the fix is redundant; (2) the plaintext initial-request capture vector is overstated because *.fly.dev is HSTS-preloaded, so browsers never send the plaintext request — Secure flag matters mainly for non-preload clients/custom domains; (3) the indefinite-replay/no-revocation point is correct (stateless signed cookie, logout is client-side only). Real hardening gap, but with HSTS preload and a single-coach threat model, low rather than medium.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Code facts confirmed: auth.py:106 sets only server.secret_key, auth.py:125 sets a non-permanent session, no SESSION_COOKIE_*/PERMANENT_SESSION_LIFETIME config anywhere (verified by repo grep), logout at auth.py:137 only pops client-side. Lines cited are correct. BUT the headline impact is refuted: the app deploys to chess-dashboard.fly.dev and the entire .dev TLD is HSTS-preloaded in all major browsers, so no browser ever sends a plaintext http:// request — the missing Secure flag cannot leak the cookie on-path for this domain. SameSite unset falls back to browser-default Lax, which already blocks cross-site POSTs to Dash callbacks. The fix's SESSION_COOKIE_HTTPONLY=True is redundant (Flask default). What genuinely survives is the no-expiry/no-revocation replay point (inherent to Flask stateless signed cookies) plus explicit-over-implicit hardening hygiene. Downgrade medium → low; keep the fix but gate SESSION_COOKIE_SECURE on production since local dev runs plain HTTP.
mediumConfirmed backend/auth effort: trivial

_safe_next open-redirect bypass via backslash path ('/\\evil.com')

auth.py:143-148 · reviewer: auth-security
What it is
_safe_next accepts any string that starts with '/' but not '//': `if raw.startswith("/") and not raw.startswith("//"): return raw`. The value '/\\evil.com' (slash-backslash) passes both checks and is returned verbatim into redirect() after login (auth.py:126-127). Browsers (per the WHATWG URL spec) normalize backslashes to forward slashes when resolving a Location header, so '/\evil.com' resolves as the scheme-relative URL '//evil.com' — a redirect off-site. Also unhandled: '/%2f%2fevil.com'-style tricks are safe here (no decode), but the backslash form is a real, well-known bypass.
Why it matters
The login page reads ?next= from the query string (auth.py:132) and echoes it into the post-login redirect. An attacker can send a victim a legitimate-looking https://<app>/login?next=/\evil.com link; after the victim types their real credentials on the genuine login page, they land on an attacker page — the classic phishing amplifier the _safe_next docstring says it exists to prevent.
How to fix
Reject backslashes too: `if raw.startswith("/") and not raw.startswith(("//", "/\\")): return raw` — or more robustly, `parts = urlsplit(raw.replace("\\", "/")); return raw if raw.startswith("/") and not parts.netloc and not parts.scheme else "/"`.
Expected improvement
The post-login redirect can no longer be steered to an external host; _safe_next actually enforces the local-path-only contract its docstring claims.
Evidence
def _safe_next(raw: str) -> str:\n    if raw.startswith("/") and not raw.startswith("//"):\n        return raw\n    return "/"
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read auth.py lines 100-160. Confirmed `_safe_next` at line 143 with the guard at line 146-147: `if raw.startswith("/") and not raw.startswith("//"): return raw` else `return "/"` (line 148). The value `/\evil.com` starts with `/` and does NOT start with `//`, so it is returned verbatim. Confirmed both call sites: line 126 (`target = _safe_next(request.form.get("next", ""))` → `redirect(target)` at line 127) and line 132 (query `?next=` echoed into the login page). Empirically verified: werkzeug 3.1.8 is installed; `redirect('/\\evil.com').headers['Location']` returns `'/\\evil.com'` verbatim (no normalization server-side). Per the WHATWG URL spec browsers treat backslash as forward slash when resolving a Location, so `/\evil.com` resolves to the scheme-relative `//evil.com` → off-site redirect. The finding's mechanism, evidence, and both call-site references are all accurate. Minor line-number nit: the actual guard is at 146-147 (finding cites 143-148, which spans the whole function including docstring — acceptable). The docstring explicitly says the function exists to prevent open redirect to another host, so this is a genuine gap in its stated contract, not intended behavior. Not covered by any ADR or known/excluded item. Suggested fix in the finding is sound (`not raw.startswith(("//", "/\\"))` or a urlsplit-based netloc/scheme check). Severity medium is fair: exploitation requires crafting a link and the victim landing post-auth on an off-site page (phishing amplifier), no direct data compromise.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/auth.py in full and tests/test_auth.py. Confirmed: _safe_next (auth.py:143-148) is exactly as quoted — `raw.startswith("/") and not raw.startswith("//")` — so '/\evil.com' passes and is returned verbatim into redirect() at line 127 (POST path; line 126 computes it). The GET path (line 132) only echoes it into a hidden field via escape(), which does not neutralize backslashes, so the value round-trips through the form into the POST redirect. No mitigation elsewhere: no other caller sanitizes next, tests/test_auth.py has zero coverage of the next parameter (only checks unauthenticated→/login and 302-on-success), and the stack is Dash 4 / modern Werkzeug where autocorrect_location_header defaults off, so the Location header carries the backslash to the browser, which per WHATWG URL normalizes '\' to '/' yielding scheme-relative //evil.com. This is the well-known bypass Django's url_has_allowed_host_and_scheme explicitly guards against. Docstring says the function exists to prevent open redirect, so this is a violation of the stated invariant, not intentional design; not covered by excluded issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86. Minor corrections: the finding cites 'auth.py:126-127' for the redirect (correct) and 'auth.py:132' as reading ?next= (correct, though that line feeds the form, and the actual redirect input is the POST form field at 126 — the chain still starts from the attacker-controlled query string). Proposed fixes are both sound; the urlsplit-on-backslash-normalized variant is the more robust choice. Severity medium is appropriate: post-login phishing amplifier requiring a crafted link, on a small gated dashboard — real but not credential-stealing by itself.

Auth.authenticate leaks valid usernames via a timing side channel

auth.py:70-75 · reviewer: auth-security
What it is
authenticate does `record = self.users.get(username); if record is not None and record.verify(password)`. For an unknown username the expensive scrypt check_password_hash (user_config.py:64-66, werkzeug default scrypt:32768:8:1) is skipped entirely, so the request returns in microseconds; for a known username with a wrong password it takes the full ~tens-of-milliseconds scrypt cost. The per-hash comparison itself is timing-safe (werkzeug uses hmac.compare_digest), but the presence/absence of the hash computation is easily measurable over the network.
Why it matters
An attacker probing the public /login endpoint can enumerate which usernames exist in USCF_DASHBOARD_USERS by response-time alone, then concentrate password guessing on real accounts. On a small allow-listed deployment the impact is modest, which is why this is low rather than medium — but it converts a two-unknowns brute force into a one-unknown one.
How to fix
On a username miss, verify the password against a fixed dummy hash so both paths pay the scrypt cost: precompute _DUMMY_HASH = generate_password_hash('!') at module import, and in authenticate do `check_password_hash(_DUMMY_HASH, password); return None` when record is None.
Expected improvement
Login timing becomes indistinguishable between unknown-username and wrong-password, removing the username-enumeration oracle from the only unauthenticated POST endpoint.
Evidence
record = self.users.get(username)\nif record is not None and record.verify(password):\n    return record\nreturn None
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/auth.py (full file) and user_config.py lines 40-79. Auth.authenticate at lines 70-75 matches the cited evidence verbatim: `record = self.users.get(username); if record is not None and record.verify(password): return record; return None`. UserRecord.verify (user_config.py:64-66) calls werkzeug check_password_hash, whose default is scrypt — so an unknown username returns without any hash computation while a known username with a wrong password pays the full scrypt cost, a measurable timing oracle for username enumeration on the public /login POST (auth.py:124). No dummy-hash mitigation and no rate limiting exists anywhere in the file. Not covered by exclusions (issues #40/#80, PRs #82-#86 don't touch auth). Corrections: none — file, lines, description, and fix are all accurate. Low severity is appropriate given the small allow-listed deployment; the fix (verify against a precomputed dummy hash on miss) is correct, with the minor caveat that the dummy hash should be computed once at module import (generate_password_hash is itself slow) exactly as the finding suggests.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/auth.py (Auth.authenticate, lines 70-75, and the /login POST route, lines 119-133) and /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/user_config.py (UserRecord.verify, lines 64-66; hash minted via werkzeug generate_password_hash, default scrypt). The finding is accurate: `record = self.users.get(username); if record is not None and record.verify(password)` short-circuits, so an unknown username returns without ever running scrypt, while a known username pays the full check_password_hash cost — a measurable timing oracle on the public /login POST path. I looked for mitigations: there is no rate limiting, lockout, or delay anywhere in auth.py, and the /login route is deliberately in _PUBLIC_PREFIXES, so the endpoint is reachable unauthenticated by design. The 401 body is identical for both failure modes ("Wrong username or password."), so timing is the only leak — the finding correctly does not claim a content-based leak. Line numbers, the werkzeug scrypt reference (user_config.py:64-66), and the evidence snippet all match the current code exactly. The proposed fix (dummy-hash verify on username miss) is the standard remedy and is correct and harmless; one nit: generate_password_hash at import time adds ~tens of ms to module import, which is negligible here. Severity: low is right, not inflated — this is a small allow-listed deployment (USCF_DASHBOARD_USERS, no self-signup) whose usernames are low-entropy anyway (the docstring example is "daniel"), so enumeration gains the attacker little; but the code path defect is real and unmitigated. Not covered by excluded issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86 (none touch auth).
lowConfirmed backend/auth effort: small

Login endpoint has no throttling and /logout is a CSRF-able GET

auth.py:119-138 · reviewer: auth-security
What it is
The /login POST handler (auth.py:119-129) accepts unlimited attempts with no per-IP or per-username throttle, lockout, or delay — the only brake is the scrypt hash cost itself, and nothing else in the repo (gunicorn.conf.py, fly.toml) adds rate limiting. Separately, /logout (auth.py:135-138) is a plain GET with no CSRF protection, so any third-party page can terminate a user's session with `<img src="https://<app>/logout">`; the login form itself also carries no CSRF token, permitting login-CSRF (silently logging a victim into an attacker-controlled account from the same allow-list — low relevance here given the tiny closed user set, but free to fix).
Why it matters
This is an internet-facing login on Fly.io protecting private coach material. Unthrottled POSTs let an attacker grind passwords at whatever rate the single worker sustains (~20-50 scrypt verifications/sec on shared-cpu-1x), which against a weak password is workable. The GET /logout is a minor forced-logout annoyance rather than a breach, but it costs one line to make state-changing routes POST-only.
How to fix
Add a small in-memory failure counter with exponential backoff keyed by (remote IP, username) in the login handler — no dependency needed and consistent with the no-database design (state resets on restart, which is acceptable for a throttle). Make /logout methods=['POST'] and render the logout control as a form in the shell.
Expected improvement
Online brute-force against the two-or-three real accounts becomes impractical, and cross-site forced logout goes away.
Evidence
@server.route(login_path, methods=["GET", "POST"])  …  @server.route("/logout")\ndef logout():\n    session.pop(_SESSION_KEY, None)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/auth.py in full plus user_config.py, gunicorn.conf.py, fly.toml, requirements.txt, shell.py. All three claims hold in current code: (1) the /login POST handler at auth.py:119-129 calls gate.authenticate() with no per-IP/per-username counter, delay, or lockout, and no rate-limiting dependency exists anywhere in the repo (no flask-limiter in requirements, nothing in gunicorn.conf.py or fly.toml); (2) /logout at auth.py:135-138 is registered with the default GET-only method and unconditionally pops the session — CSRF-able via a cross-site GET as described; (3) the login form (_login_page, auth.py:184-195) carries only a hidden `next` field, no CSRF token. user_config.py:20 confirms scrypt password hashes, so the hash cost really is the only brake. Line citations are exact. One correction to the proposed fix: shell.py contains no logout link at all (grep for "logout" finds nothing outside auth.py), so "render the logout control as a form in the shell" would be adding a control, not converting an existing one — making the route POST-only currently breaks the only way to log out (typing the URL). Severity low is appropriate given the tiny closed allow-list and scrypt cost; not covered by issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86 exclusions.

Dockerfile runs the app as root with no USER directive

Dockerfile:1-7 · reviewer: deploy-config
What it is
The 7-line Dockerfile never creates or switches to a non-root user, so gunicorn and all request-handling code run as root inside the container, both on Fly and in docker-compose. The app parses untrusted external inputs (Lichess API responses, scraped USCF HTML) and writes cache files, all as uid 0.
Why it matters
Container root turns any code-execution bug in the app or its dependency tree into root inside the container (and full write access to the mounted /data volume). It is also one of the first things a reviewer of a showcase repo looks for in a Dockerfile. The app binds port 8050, so nothing requires privileged ports.
How to fix
Add a non-root user after installing dependencies, e.g. `RUN useradd --create-home appuser` then `USER appuser` before CMD. Ensure /data on Fly is chown-able or writable by that uid (Fly volumes default to root-owned; chown in an entrypoint or use `--uid` consistent ownership).
Expected improvement
Reduced blast radius of any RCE in the request path; standard container-hardening box checked.
Evidence
Entire Dockerfile:
```
FROM python:3.11-slim
WORKDIR /app
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt
COPY . .
EXPOSE 8050
CMD ["gunicorn", "app:server", "--config", "gunicorn.conf.py"]
```
— no USER line.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/Dockerfile (7 lines) — matches the quoted evidence exactly; no USER directive, no useradd, so gunicorn runs as uid 0. No alternative Dockerfile exists. fly.toml confirms a volume mounted at /data (source chess_dashboard_data) with CACHE_PATH/USCF_CACHE_PATH/ANALYSIS_CACHE_PATH/DATA_DIR all under /data, so the root-writable-volume detail and the how_to_fix caveat about Fly volume ownership are accurate. docker-compose.yml also uses this Dockerfile. Not covered by exclusions: issues #80/#40 and PRs #82-#86 do not touch the Dockerfile. Severity low is appropriate for a single-user showcase app in a container sandbox.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/Dockerfile (7 lines, exactly as quoted — no USER, no useradd/entrypoint), fly.toml, docker-compose.yml, and grepped docs/AGENTS.md/CONTEXT.md/ADRs for any documented decision to run as root (none found; ADRs 0005/0006 cover single-worker/per-user store, not container user). Finding is accurate: gunicorn runs as uid 0 in both Fly and compose deployments, and fly.toml mounts a volume at /data with all three cache paths (CACHE_PATH, USCF_CACHE_PATH, ANALYSIS_CACHE_PATH) pointed at it, so the /data write-access claim checks out. No mitigation exists (no compose `user:` key, no gunicorn user/group setting in the repo). The proposed fix is correct including the caveat that Fly volumes are root-owned by default, so the chown/entrypoint note is load-bearing — a bare USER switch would break cache writes to /data on Fly. Severity low is appropriate: single/known-user app behind optional auth, standard container-hardening gap rather than an exposed vulnerability, but it is a fair catch for a resume-showcase Dockerfile and is not covered by issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86.

Activity calendar encodes winning vs losing days in red-vs-green hue alone (trends.py)

pages/trends.py:150-213 · reviewer: pages-contracts
What it is
The Trends activity calendar colors each day cell on a single diverging scale from COLORS["loss"] (systemRed #ff453a) through DRAW_FILL to COLORS["win"] (systemGreen #30d158), with intensity driven by |Net| clamped to ±3. Because intensity is symmetric, a +2 day and a −2 day are the exact same brightness and saturation and differ only in red-vs-green hue. There is no glyph, letter, or positional cue in the cell; the only disambiguation is the per-cell hover popup. Daniel is red-green colorblind, so the calendar's core meaning (did I win or lose that day) is invisible to him at a glance — the explicit global rule says never encode meaning in red-vs-green alone.
Why it matters
This is the lead visualization on the Trends page and its entire information content (winning day vs losing day) collapses to 'some days had games' for the primary user. The repo is also a resume showcase, where an accessibility miss in the flagship chart is a bad look. No document in the repo records a colorblind mitigation (grep for colorblind/color-blind returns nothing).
How to fix
Pair hue with a second channel: e.g. render a small glyph or letter overlay (W/L), or make the losing side of the scale differ in lightness/shape (e.g. hollow vs filled cells via a pattern/annotation layer), or switch the diverging scale to a colorblind-safe pair (blue/orange) since WDL_COLOR_MAP's red/green is the token pair. At minimum make intensity asymmetric so net-negative and net-positive days differ in luminance, which survives red-green confusion.
Expected improvement
The calendar becomes readable at a glance for the app's actual user (and any red-green colorblind viewer), honoring the stated global accessibility rule.
Evidence
_CAL_COLORSCALE = [
    [0.0,  COLORS["loss"]],     # net −3 or worse: full loss-red
    ...
    [1.0,  COLORS["win"]],      # net +3 or better: full win-green
]  ... game_z[weekday][week] = max(-_NET_CLAMP, min(_NET_CLAMP, int(row["Net"])))
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed in pages/trends.py. _CAL_COLORSCALE (lines 151-157) is a symmetric diverging scale COLORS["loss"] #ff453a -> LOSS_FILL -> DRAW_FILL -> WIN_FILL -> COLORS["win"] #30d158; both FILL stops are rgba(...,0.55) of the full tokens (styles.py:108-110), so a +N and -N day have identical opacity/luminance treatment and differ in hue alone. z is int(row["Net"]) clamped to +/-3 (line 181, _NET_CLAMP=150), rendered as a go.Heatmap (lines 208-213) with no text/annotation/glyph layer — the only disambiguation is the hover string (line 185-187). No colorblind mitigation exists anywhere in the repo (grep for colorblind/color-blind: zero hits in code or docs). This directly violates the explicit global rule (Daniel is red-green colorblind; never encode meaning in red-vs-green alone), and unlike the WDL bar charts there is no positional/label backup channel here. Not a duplicate: issue #40 covers visual-design taste, and the design docs list red-green-alone encoding as a finding, not an intentional design. Minor corrections: the cited line range 150-213 is accurate; the evidence snippet matches verbatim except for elided middle stops. The per-year header ("NW ML" totals, line 251) gives yearly aggregates but not per-day information, so it does not mitigate. Suggested fix in the finding is sound; the simplest token-consistent option is an asymmetric-luminance scale or a W/L annotation layer.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/pages/trends.py lines 100-240 and the token definitions in styles.py (COLORS["win"]=#30d158, COLORS["loss"]=#ff453a, WIN_FILL/LOSS_FILL/DRAW_FILL at 0.55 alpha). Confirmed: _CAL_COLORSCALE (lines 150-157) is a symmetric red-through-gray-to-green diverging scale, game_z is the clamped signed Net (line 181), and the heatmap trace (208-213) carries no glyph, letter, annotation, or positional cue — the only disambiguation is the hover text. Grep for colorblind/color-blind across the repo returns nothing; no documented mitigation. The verifier instructions themselves state that red-vs-green-alone encoding without shape/label/position IS a finding, so this is not covered by the intentional-design list, and it is an accessibility defect rather than a visual-taste issue, so it is not subsumed by issue #40 (design overhaul) or #80 (polish backlog). Line range 150-213 is accurate. One correction: the claim that a +2 and a -2 day are "the exact same brightness" is overstated — #30d158 has roughly 0.47 relative luminance vs 0.26 for #ff453a, so some incidental luminance difference survives deuteranopia — but that difference is accidental, muddied by the 0.55-alpha mid-stops, and is not a designed second channel, so the core finding stands. Proposed fixes (glyph overlay, asymmetric luminance, or a blue/orange diverging pair) are all reasonable; note the red/green tokens are reused app-wide, so a scale swap local to the calendar is the least invasive. Severity high is fair: lead visualization on Trends, meaning invisible at a glance to the primary (colorblind) user, and the repo is a resume showcase.

Sync swap is not atomic: store.df rebound four times after _swap, and enrichment failure leaves the store half-updated

data.py:452-455, 279-333, 462-464 · reviewer: sync-store
What it is
ADR 0006 and the Store docstring promise readers "either the previous complete dataset or the new one, never a mix", but refresh() and _sync_store() rebind store.df four separate times after the initial swap: _swap(store, result) installs the raw Lichess df, then _sync_uscf_into_store rebinds it twice (store.df = enrich_games(...), store.df = attach_round_numbers(...)), then _run_analysis_into_store rebinds it again with Analysis/Analyzed/Summary columns. Two consequences. (a) Transient: in any threaded server (the Dash dev server via dash_app.run, or gunicorn with threads), a callback that reads data.get_df() mid-Sync gets a df with NO enrichment columns — directly violating ADR 0003/0004's "enrichment columns ALWAYS exist; pages never check column presence". The code itself admits this: get_reconciliation carries a workaround comment ("Mid-Sync, the store briefly holds the freshly-swapped Lichess df before USCF enrichment rebinds it"), and pages/games.py:121 defensively checks `if "UscfMatched" in df_f.columns` — itself a violation of the pages/AGENTS.md rule that pages never check column presence, existing only to paper over this window. (b) Permanent and thread-count-independent: refresh()'s blanket `except Exception` runs AFTER _swap has already replaced the data, so any exception inside _sync_uscf_into_store / _run_analysis_into_store / _run_coach_into_store (e.g. a malformed uscf_cache.json making UscfCache.get_current raise, see separate finding) returns status="error" while the store now permanently holds the new games WITHOUT USCF/Analysis/Summary columns — contradicting the docstring "Never raises and never disturbs current data on failure."
Why it matters
This is the project's central concurrency invariant (ADR 0006) and it is not actually implemented. The transient window makes pages crash or silently render un-enriched data during every Sync in dev, and has already forced two documented workarounds downstream. The error path corrupts the served dataset in production (single-threaded gunicorn included): after one enrichment exception the user sees new games with all USCF matching, round numbers, analysis, and summaries gone until the next fully-successful Sync.
How to fix
Build the complete next snapshot off to the side and swap exactly once: have _sync_uscf_into_store / _run_analysis_into_store / _run_coach_into_store operate on and return a candidate (df, uscf, match_result, coach, ...) bundle without touching the Store, then assign all Store fields in one final _swap at the end of the try block. Then delete the get_reconciliation mid-Sync workaround and the games.py column-presence checks, which become dead.
Expected improvement
The atomic-swap contract becomes true: readers never observe enrichment-less data, a failed Sync genuinely leaves current data untouched, and two ADR-violating downstream workarounds can be removed.
Evidence
data.py refresh(): "_swap(store, result)\n        _sync_uscf_into_store(store)  # USCF failing never fails the Sync" ... "except Exception as exc:  # a failed Sync must never break the running app"; _sync_uscf_into_store: "store.df = enrich_games(store.df, store.match_result)\n    ...\n    store.df = attach_round_numbers("; get_reconciliation: "# Mid-Sync, the store briefly holds the freshly-swapped Lichess df before\n    # USCF enrichment rebinds it."; pages/games.py:121: "if \"UscfMatched\" in df_f.columns:"
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed by direct read of data.py and pages/games.py. refresh() swaps at line 452 then rebinds store.df three more times via _sync_uscf_into_store (lines 294, 296), _run_analysis_into_store (318), plus _run_coach_into_store mutating store.coach; the blanket `except Exception` at 462 runs after _swap and does not restore prior data, contradicting the docstring "Never raises and never disturbs current data on failure" (418-419) and the module docstring's "never a mix" promise (23-25). The get_reconciliation workaround comment is at data.py:678-681 and the pages/games.py:121 column-presence check exists as cited; additional un-cited guards in data.py accessors (lines 580, 599, 615, 655) further corroborate the papered-over window. Scope corrections: production gunicorn is 1 sync worker with no threads (gunicorn.conf.py:17-18), so the transient window (a) is dev-server-only in practice; the permanent corruption path (b) requires an enrichment exception, which the enrichment layers are designed to avoid — but the invariant is structurally unenforced either way. Severity high is defensible: it is the project's central ADR 0006 invariant, the error path corrupts served data in production, and the fix (build candidate snapshot off-store, single swap) also deletes two documented workarounds. Not a duplicate of excluded items.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read data.py (module docstring lines 23-26, Store docstring 92-93, _sync_store 253-276, _sync_uscf_into_store 279-304, _run_analysis_into_store 307-318, refresh 414-466, _swap 469-476, get_reconciliation 670-686), gunicorn.conf.py, ADR 0006, sync.py exception structure, pages/games.py:121-126, pages/game_detail.py, shell.py:230. The code facts are all confirmed: refresh() calls _swap then three helpers that each rebind store.df; the docstrings promise "never a mix" and "never disturbs current data on failure"; get_reconciliation carries the mid-Sync workaround comment; games.py:121 checks `if "UscfMatched" in df_f.columns`, contradicting the pages rule and _sync_uscf_into_store's own docstring ("pages never check for their presence"). The blanket `except Exception` at data.py:462 runs after _swap, so an unanticipated exception in any enrichment step returns status="error" and logs "keeping current data" while the store now holds the new df WITHOUT enrichment columns — the docstring claim is genuinely false on that path. The proposed fix (build the candidate bundle aside, swap once) is correct and would make both workarounds deletable. Severity is inflated, though — two material corrections: (a) The transient window does NOT exist in production. gunicorn.conf.py pins workers=1 AND worker_class="sync" (one thread); the Sync callback holds the only request thread, so no reader can observe mid-Sync state. The window is dev-server-only (Flask threaded default), and the two spots known to be exposed are already guarded. It's an invariant-integrity/dead-workaround problem, not a user-facing prod bug. (b) The permanent-corruption path requires an *unanticipated* exception: all documented failure modes are caught downstream (sync_uscf "never raises" catching UscfError, UscfCache catches OSError/JSONDecodeError — so the finding's cited trigger "malformed uscf_cache.json making UscfCache.get_current raise" is wrong, that path degrades; ai_summary degrades to ""; sync_coach never raises). It fires only on a genuine bug in the pure match/enrich code, i.e. low probability, high consequence. Also: _sync_store's cache-fallback path (data.py:265-268) has the same multi-rebind pattern, and shell.py:230's comment is a third documented acknowledgment of the rebinding. Real finding, correct fix, but medium: a design-integrity violation of ADR 0006's stated invariant with defensive contortions downstream, not a live high-severity production bug.

Game-length histogram overlays translucent green and red distributions with no positional channel

pages/trends.py:458-463 · reviewer: colorblind-a11y
What it is
update_length_hist builds `px.histogram(..., color="Outcome", barmode="overlay", color_discrete_map=WDL_COLOR_MAP, opacity=0.75)`. Unlike the app's stacked W/D/L bars (where the fixed Win→Draw→Loss segment order gives a positional channel), overlay mode superimposes the win-green and loss-red bars at the same x positions. The legend labels the colors, but a red-green colorblind viewer cannot map a given translucent bar back to its legend entry, and 0.75-opacity overlap blends the two hues further. The hover ('<b>N</b> games · X moves') omits the outcome word entirely, so even hovering does not disambiguate.

sync_studies overwrites the offline PGN cache before callers reject an empty result, destroying the fallback

sync.py:140-155 · reviewer: sync-store
What it is
sync_studies() writes the PGN cache (`if cache_path: _write_cache(cache_path, merged_pgn)`) unconditionally on any fetch success, but its two callers treat an empty DataFrame as a failed Sync only AFTER the cache has been clobbered: data.refresh() returns status="error" on `result.df.empty` (data.py:443-447) and _sync_store raises RuntimeError (data.py:271-272). If the designated Studies fetch successfully but currently contain no parseable games (chapters deleted/emptied on Lichess, or a transient parse regression), the previous good games.pgn — the only offline-boot fallback — is replaced with a gameless PGN. A later boot with Lichess unreachable then dies: _boot_from_cache loads the cache, hits `if df.empty: raise sync_error` (data.py:406), and the app exits, even though a perfectly good cache existed before that Sync.
Why it matters
The cache is documented as disposable, but it is also the entire offline-resilience story ("boot from PGN cache" per the data.py header and ADR 0006 notes). One bad-but-reachable Sync silently converts "Lichess down → serve cached games" into "Lichess down → app fails to boot", and refresh() even reports the Sync as an error while having already destroyed the fallback.
How to fix
In sync_studies, only write the cache when the parsed result is non-empty: move the `_write_cache` call below `load_games_from_text`/`_dedupe_and_sort` and gate it on `not df.empty` (or let the caller trigger the cache write after accepting the result).
Expected improvement
An empty-Study Sync can no longer wipe the offline fallback; degraded boots keep working after any rejected Sync.
Evidence
sync.py: "    if cache_path:\n        _write_cache(cache_path, merged_pgn)\n\n    return SyncResult(df=df, player=player, failures=failures)" — while data.py refresh(): "if result.df.empty:\n            return RefreshOutcome(\n                status=\"error\"," and _boot_from_cache: "if df.empty:\n        raise sync_error"
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/sync.py (sync_studies, ~lines 106-154) and /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/data.py (_sync_store ~253-276, _boot_from_cache ~389-411, refresh ~414-460). uscf_core._pair_group greedy pairing can attach the wrong USCF record when a full-agreement assignment exists

uscf_core.py:1103-1118 · reviewer: uscf-matching
What it is
In the ID pass, _pair_group resolves repeat-opponent groups (same opponent member ID + same result) by sorting all game-record pairs by tiebreak score and greedily assigning. Greedy assignment is not an optimal bipartite matching: when the top pairs tie, the arbitrary pick (lowest game_order/record_order) can consume a record that another Game needed, forcing the remaining Game onto a score-0 record. Concretely, with Games G0,G1 and records R0,R1 scoring G0-R0=3, G0-R1=3, G1-R0=3, G1-R1=0, the sorted order picks G0-R0 first, then G1 can only take R1 (score 0: color disagrees AND outside the event window), even though the alternative assignment G0-R1 / G1-R0 agrees on every tiebreak fact for both pairs. The wrong record silently attaches a wrong UscfEventId/UscfSection and can raise a phantom UscfColorConflict reconciliation entry for a game whose true record matched its color.
Why it matters
ADR 0007's stated bias is 'prefer a missed match to an invented one' because a single wrong pairing corrupts the rating lens, upset stats, real round numbers, and Rated Event scores. Monthly ladders — which the code's own comments say routinely have event windows that fail to contain the true play date — are exactly where repeat opponents with identical results and collapsed window scores occur, making the asymmetric-tie trigger plausible in normal use. The existing test (test_date_window_disambiguates_when_color_cannot) only covers the symmetric 2x2 case where greedy happens to work.
How to fix
For the small groups involved (repeat opponents in one key, typically 2-3 each side), compute the max-total-score assignment (brute-force permutations is fine at this size) instead of greedy-by-best-pair; or, more in the spirit of ADR 0007, refuse to assign any pair whose choice was an unresolved tie against a materially different record (different event_id) and leave those Games unmatched to surface in Reconciliation.
Expected improvement
Repeat-opponent groups always get the assignment that maximizes tiebreak agreement, eliminating a class of silent wrong-event attachments and false color-conflict entries.
Evidence
scored = sorted(
    (-_tiebreak_score(game, records[i]), game_order, record_order, i)
    ...
for _neg_score, game_order, _record_order, i in scored:
    if game_order in taken_games or i in used:
        continue
    matches.append(GameMatch(games[game_order]["ChapterURL"], records[i], matched_by))
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed at uscf_core.py:1103-1118 (code matches the quoted evidence exactly). _pair_group is greedy-by-best-pair with arbitrary (game_order, record_order) tie-breaks, not an optimal assignment, and hand-tracing shows real misassignment cases. One correction: the finding's concrete score matrix (3,3,3,0) is infeasible — G0 scoring 3 vs both records forces both records to G0's color, and G1R0=3 then forces G1 to the same color, contradicting the color mismatch required for G1R1=0. However, feasible matrices reproduce the same defect: (3,3,3,2) — greedy attaches a window-disagreeing record (wrong UscfEventId) to G1 when a full-agreement assignment exists, matching the title claim; and (3,1,3,0) — greedy forces G1 onto a score-0 record (color and window both disagree), producing the phantom UscfColorConflict described. Test test_uscf_core.py:577 (test_date_window_disambiguates_when_color_cannot) indeed only covers a case where each game scores 3 against exactly one record, so greedy happens to be optimal there. Violates ADR 0007's stated bias and the function's own docstring ("pairs that agree on color and the Rated Event date window win"). Suggested fix in the finding (brute-force optimal assignment for these tiny groups, or leave materially-ambiguous ties unmatched) is sound. Not covered by issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/uscf_core.py lines 950-1150 (_id_pass, _pair_group at 1103-1118, _tiebreak_score, _within_event_window) and tests/test_uscf_core.py TestRepeatOpponentDisambiguation (lines 544-623). Core claim CONFIRMED and reproduced by executing match_games: two same-color wins vs the same opponent, R0 window Dec 1-31, R1 window Dec 1-14, games on Dec 10 and Dec 20 -> greedy attaches the Dec-20 game to the Dec-1-14 event (score 2) although the swap assignment scores 3 on both pairs. Wrong UscfEventId/EventName/Section silently attach, violating ADR 0007's 'prefer a missed match to an invented one'. Two corrections: (1) the finding's concrete 3/3/3/0 matrix is infeasible — a score-3 tie forces both records to share G0's color, and G1-R0=3 forces G1 to share it too, so G1-R1 >= 2; realizable failure matrices are 3/3/3/2 or 1/1/1/0, i.e. the displacement is always window-driven, never color-driven. (2) Consequently the 'phantom UscfColorConflict' claim is wrong: in every realizable tie-displacement the displaced game lands on a record with the same player_color as the one it lost, so the conflict flag is identical under either assignment; the material harm is wrong event attachment (event ID/name/section, rating deltas, real round numbers, Rated Event scores). Line range 1103-1118 is correct. Existing tests (test_date_window_disambiguates_when_color_cannot at line 577) only cover the symmetric 3/2/2/3 case where greedy happens to work, as the finding says. Proposed fixes are sound: groups are tiny (repeat opponents sharing opponent-ID+result), so brute-force optimal assignment is trivial; the leave-ambiguous-ties-unmatched variant is more in the ADR 0007 spirit. Severity medium is fair: trigger needs repeat opponent + same result + same color + overlapping/asymmetric windows — exactly the monthly-ladder shape the code comments call routine — but it is a niche corner, not a common path.

performance_rating_stats counts forfeit wins, inflating the performance rating

pgn_stats_core.py:1180-1189 · reviewer: pgn-stats
What it is
performance_rating_stats() filters only on OpponentRatingNum.notna() and Outcome in Win/Draw/Loss; it never calls _without_forfeits(). A forfeit win against a rated opponent (Forfeit=True rows produced by uscf_core enrichment, which map WinForfeit -> Outcome 'Win') therefore counts as a full point against that opponent's rating in the FIDE performance-rating formula. This contradicts the module's own rule stated in _without_forfeits ('a forfeit win is not chess', issue #29) and the sibling functions win_draw_loss_counts, streaks, win_rate_over_time, opening_summary, repertoire_tree, and upset_tracker, which all exclude forfeits. The inflated number flows into kpi_stats()['performance_rating'] (overview KPI card) and pages/events.py line 345 (per-event performance rating).
Why it matters
A no-show win adds a free 1.0 score point at the opponent's full rating, pushing the displayed performance rating up by a spurious amount — exactly the distortion issue #29 was created to prevent, on one of the most prominent numbers in the dashboard.
How to fix
Add `df = _without_forfeits(df)` at the top of performance_rating_stats(), before the rated-games filter, matching the pattern used in win_rate_over_time and streaks.
Expected improvement
Performance rating on the Overview KPI card and Events page reflects only games actually played, consistent with the win-rate and streak numbers next to it.
Evidence
rated = df[
        df["OpponentRatingNum"].notna() & df["Outcome"].isin(["Win", "Draw", "Loss"])
    ].copy()

compute_milestones and _best_win/milestone_deltas count forfeit wins as win streaks and giant kills

pgn_stats_core.py:1783-1809 · reviewer: pgn-stats
What it is
compute_milestones() works on `d = df.copy()` with no _without_forfeits() call, so its 'Beat highest-rated opponent' milestone (line 1783: `beaten = d[(d["Outcome"] == "Win") & d["OpponentRatingNum"].notna()]`) and its 'longest win streak' scan (lines 1795-1809) both count forfeit wins. Likewise _best_win() (lines 1823-1831), which feeds the 'giant_kill' celebration delta in milestone_deltas(). This directly contradicts upset_tracker(), whose docstring states 'Forfeits are never upsets (issue #35): a no-show win is not a giant kill', and streaks(), which excludes forfeits from win streaks — so kpi_stats' longest_win_streak (via streaks) and the milestone timeline's longest-win-streak entry can disagree on the same data, and a post-Sync banner can celebrate beating a highest-rated opponent who never showed up.
Why it matters
The milestones timeline and the sync celebration banners can show records (streaks, giant kills) that the rest of the app deliberately refuses to count, producing visibly contradictory numbers between the Overview KPIs and the Milestones page.
How to fix
In compute_milestones(), apply _without_forfeits() before the win-streak scan and the highest-rated-opponent-beaten selection (the 'first game' / 'every 10th game' entries can keep the full frame if game numbering should include forfeits). In _best_win(), filter with _without_forfeits(df) before selecting beaten opponents.
Expected improvement
Milestone timeline and milestone_deltas celebrations agree with streaks() and upset_tracker() on what counts as a win streak or a giant kill.
Evidence

game_length_data includes 0-move forfeit games, skewing the length histogram and per-outcome averages

pgn_stats_core.py:1025-1031 · reviewer: pgn-stats
What it is
game_length_data() filters only on Outcome in Win/Draw/Loss and FullMoves.notna(). Forfeit games are, per uscf_core's detection rule (an unmatched Game with at most one move), rows with FullMoves 0 or 1 and Outcome 'Win' or 'Loss' — they pass both filters. FullMoves is always an int from the parser (`(plies + 1) // 2`), so notna() never removes them. Each forfeit contributes a 0- or 1-move bar to the histogram and drags the Win (or Loss) average move count toward zero.
Why it matters
A single forfeit win among, say, 20 real wins averaging 40 moves shifts the displayed 'average winning game length' by ~2 moves and puts a nonsense zero-length spike in the histogram — a chart about how games unfold should not contain games that were never played.
How to fix
Call `df = _without_forfeits(df)` at the top of game_length_data(), same as the other played-games stats.
Expected improvement
Game-length histogram and per-outcome averages describe only games with actual moves.
Evidence
d = df[df["Outcome"].isin(["Win", "Draw", "Loss"]) & df["FullMoves"].notna()].copy()
Verifier notes (2)

The optional min/max-moves user filter in filter path (pgn_stats_core lines 532-534) would only mask this if the user sets a minimum, which is not the default. Suggested fix (call _without_forfeits at the top of game_length_data) matches the established pattern and is correct. Line range 1025-1031 accurate. Not covered by PRs #82-86 or the excluded issues. kpi_stats favorite_eco_family is the family of the single most-common ECO code, not the most-common family

pgn_stats_core.py:694-695 · reviewer: pgn-stats
What it is
kpi_stats() computes the favourite ECO family as `str(eco_vals.value_counts().index[0])[0].upper()` — it value-counts full ECO codes (e.g. 'B22', 'C50') and then takes the first letter of whichever single code is most frequent. When a family's games are spread across several codes, this picks the wrong family: with B20 x3, B22 x3, C50 x4, family B has 6 games but the KPI reports 'C' because C50 is the most common individual code. opening_summary() does this correctly by mapping each code to its family first and then aggregating.
Why it matters
The 'favorite ECO family' KPI on the Overview page (pages/overview.py) can silently name the wrong family whenever the true favourite family's games are split across multiple ECO codes — a common situation for anyone with a real repertoire.
How to fix
Derive the family per game before counting: `fam_vals = eco_vals.str[0].str.upper()` then `fav_eco = str(fam_vals.value_counts().index[0]) if not fam_vals.empty else "—"`.
Expected improvement
The KPI reports the family Daniel actually plays most, matching what the Openings page's family table shows as its top row.
Evidence
eco_vals = played["ECO"].replace("", pd.NA).dropna()
    fav_eco = str(eco_vals.value_counts().index[0])[0].upper() if not eco_vals.empty else "—"

Missing [%eval] moves are carried forward as zero-drop, so a partially evaluated Game reads as fully analyzed with inflated accuracy

engine_analysis_core.py:314-318, 350, 204-206 · reviewer: engine-analysis
What it is
In _parse_move_evals, a mainline move without an [%eval] gets `cp_after = prev_cp` (carry the prior eval forward, drop = 0), and the whole Game is flagged analyzed if ANY single move carries an eval (`any_eval = True` on the first hit; `return moves if any_eval else []`). Every eval-less move therefore scores _move_accuracy(0) ≈ 100 in player_accuracy's arithmetic mean, and any mistake made on an eval-less move is invisible to classify_severity (drop is exactly 0). A Study chapter where the user pasted a single manual eval comment, or where Lichess's server analysis was truncated partway through, produces a GameAnalysis with analyzed=True, near-perfect accuracy, and an empty error profile — which then flows into accuracy_trend and mistake_type_trend in analysis_trends.py as a full-weight data point (those functions gate only on `analysis.analyzed`, so this is effectively an awaiting-analysis Game leaking into the trend aggregates).
Why it matters
The accuracy trend and mistake-type trend are the headline charts of the Analysis page; one barely-evaluated Game charts as a ~100%-accuracy, zero-mistake outlier and skews the improvement signal. Mistakes made on eval-less plies are silently dropped from the error profile, phase_type_matrix, and emitted tags.
How to fix
Track eval coverage in _parse_move_evals (e.g. count evaluated nodes). Either require coverage above a threshold (say >80% of plies) to set analyzed=True, or mark carried-forward MoveEvals (e.g. `has_eval: bool`) and have player_accuracy skip them and classify_severity/critical-moment treat them as unknown rather than perfect.
Expected improvement
Partially analyzed or manually eval-annotated Games no longer pollute accuracy/mistake trends with phantom perfect scores; trend charts reflect only genuinely evaluated moves.
Evidence
cp_after = _node_cp(node)
        if cp_after is None:
            cp_after = prev_cp  # carry the prior eval forward → no swing
        else:
            any_eval = True
...
    return moves if any_eval else []

Every cited mechanism is present as described: (1) _parse_move_evals lines 314-318 set cp_after = prev_cp when _node_cp returns None (carry-forward, win_pct_drop computes to 0 for that ply) and flip any_eval on the first move that has an eval; (2) line 350 returns the full move list if any_eval — so a single [%eval] anywhere makes every ply a MoveEval; (3) analyze_game (lines 711-718) sets analyzed=True whenever _parse_move_evals is non-empty, with no coverage check; (4) player_accuracy (lines 209-223) is an unweighted arithmetic mean over all of the player's MoveEvals, and _move_accuracy(0) = 99.9999 (103.1668*e^0 - 3.1669 clamped to 100), so eval-less plies read as near-perfect moves; (5) classify_severity uses win_pct_drop, so mistakes on eval-less plies are invisible to the error profile, and _build_error_profile/emitted_tags/critical_moment all derive from the same zero drops; (6) analysis_trends.py _analysis() gates only on analysis.analyzed (line 44), so accuracy_trend and mistake_type_trend take such a Game as a full-weight point. _refutation_line blindly takes siblings[0], so a user-annotated variation can be presented as the engine's recommended line and misclassify the mistake

engine_analysis_core.py:263-290, 328-331 · reviewer: engine-analysis
What it is
_refutation_line selects `siblings[0]` — the first variation off the parent node that isn't the played move — and treats its mainline as 'the engine's recommended line'. But the whole premise of this app is user-annotated Study chapters (Lessons and the player's own sidelines live as variations, per ADR 0002). When a move carries both a hand-written variation (added before analysis was requested, so serialized first by extract_movetext with variations=True) and the engine's judgment variation, siblings[0] is the user's line, not the engine's. The error cascades: in _parse_move_evals, when the judgment text lacks a parsable 'X was best' (e.g. the castling gap below), `best_move = refutation[0]` falls back to the user's first move, which then drives _best_move_is_forcing and therefore the tactical-vs-positional classification in _mistake_type — corrupting the error profile, phase_type_matrix, mistake_type_distribution, and the emitted Tags.
Why it matters
On exactly the Games this dashboard is built for — heavily annotated chapters — the displayed refutation line can be the player's own speculative sideline labeled as engine advice, and the tactical/positional split (the Analysis page's 'single biggest weakness' aggregate) is computed from the wrong move.
How to fix
Prefer the sibling whose first move's SAN matches _best_move_from_judgment(judgment) when a judgment names a best move; otherwise prefer a sibling whose nodes carry [%eval] directives (engine variations carry evals, hand lines usually don't); fall back to siblings[0] only when neither signal exists.
Expected improvement
Refutation lines and best-move fallbacks always reflect the engine's variation on annotated chapters, keeping the tactical/positional error profile trustworthy.
Evidence
siblings = [v for v in parent.variations if v is not node]
    if not siblings:
        return []
...
    cursor: chess.pgn.GameNode | None = siblings[0]
...
        if best_move is None and refutation:
            best_move = refutation[0]
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/engine_analysis_core.py lines 228-350 and 570-677, plus pages/game_detail.py lines 259-273. Sibling ordering is PGN serialization order, so a pre-existing user variation preceding the Lichess-appended engine one is plausible; the code has no defense either way. ONE CORRECTION: the finding's example trigger ("the castling gap") is wrong — _BEST_MOVE_RE (lines 236-237) explicitly matches O-O and O-O-O. The judgment-parse fallback actually fires for non-English/user-edited judgment comments, or for a large-eval-swing move carrying a user variation but no recognizable "X was best" text (severity is classified from win_pct_drop alone, independent of judgment text). Not covered by excluded issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86. Proposed fix direction (prefer judgment-matching sibling, then eval-carrying sibling) is sound.

Default (and un-clearable) date range permanently hides undated Games from every chart

filters.py:200-205 · reviewer: shell-filters
What it is
make_filter_drawer initializes the DatePickerRange with start_date=b["min_date"] and end_date=b["max_date"], so from first render get_filtered always passes non-None dates into apply_filters. apply_filters (pgn_stats_core.py:525-526) drops all rows with Date_dt NaT whenever either bound is set: `if date_start or date_end: out = out[out["Date_dt"].notna()]`. The pipeline explicitly supports undated Games — pgn_stats_core.py:447-449 maps the PGN placeholder "????.??.??" to NaT — yet those Games are excluded from every page in the app's default state. The DatePickerRange is not created with clearable=True, so the user cannot empty the dates to ever see them; the drawer summary would permanently read "Showing N of M games" with no active-filter badge (the badge logic at lines 324-325 counts the date filter as inactive when start == min_date).
Why it matters
This is a silent-exclusion failure mode: a Study chapter with an unknown date vanishes from all stats, the game count, the Games table, and Lessons, with no filter shown as active and no way to recover from the UI. It also contradicts the drawer's own "Showing all N games" framing.
How to fix
Either initialize the DatePickerRange with start_date=None/end_date=None (treating the full range as 'no date filter', and only excluding NaT rows when the user actively narrows the range), or change apply_filters to keep NaT rows when the selected range equals the data's full extent. Setting clearable=True on the picker is a complementary escape hatch.
Expected improvement
Games with unparseable dates (an explicitly supported case) appear in the default view and can only be excluded by a deliberate user choice, and the active-filter badge tells the truth.
Evidence
filters.py: start_date=b["min_date"], end_date=b["max_date"] — pgn_stats_core.py: if date_start or date_end: out = out[out["Date_dt"].notna()] — pgn_stats_core.py: df["Date"].replace("????.??.??", None), errors="coerce"
Verifier notes (2)

PGN placeholder to NaT. No escape hatch exists: the "All games" preset (apply_preset, filters.py:249-277) and update_filter_options (346-373) always write global min/max back, never None. Badge logic (actually lines 324-326, finding said 324-325) treats start==min_date/end==max_date as inactive, so the exclusion is silent — though the summary reads "Showing N of M games" rather than the claimed "Showing all N games" when rows are dropped, which the finding itself correctly notes. One scope nuance: if ALL games are undated, min/max_date are None and the bug doesn't trigger; it bites only in the mixed dated+undated case. Not a duplicate of excluded items (#80, #40, PRs #82-#86 untouched this logic). _prefixes_match treats 'agrees over an 8-19 ply overlap' as identity, letting short opening-lesson Chapters false-match real Games

coach_match_core.py:285-291 (and _MIN_OVERLAP at 68) · reviewer: coach-review-matching
What it is
`_prefixes_match` computes `overlap = min(len(a), len(b))` and returns True when `overlap >= _MIN_OVERLAP` (8) and the prefixes agree over that overlap. When either side is shorter than _PREFIX_PLIES (20), 'same opening for 8-19 plies' is treated as 'same Game'. Two concrete failure paths: (1) a coach opening-lesson Chapter that starts from the initial position with, say, 8-14 mainline plies (e.g. the first 4-7 moves of a Najdorf lesson) — it clears _MIN_OVERLAP, and if exactly one of the user's Games opens with that line, uniqueness holds in both directions and the teaching Chapter is CLAIMED as that Game's coach review, rendering a lesson stub in the Coach tab and its comments in the Coach's Notes feed as if they were about that Game; (2) a short user Game (8-19 recorded plies — a quick draw or miniature) is prefix-matched by ANY full-length coach Chapter sharing its opening, e.g. one of the coach's online blitz games. The module docstring says sub-_MIN_OVERLAP Chapters are 'a fragment ... not one of the user's Games', but 8-19-ply fragments pass the gate. FEN-based teaching positions are safe (their SANs won't align from ply 1), so the exposure is specifically initial-position opening material.
Why it matters
This is the one structural hole in the 'ambiguity is never a guess / zero false matches' promise: uniqueness among the user's Games does not protect against a coach *extra* that shares only an opening with a unique Game. A false match attaches the wrong prose to a Game — worse than no match, and invisible because the match looks successful.
How to fix
Require the overlap to be substantial relative to the Chapter, not just >= 8 absolute — e.g. demand `len(a) >= _PREFIX_PLIES or len(a) == full chapter length AND overlap >= some higher floor`, or simplest: require overlap >= _PREFIX_PLIES unless BOTH sides are exhausted (both games actually ended within the overlap, i.e. the chapter's mainline and the Game's movelist are each fully consumed). Comparing the Chapter's real mainline length (capture it during parsing) against the Game's Moves length makes 'both ended here' checkable.
Expected improvement
Opening-lesson material and blitz games in the coach Studies can no longer be claimed as reviews of the user's OTB Games; the 'match, never guess' guarantee becomes structural instead of empirical.
Evidence
overlap = min(len(a), len(b))
    if overlap < _MIN_OVERLAP:
        return False
    return a[:overlap] == b[:overlap]
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read coach_match_core.py in full. Evidence is verbatim and correctly located: _MIN_OVERLAP = 8 at line 68, _prefixes_match at lines 285-291 computes overlap = min(len(a), len(b)) and returns True when overlap >= 8 and prefixes agree, so any 8-19-ply agreement counts as identity when either side is shorter than _PREFIX_PLIES (20). Both claimed failure paths are real: (1) an initial-position opening-lesson Chapter whose mainline is 8-19 plies (its move_prefix from _mainline_prefix will just be shorter than 20) matches any Game opening with that line; if exactly one Game does, the bidirectional-uniqueness gate at lines 258-261 passes and the lesson is CLAIMED as that Game's review. (2) _game_prefixes (line 279) admits user Games with only 8-19 recorded plies, and their short prefix is then matched by any full-length coach Chapter sharing that opening. The docstring claim that sub-threshold chapters are "a fragment... not one of the user's Games" (lines 66-68) indeed only guards <8, not 8-19. Two mitigating factors the finding slightly understates: (a) common short openings (e.g. 8-10 plies of mainline theory) usually hit multiple user Games, and ambiguity then blocks the match — the exposure is narrower, requiring a rarer 10-19-ply line unique to one Game; (b) if the coach ALSO has a genuine review Chapter for that Game, both Chapters claim it and BOTH are dropped (false match becomes a silently lost true match — a second failure mode the finding doesn't mention, same root cause). The FEN-teaching-position safety claim is correct (game.board() honors FEN headers so SANs won't align from ply 1). Proposed fix direction is sound; capturing the chapter's true mainline length during parsing (currently truncated at 20 by _mainline_prefix) would be needed for the "both sides exhausted" check. Design docstring's "zero false matches" measurement (line 20) was empirical on one dataset, not a structural guarantee, so this does violate the documented "ambiguity is never a guess" intent rather than being intentional design. Medium severity is right: real structural hole, but probabilistically narrow in practice.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read coach_match_core.py in full plus tests/test_coach_match_core.py and tests/data/coach-study.pgn. Code matches the evidence exactly: _prefixes_match (lines 285-291) accepts any 8-19-ply agreement when either side is shorter than _PREFIX_PLIES=20, and _game_prefixes (line 279) admits user Games down to 8 plies, so both failure paths (short opening-lesson Chapter claiming a unique Game; short user Game claimed by any full Chapter sharing its opening) are real. Bidirectional uniqueness (lines 258-261) only mitigates when the Game's genuine review Chapter coexists or multiple Games share the opening — it does not protect an un-reviewed Game unique in its line. Notably, the test fixture's own extras ("Online blitz brilliancy" = 9 plies, "Immortal" = 12 plies, both from the initial position) clear _MIN_OVERLAP and stay unmatched only because no fixture Game shares their openings — no test guards this band. The FEN-based extra is safe as the finding says. Corrections: minor only — the docstring's "zero false matches" is an empirical claim on one 63-Game dataset, so probability in practice is low for this single-user showcase, but the impact (silent misattribution of coach prose, violating the module's stated "never a guess" principle, invisible in Reconciliation) justifies medium. The proposed fix is sound but requires capturing the Chapter's true mainline length at parse time, since move_prefix is already truncated to 20.
