lpv-init.js: switching to Engine while a board render is in flight leaves both the board and the Engine panel visible

assets/lpv-init.js:42-66, 96-115 · reviewer: client-js-lpv-seam
What it is
renderBoard() is asynchronous (it awaits loadLpv()), and by the file's own comment (lines 18-22) "The viewer REPLACES its mount element on every render". The Engine switch hides the board synchronously via `liveMount.style.display = "none"`. Sequence that desyncs: initCard() (or a Game/My Analysis click) queues renderBoard(); before the import resolves, the user clicks Engine — the current `.lpv` element gets display:none and the engine panel is shown; the pending `.then` then fires, re-queries `.lpv` (still the hidden div), and the viewer replaces it with a fresh root that does NOT carry the inline display:none. Result: the newly rendered board appears on top of / alongside the open Engine panel. The renderBoard callback never checks which switch is currently active before rendering and showing the board.
Why it matters
On the first load of a Game-detail page (exactly when the module import is slowest) an impatient click on Engine yields two stacked views — board plus eval chart and judgments — a visibly broken state on the app's showcase page. The same race applies to Coach/My Analysis clicks queued behind the import: the last-rendered board wins regardless of display state.
How to fix
Track the desired view per card (e.g., `var currentView` in initCard, set synchronously in the click handler) and have renderBoard's `.then` bail out — or re-apply `display:none` to the fresh mount — when `currentView === "engine"` (more generally, when the view it was asked to render is no longer the current one).
Expected improvement
The board and Engine panel become mutually exclusive under all click timings, including slow first loads.
Evidence
// The viewer REPLACES its mount element on every render, destroying the
// data-pgn-* payload ...
if (view === "engine") {
  if (liveMount) { liveMount.style.display = "none"; }
  ...
} else { ... renderBoard(card, data, view); }
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/assets/lpv-init.js in full (137 lines). The race is real in current code. renderBoard (lines 42-66) is asynchronous: it defers to loadLpv().then(...), and the click handler (lines 89-116) toggles views synchronously. On the Engine branch (lines 97-106) it sets `liveMount.style.display = "none"` on the current `.lpv` element and shows the engine panel. The file's own header comment (lines 18-22) documents that the viewer REPLACES its mount element on every render — and the code's reliance on re-querying `.lpv` at use time (mountFor, line 49) confirms the replacement keeps the `.lpv` class but drops the old element's inline styles and data attributes. So: initCard queues renderBoard(card, data, "game") at line 80; if the user clicks Engine before the dynamic import of lichess-pgn-viewer.min.js resolves, the pending .then mounts the viewer onto the hidden div, the viewer swaps in a fresh root without display:none, and the board renders visible alongside the open Engine panel. Nothing in the .then checks the currently active view before rendering. Not fixed by PRs #82-#86 (this file untouched by those changes per the code as it stands) and not covered by the known/excluded list. Minor scope correction: after the first import resolves, lpvPromise is cached module-wide, so subsequent renderBoard calls resolve on a microtask — the realistic race window is essentially only the first board render per browser session (first Game-detail page load), which the finding itself acknowledges. The same-race claim for Coach/My Analysis clicks queued behind the import is also correct (line 114 goes through the same async path). Proposed fix (per-card currentView flag checked/re-applied in the .then) is sound. Severity medium is defensible given it hits the showcase page on first load; low would also be arguable given the narrow window.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read all of assets/lpv-init.js (137 lines) and confirmed the mechanism end to end. renderBoard() (lines 42-66) is async: it awaits loadLpv() and its .then re-queries `.lpv` via mountFor(card) with no check of which switch is currently active. The Engine branch (lines 97-106) hides the board only via inline `liveMount.style.display = "none"`. The vendored viewer really does replace the mount element — the file's own comment (lines 18-22) says so, and I grepped assets/lichess-pgn-viewer.min.js and found the snabbdom `replaceChild` call — so the fresh root loses the inline display:none while keeping the `.lpv` class (proven by lines 96/111 re-querying `.lpv` successfully after renders). Result: board rendered visible while the engine panel is also shown. No mitigation exists: the MutationObserver/mounted WeakSet doesn't help, and the test suite is Python-only (no client-side JS tests). The proposed fix (per-card currentView checked in the .then) is correct and minimal. Corrections: (1) scope is narrower than described — the race window is ONLY while the one-time dynamic import is unresolved (first card init after page load). Once lpvPromise is resolved, renderBoard's .then is a microtask that runs before any subsequent click event can be dispatched, so a Coach/My Analysis click followed by an Engine click cannot race post-load; the finding's "same race applies to Coach/My Analysis clicks" holds only within that same first-load import window. (2) The broken state is self-healing — clicking any switch again restores consistency (Engine re-hides the live `.lpv`; board views re-hide the panel). Given the sub-second, one-time window on a locally-served asset and trivial recovery, medium overstates it; suggest low. Relevant lines: queued initial render at lpv-init.js:80, race sink at 48-64, Engine hide at 97-100.

extract_movetext drops FEN/SetUp headers, silently breaking every downstream reparse of a custom-position chapter

pgn_stats_core.py:194-218 · reviewer: pgn-parse-lesson-tag-extraction
What it is
extract_movetext exports a Game with `chess.pgn.StringExporter(headers=False, ...)`, and load_games_from_text never captures the FEN or SetUp header into the row dict (the _first_present calls at lines 391-420 cover ratings, IDs, dates, ECO, Study identity — no 'fen'/'setup'). Three call sites later reparse that headerless Movetext with `chess.pgn.read_game(io.StringIO(movetext))`: mainline_movetext (line 212), has_my_analysis (line 305), and engine_analysis_core.analyze_game (engine_analysis_core.py line 705). All of them reconstruct the game from the standard starting position. For a Lichess Study chapter that starts from a custom FEN (Studies allow this — e.g. a position chapter or a game resumed from a diagram), the first move is illegal from the standard start, python-chess records the error into game.errors and truncates, and the reparse yields an empty or near-empty mainline. The Game-detail clean-replay view, the 'My Analysis' flag, and engine analysis all silently degrade for that chapter, while the primary parse (which still had the header) shows full Moves/Plies — an inconsistent row.
Why it matters
The initial parse and the Movetext-derived features disagree for the same Game with no error anywhere: the games list shows a 40-move game while the detail viewer replays nothing and Analyzed=False even when Lichess embedded [%eval]s. ADR 0004's 'degrades to analyzed=False' is meant for genuinely un-analyzed Games, not for Games whose data was corrupted at an internal boundary.
How to fix
Preserve the starting position across the boundary: either export with headers included (or at minimum re-emit `[FEN "..."]`/`[SetUp "1"]` when game.headers carries them) in extract_movetext, or store the FEN in its own column and have the three reparse sites prepend it before read_game.
Expected improvement
Custom-position chapters get a correct replay view, correct has_my_analysis, and working engine-analysis enrichment instead of silently empty features.
Evidence
exporter = chess.pgn.StringExporter(
    headers=False, variations=True, comments=True
)
return game.accept(exporter).strip()  ...later...  game = chess.pgn.read_game(io.StringIO(movetext))

Concurrent UscfCache instances do whole-file read-modify-write: a dismissal made during a running Sync is erased from disk

sync.py:320-330 · reviewer: sync-store
What it is
Every UscfCache instance loads the entire JSON file into self._data at construction and _write() dumps that entire in-memory copy back (atomically per-write via os.replace, but not merged with concurrent writers). Multiple instances of the same file are live at once: sync_uscf constructs one at Sync start (sync.py:379) and calls replace_current after its network fetches complete (seconds to minutes later), while data.dismiss_reconciliation_entry constructs a fresh instance per click (data.py:694) and _detect_new_achievements another (data.py:366). In a threaded server, a dismissal clicked while a Sync's USCF fetches are in flight is written to disk, then overwritten when the Sync's stale instance writes its pre-dismissal snapshot — the dismissal survives in store.dismissed for this process's lifetime (the `| store.dismissed` merge at data.py:301) but silently vanishes from the file, so it reappears in Reconciliation after the next restart. Same lost-update shape applies between fetch_immutable/fetch_aged writes and any concurrent instance. Latent under the deployed single-threaded gunicorn config, real on the threaded dev server.
Why it matters
Dismissals are the one piece of durable user judgement the app stores (issue #30: 'survive restarts via the cache'); losing them is a silent, delayed data loss the user only notices when an already-judged discrepancy resurfaces after a redeploy.
How to fix
For the user-state sections (dismissals, seen_achievements), re-read the file inside the mutating method before writing (read-merge-write), or narrow _write to update only the section that changed by merging into a freshly-read copy. A module-level lock around UscfCache writes for the same path would also close the threaded window cheaply.
Expected improvement
User dismissals and seen-achievement bookkeeping survive a Sync racing a click, matching the documented persistence promise.
Evidence
sync.py: "def _write(self) -> None:\n        ...\n            json.dump(self._data, f)\n        os.replace(tmp_path, self._path)" — whole-object dump; sync_uscf: "cache = UscfCache(cache_path)" held across all fetches before "cache.replace_current({...})"; data.py:694: "UscfCache(store.uscf_cache_path).add_dismissal(entry_id)"
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read sync.py:162-501 (UscfCache class, sync_uscf, _fetch_standings/_fetch_opponent_profiles), data.py:280-310/355-375/680-700, and gunicorn.conf.py. All cited mechanics check out exactly as described: __init__ (sync.py:189) snapshots the whole file into self._data once; _write (sync.py:320-330 — line cite correct) json.dumps the entire in-memory dict and os.replace's the file, with no re-read/merge. sync_uscf constructs its instance at sync.py:379, runs seven network fetches (382-388) before replace_current at 393, and keeps writing through fetch_aged (line 260) and fetch_immutable (line 229) during _fetch_opponent_profiles/_fetch_standings — each write dumps the construction-time snapshot of the dismissals/seen_achievements sections. A dismissal written by the fresh per-click instance at data.py:694 in that window is clobbered on disk by the Sync instance's next write; it survives in memory only via the union at data.py:301, so it silently reappears in Reconciliation after restart — exactly the claimed failure. The store.sync_lock (data.py:431) only serializes Syncs, not dismissal-vs-Sync. Production exposure is correctly scoped: gunicorn.conf.py pins workers=1 with worker_class="sync" (one request at a time), so the race is latent in the deployed config and real on the threaded Flask dev server (Flask's run() defaults threaded=True) — the finding already says this, and "low" severity matches that exposure. This is a genuine concurrency bug, not the ADR 0006 single-worker design (which covers the in-memory store, not the cache file). Not covered by issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86. Proposed fix (read-merge-write for user-state sections, or a module-level per-path lock) is sound; note both are needed for full coverage on the dev server since the writers are in different call stacks, but the lock alone closes the practical single-process window.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Verified against /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/sync.py and data.py. All cited anchors are accurate: UscfCache._write (sync.py:320-330) json.dumps the entire self._data snapshot loaded at construction (sync.py:189) and os.replace()s the whole file; sync_uscf constructs its instance at sync.py:379 and calls replace_current at sync.py:393 only after seven sequential network fetches; dismiss_reconciliation_entry constructs a fresh instance per click at data.py:694; _detect_new_achievements another at data.py:366; the in-memory `| store.dismissed` merge at data.py:301 confirms the dismissal survives in-process while the file copy is clobbered. No lock, no re-read before write anywhere in the class — the lost-update is real code behavior. Materiality checks I ran to refute it: (1) Production is immune — gunicorn.conf.py pins workers=1, worker_class="sync" (ADR 0006), so the sole thread is busy inside refresh() during a Sync and a dismiss request cannot interleave; refresh() itself is fully synchronous (no Dash background/long callbacks, no threading.Thread anywhere in app.py/shell.py/pages). (2) The dev path is exposed — app.py:254 calls dash_app.run() with no threaded= override, and the Flask dev server is threaded by default, so the described race (dismiss clicked during a Sync's USCF fetch window, then erased by replace_current's stale whole-file write) is reachable exactly as stated. (3) Not intentional: the class docstring (sync.py:180-184) promises dismissals are "never touched by replace_current" — true of the dict key, false of the file write — and add_dismissal's docstring only disclaims the unwritable-disk case, not silent overwrite; issue #30 says dismissals should survive restarts. (4) Not covered by exclusions #80/#40/PRs 82-86. Corrections: none material. The finding itself already correctly scopes it as latent in the deployed config, so severity "low" is right (not higher — the deployed topology mitigates it by design; not "info" — dismissals are the app's only durable user judgement and the loss is silent and delayed). Proposed fix (read-merge-write inside add_dismissal/record_achievements, or a module-level per-path lock) is sound and small; note replace_current should also merge-preserve the dismissals/seen_achievements/immutable/aged sections from a fresh read to fully close the window.

enrich_games returns an empty DataFrame without the enrichment columns, breaking the always-exist contract

uscf_core.py:1192-1197 · reviewer: uscf-matching
What it is
enrich_games short-circuits on an empty input ('if enriched.empty: return enriched') before the loop that adds _ENRICHMENT_DEFAULTS, so an empty Games DataFrame comes back with no UscfMatched/Forfeit/UscfEventId/... columns. This directly contradicts ADR 0003's contract that enrichment columns ALWAYS exist so pages never check column presence, and it is inconsistent with attach_round_numbers in the same file, which explicitly handles the empty case by adding the column anyway ('out["UscfRound"] = pd.Series(dtype="float64")', lines 534-536) with a comment citing the contract. Today nothing crashes only because every consumer independently guards with df.empty (series_summary line 636-640 even re-adds the defaults defensively), i.e. pages/helpers are doing exactly the column-presence-style checking the contract says they should never need.
Why it matters
The always-exist contract is one of the repo's documented invariants; the empty-df hole means any new consumer that trusts the contract (e.g. df[df["Forfeit"]] without an empty guard) raises KeyError precisely in the no-games state — a silent landmine that only fires in the least-tested configuration (fresh sync, demo user with zero games).
How to fix
In enrich_games, add the _ENRICHMENT_DEFAULTS columns (with appropriate empty dtypes) before the empty early-return, mirroring attach_round_numbers' empty-case handling; the defensive default-injection in series_summary can then stay purely for the mid-sync window it documents.
Expected improvement
The enrichment-columns-always-exist invariant holds unconditionally, and boolean-mask consumers no longer need df.empty guards to avoid KeyError on the zero-games state.
Evidence
enriched = df.copy()
    if enriched.empty:
        return enriched

    for column, default in _ENRICHMENT_DEFAULTS.items():
        enriched[column] = default

_normalize_name never folds diacritics, so accented chapter opponent names can never name-match USCF's ASCII records

uscf_core.py:1082-1085 · reviewer: uscf-matching
What it is
The name-fallback normalizer only lowercases, strips punctuation ([^\w\s], which keeps Unicode letters because \w is Unicode in Python), and collapses whitespace. USCF registers names in plain ASCII (e.g. 'JOSE GARCIA'), while a Lichess chapter can carry the accented spelling ('José García'). After normalization the strings still differ ('jose garcia' vs 'josé garcía'), the exact-equality check fails, and the spelling-variant fallback also fails because the last names ('garcia' vs 'garcía') are compared for exact equality. The same normalizer also turns hyphenated last names ('Smith-Jones' → 'smithjones') into a single token that can never equal USCF's space-separated form. Result: these opponents are systematically unmatched by the name pass — a permanent false negative, never a false positive.
Why it matters
ADR 0007 accepts missed matches, but this miss is systematic and invisible: every game against an accented-name opponent without a typed FideId shows up forever as a lichess_only + missing_fide_id pair in Reconciliation with no hint that the name pass was structurally incapable of matching, even when USCF has exactly one fitting record in the window. Typing the FideId fixes each case manually, but the normalizer's stated purpose (case- and punctuation-insensitive matching) implies it should already handle the common Latin-diacritic case.
How to fix
In _normalize_name, fold diacritics before comparison (unicodedata.normalize('NFKD', name) then strip combining marks), and replace punctuation with a space instead of the empty string so 'Smith-Jones' normalizes to 'smith jones'. Both changes only widen equality toward USCF's own ASCII spellings, so the false-positive risk is limited to the already-accepted variant-tolerance rules.
Expected improvement
Name-fallback matching works for accented and hyphenated opponent names, removing a class of perpetual Reconciliation noise without loosening the ambiguity rules.
Evidence
def _normalize_name(name: str) -> str:
    """Lowercase, punctuation stripped, whitespace collapsed."""
    cleaned = re.sub(r"[^\w\s]", "", name.lower())
    return " ".join(cleaned.split())
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read uscf_core.py:1062-1085; evidence snippet is verbatim at cited lines 1082-1085. Verified live: Python's \w is Unicode for str, so re.sub(r"[^\w\s]","", 'josé garcía') keeps accents; _names_match's exact-equality and last-name-variant fallback (line 1078) both fail for 'garcía' vs 'garcia'. No unicodedata/NFKD/unidecode folding anywhere in the repo. Also confirmed 'smith-jones' -> 'smithjones' (hyphen deleted, not replaced with space); that sub-claim only bites when USCF stores the name space-separated — if USCF also hyphenates, both fold identically and match, so its scope is slightly narrower than stated. Miss is a pure false negative (never a false positive), consistent with ADR 0007's accepted-miss posture — low severity is appropriate. Not a duplicate of #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86. Proposed fix (NFKD fold + replace punctuation with space) is sound.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/uscf_core.py lines 1021-1135 (_name_pass, _names_match, _normalize_name) and the name-pass tests in tests/test_uscf_core.py (TestMatchGamesByName, ~lines 685-780). Confirmed at the cited lines 1082-1085: _normalize_name only lowercases, strips [^\w\s] (Unicode \w keeps accented letters), and collapses whitespace — no unicodedata/NFKD folding anywhere in the repo (grep for diacritic/unicodedata/NFKD found nothing). The core claim holds: 'José García' normalizes to 'josé garcía', which fails both the exact-equality check and the variant fallback (last tokens 'garcía' vs 'garcia' compared exactly at line 1078), so an accented chapter name can never name-match USCF's ASCII record. Tests cover case and punctuation but not diacritics, so this is untested behavior, not a documented invariant — the docstring's cited PRD rules ('case- and punctuation-insensitive') arguably promise more than the code delivers for the common Latin-diacritic case. Mitigations that keep severity at low, as the finding itself concedes: the miss is fail-safe (never a false positive), consistent with ADR 0007's match-never-guess bias; every miss surfaces in Reconciliation as lichess_only + missing_fide_id; and typing the FideId resolves it permanently. One overstatement: the hyphen sub-claim ('Smith-Jones' → 'smithjones') only bites if the two sources disagree on hyphen-vs-space — if USCF also stores 'SMITH-JONES', both sides normalize identically to 'smithjones' and match fine, and the proposed punctuation→space fix would then be needed on both sides anyway (which it is, since both names pass through _normalize_name, so the fix is still safe). The diacritic half of the fix (NFKD + strip combining marks) is correct and strictly widens matches toward USCF's ASCII spellings. Not covered by excluded issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86.
lowConfirmed backend effort: trivial

_rating_mismatch_entries uses an exact-month supplement lookup while the rating lens uses latest-on-or-before, silently skipping gap months

uscf_core.py:1567-1581 · reviewer: uscf-matching
What it is
The reconciliation rating-mismatch check builds official_by_month keyed by (year, month) and looks up the supplement for the matched event's start month exactly: 'official = official_by_month.get((start.year, start.month))'; when no supplement exists in that calendar month it gets None and the entry is skipped ('if official is None or typed == official: continue'). But the module's own definition of the Official Rating in effect — _supplement_in_effect (lines 1381-1391), used by the Official lens — is 'the latest supplement published on or before' the date. build_official_series explicitly documents that gap months exist ('neither are gap months nor months whose supplement carries no Regular rating', lines 182-184). So for an event starting in a gap month, the lens displays May's supplement as the Official Rating while the reconciliation check compares against nothing and silently reports no mismatch, even when the typed header rating disagrees with the in-effect value.
Why it matters
Two different definitions of 'the Official Rating in effect' live in the same module: the one users see (the lens) and the one reconciliation validates against. A typed-rating discrepancy in a gap month is exactly the bookkeeping this feature exists to surface, and it goes undetected with no signal that the check was skipped.
How to fix
Replace the (year, month) dict lookup with _supplement_in_effect(official_series, start) so the mismatch check compares typed ratings against the same in-effect supplement the Official lens displays (adjust the uscf_says wording to name the supplement's actual month).
Expected improvement
Rating-mismatch reconciliation entries appear for events in supplement gap months, and the check is definitionally consistent with the Official lens.
Evidence
official_by_month = {
    (point.month.year, point.month.month): point.rating
    for point in official_series
}
...
official = official_by_month.get((start.year, start.month))
typed = int(game["PlayerRatingNum"])
if official is None or typed == official:
    continue
Verifier notes (2)

Meanwhile _supplement_in_effect (lines 1381-1391) — used by the lens path via _official_rating_for_game at line 1378 — defines the Official Rating as the latest supplement on or before the date. build_official_series's docstring (lines 181-183) explicitly acknowledges gap months and months whose supplement carries no Regular rating, so the divergence is reachable: an event in a gap month gets a displayed Official Rating from the lens but is silently skipped by the mismatch check. Two nuances: (1) the inline comment at lines 1565-1566 shows the exact-month keying is deliberate, but its stated purpose is day-of-month quirks, not gap months, so this is not an intentional-design exclusion; (2) one could argue the docstring ('the Official Rating for the matched Rated Event's start month') scopes the check to same-month supplements by design, but that scoping contradicts the module's own in-effect definition, which is exactly the finding's point. Cited lines are accurate; severity low is appropriate (validation-only bookkeeping, per the function's own docstring — typed values power no stats). The proposed fix (_supplement_in_effect(official_series, start) plus uscf_says wording naming the supplement's actual month) is correct.

Severity low is appropriate: reconciliation is bookkeeping only (the docstring notes typed ratings power no stats), impact is a missed advisory entry, and no ADR is violated. Forfeit exclusion missing from opponent_summary, activity_data, daily_activity, and round_performance win rates

pgn_stats_core.py:758-774 · reviewer: pgn-stats
What it is
Beyond the performance-rating and game-length cases reported separately, three more per-category win-rate functions skip _without_forfeits(): opponent_summary (line 766 groups the raw df), activity_data (line 1050 filters only on date + decisive outcome), daily_activity (line 1097, same pattern), and round_performance (line 1438). A forfeit win therefore raises the displayed WinRate against that opponent, for that month/day-of-week, on the calendar's Net, and for that round number, while the adjacent Overview win rate excludes it. Whether every one of these should exclude forfeits is a product call (a forfeit is arguably real 'activity'), but the WinRate columns specifically contradict the issue #29 rule that a forfeit win never counts as a win.
Why it matters
Cross-page inconsistency: the same forfeit game counts as a win in the opponents table, activity charts, and round-fatigue table but not in the headline win rate, which reads as a data bug to anyone comparing the numbers.
How to fix
Apply `df = _without_forfeits(df)` in these four functions (or, if forfeits should still appear as activity volume, exclude them only from the Win/WinRate/Net computations and document the choice).
Expected improvement
One consistent forfeit policy across every win-rate surface, matching win_draw_loss_counts and streaks.
Evidence

kpi_stats current_rating uses a non-stable single-key sort, so same-day rating ties resolve arbitrarily

pgn_stats_core.py:679-681 · reviewer: pgn-stats
What it is
current_rating is taken as `dated.sort_values("Date_dt").iloc[-1]["PlayerRatingNum"]`. pandas sort_values defaults to quicksort, which is not stable, and there is no Index tiebreaker — so among several games on the same (most recent) date, which row lands last is unspecified. Every other 'latest' computation in the module breaks ties explicitly: player_rating_over_time sorts by ["Date_dt", "Index"] (line 747) and scouting_report's _latest_rating does the same (line 865). PGN headers carry pre-game ratings, so within a multi-round tournament day the rows can genuinely differ, and the KPI can show a stale round's rating depending on quicksort's whim.
Why it matters
The 'current rating' KPI can silently flip between values after an unrelated re-sort or pandas upgrade, and can disagree with the rating timeline chart, which uses the Index tiebreak.
How to fix
Sort with the same key as the siblings: `dated.sort_values(["Date_dt", "Index"]).iloc[-1]`.
Expected improvement
Deterministic current-rating value that always matches the last point of player_rating_over_time.
Evidence
dated = df[df["Date_dt"].notna() & df["PlayerRatingNum"].notna()]
    if not dated.empty:
        current_rating = int(dated.sort_values("Date_dt").iloc[-1]["PlayerRatingNum"])
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/pgn_stats_core.py lines 665-694 and grepped all sort_values calls. Line 681 is exactly as quoted: `dated.sort_values("Date_dt").iloc[-1]["PlayerRatingNum"]` with no Index tiebreaker. Cited siblings confirmed: line 747 sorts ["Date_dt", "Index"], line 865 (scouting _latest_rating) sorts ["Date_dt", "Index"]; lines 602, 788, 1636, 1753 also use the Index tiebreak, making 681 the lone outlier. pandas sort_values default kind is quicksort (unstable), so same-day ties resolve in unspecified order and the KPI can disagree with the rating timeline chart. Minor nuance: for a fixed pandas/numpy version and identical input the result is deterministic, so "flips after a pandas upgrade or re-sort" is the accurate failure mode rather than run-to-run nondeterminism — the finding says as much. Fix suggestion is correct. Low severity appropriate.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read pgn_stats_core.py lines 660-710 and grepped all sort_values calls in the module. Confirmed: line 681 in kpi_stats is `dated.sort_values("Date_dt").iloc[-1]["PlayerRatingNum"]` — single-key sort, default kind (quicksort, not stable), no "Index" tiebreak. The module's established convention is ["Date_dt"/"_ds", "Index"] everywhere else (lines 602, 747, 788, 865, 1636, 1753), and sync.py:695-700 / uscf_core.py:643 do the same, so line 681 is the lone outlier and can disagree with the rating timeline (line 747) and scouting_report's _latest_rating (line 865), whose line references in the finding are exactly right. "Index" is a real column assigned in PGN parse order (line 426) and reassigned after dedupe in sync.py, so the proposed fix `sort_values(["Date_dt", "Index"])` is correct and matches siblings. Tests only assert the KPI dict keys exist (tests/test_pgn_stats_core.py:1682) — no tie-order coverage, so no mitigation. Two materiality caveats that keep this at low, not higher: (1) quicksort is deterministic for a given array and pandas version, so the value doesn't flip run-to-run — it can only change across pandas upgrades or upstream reorderings, slightly softer than the finding's "quicksort's whim" phrasing; (2) for OTB USCF events the PGN header rating is typically constant across all rounds of one event, so same-day ties usually carry identical ratings and the wrong tiebreak often produces the same number. Multi-event same-day games or differing headers are where it bites. Severity low is appropriate; the finding stands as a real consistency bug with a correct one-line fix.
lowConfirmed backend effort: trivial

_BEST_MOVE_RE cannot match castling with check/mate suffix ('O-O+ was best')

engine_analysis_core.py:236-238 · reviewer: engine-analysis
What it is
The piece-move alternative in _BEST_MOVE_RE ends with `[+#]?`, but the castling alternative `O-O(?:-O)?` has no optional check/mate suffix before `\s+was\s+best`. A Lichess judgment like 'Mistake. O-O+ was best.' (castling with check is legal SAN and Lichess includes the + suffix) fails to match, so best_move falls back to refutation_line[0] — which, per the siblings[0] issue above, may be a user variation's first move rather than the engine's castle, feeding _best_move_is_forcing the wrong move.
Why it matters
A missed castling-with-check best move is by definition a missed forcing move; misparsing it can flip the mistake's tactical classification and the resulting emitted Tags on exactly the moves where the distinction matters.
How to fix
Move the `[+#]?` outside the alternation or append it to the castling branch: `(O-O(?:-O)?[+#]?)`.
Expected improvement
Judgments recommending castling with check parse correctly instead of relying on the variation fallback.
Evidence
_BEST_MOVE_RE = re.compile(
    r"\b([KQRBN]?[a-h]?[1-8]?x?[a-h][1-8](?:=[QRBN])?[+#]?|O-O(?:-O)?)\s+was\s+best",
)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Verified in /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/engine_analysis_core.py. The regex at lines 236-238 is exactly as quoted: the [+#]? suffix is inside the piece-move alternative only, and the castling alternative `O-O(?:-O)?` has no optional suffix; since `+`/`#` cannot satisfy the following `\s+`, the match fails entirely (not just partially). Confirmed empirically: re.search returns None for 'Mistake. O-O+ was best.' and 'Blunder. O-O-O# was best.' but matches 'O-O was best'. The claimed fallback chain is also real: line 329-331 sets best_move = refutation[0] when the judgment parse returns None, and _refutation_line (line 275) takes siblings[0] of the parent node, so the fallback can pick a user variation's first move when one precedes the engine line. best_move feeds _best_move_is_forcing (lines 575-581), which drives tactical classification at line 627. One caveat softening impact: in typical Lichess exports the sibling variation IS the engine line starting with the missed castle, so the fallback usually yields the correct move; the wrong-classification outcome requires a manually-added variation ordered before the engine one. Severity low is appropriate. Suggested fix (`O-O(?:-O)?[+#]?` or moving [+#]? outside the alternation) is correct; if moved outside, group boundaries need care so group(1) still captures the suffix consistently.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed empirically: I read engine_analysis_core.py lines 226-345 and 575-630, and executed the regex — 'O-O+ was best', 'O-O-O+ was best', and 'O-O# was best' all return None; 'O-O was best' matches. The castling branch of _BEST_MOVE_RE (lines 236-238) has no [+#]? suffix, exactly as described. Proposed fix (append [+#]? to the O-O(?:-O)? branch or hoist it outside the alternation) is correct and harmless — parse_san in _best_move_is_forcing (line 581) accepts SAN with +/# suffixes. Materiality caveat that supports keeping severity at low: the fallback at lines 328-331 sets best_move = refutation_line[0], and in a standard Lichess export the judged move's sibling variation IS the engine's best line, so refutation[0] would be the correct 'O-O+' SAN in the common case. The misparse only produces a wrong best_move when siblings[0] is a user-authored variation preceding the engine line (the linked siblings[0] finding), or a None best_move when there is no sibling variation at all — in that case _best_move_is_forcing returns False (line 578) and a tactical mistake gets classified positional. Also, ADR 0004 frames engine analysis as enrichment-only, so the blast radius is Tags/classification, not core data. Real bug, narrow trigger (missed castling-with-check as the best move, plus a degraded/ambiguous variation structure), low severity confirmed. No test in tests/ covers castling-with-suffix judgments.
lowConfirmed frontend effort: trivial

'Last 20' preset windows over NaT-dated rows, covering fewer than the last 20 games

filters.py:264-267 · reviewer: shell-filters
What it is
apply_preset computes the Last-20 window from the full DataFrame: `last20 = df.sort_values("Date_dt").tail(20)`. pandas sorts NaT last, so when N undated Games exist the tail(20) contains those N NaT rows plus only the latest 20-N dated Games, and the resulting start date covers fewer than 20 real games. The function already builds `dated = df[df["Date_dt"].notna()]` two lines above (line 256) but doesn't use it here.
Why it matters
The preset's contract is 'the last 20 games'; with any undated Games in the archive it silently delivers a smaller window (and the undated games themselves are then excluded by the date filter, compounding the previous finding).
How to fix
Sort the already-computed `dated` frame instead: `last20 = dated.sort_values("Date_dt").tail(20)`.
Expected improvement
The Last-20 preset always spans the 20 most recent dated Games regardless of how many undated rows exist.
Evidence
dated = df[df["Date_dt"].notna()] ... if not dated.empty: last20 = df.sort_values("Date_dt").tail(20)

update_filter_options can leave moves-slider value and date selection outside the new bounds after a shrinking Sync

filters.py:361-372 · reviewer: shell-filters
What it is
After a Sync, update_filter_options always pushes new min/max onto moves-filter and new min/max_date_allowed onto date-filter, but only resets the *selected* value/start/end when `(sync_store or {}).get("new_games", 0) > 0`. A Sync that changes the data without adding games — a chapter deleted from a Study, or a date/movetext correction that shrinks the FullMoves or date extent — updates the bounds while the stale selection stays, leaving the RangeSlider value (and possibly the date selection) outside [min, max]. get_filtered then keeps filtering with the stale out-of-range values, and the slider renders an inconsistent state.
Why it matters
Studies are the source of truth and are edited on Lichess, so shrinking Syncs are a legitimate path; the resulting slider/filter state silently disagrees with its own bounds until the user manually touches the control.
How to fix
Clamp instead of skipping: when has_new_games is false, still emit a moves value clamped into [b["min_mv"], b["max_mv"]] (and start/end clamped into the new allowed date window) whenever the current selection falls outside the new bounds. That requires reading the current values as State in this callback.
Expected improvement
Filter controls can never hold selections outside their own advertised ranges after any kind of Sync, not just additive ones.
Evidence
has_new_games = (sync_store or {}).get("new_games", 0) > 0 ... moves_value = [b["min_mv"], b["max_mv"]] if has_new_games else no_update ... return (..., b["min_mv"], b["max_mv"], moves_value)
Verifier notes (2)

Confirmed: (1) shell.py run_sync writes {"seq": seq+1, "new_games": len(outcome.new_games)} on EVERY successful Sync, including one with 0 new games — so a shrinking Sync (deleted chapter, corrected date/movetext) does trigger update_filter_options. (2) update_filter_options (filters.py 346-373) unconditionally emits new min/max on moves-filter and min/max_date_allowed on date-filter, but gates start_date/end_date/value behind has_new_games = new_games > 0 (lines 362-365), returning no_update otherwise — the evidence quote matches the file verbatim. (3) get_filtered passes the stale slider value and date strings straight into apply_filters with no clamping, so a selection like moves [40,60] against a new max of 35 filters everything out while the slider shows handles outside its own track. No other callback clamps (the reset callback at ~line 252 only fires on the reset button). Minor correction: the gating logic starts at line 362, not 361 (361 is the tail of a comment). Also note the "active filters" badge logic at lines 324-327 compares selections against fresh bounds, so a stale out-of-range selection can additionally miscount as an active filter — same root cause. Severity low is right: requires a shrinking Sync plus a pre-existing selection near the old extremes, and touching the control recovers. Proposed fix (clamp via State on current values) is sound.

Repertoire node score % encodes above/below-baseline only as green-vs-red text color

pages/openings.py:150-159 · reviewer: colorblind-a11y
What it is
In the repertoire tree, each branch node's score is colored `score_cls = "win" if node["score_pct"] >= baseline else "loss"` and rendered as `html.Span(f"{node['score_pct']:.0f}%", className=f"rep-node-score {score_cls}")` (`.rep-node-score.win/.loss` color-only, custom.css:1987-1988). The baseline is the player's dynamic overall score, not 50%, so the number itself does not reveal which side of the threshold it is on; the color is the sole carrier of the above/below-baseline judgment. The separate "⚠ leaking points" flag only appears for nodes past the stricter `underperforming` test, so merely-below-baseline nodes have no non-color cue.
Why it matters
For a red-green colorblind viewer the green and red score percentages look alike, and unlike the KPI tiles (labeled "Win %") or signed rating deltas, there is no textual fallback: a 48% node above a 45% baseline and a 48% node below a 52% baseline are visually identical. It is a secondary cue (the W/D/L mini-bar and game counts sit alongside), hence low severity.
How to fix
Add a glyph or sign to the score span when below baseline (e.g. a small "▾"/"▴" prefix, or show the delta vs baseline as signed text in the title/inline), or drop the below-baseline red entirely and rely on the existing ⚠ flag as the sole negative marker.
Expected improvement
Above/below-baseline standing in the repertoire tree becomes readable without hue discrimination, consistent with how the rest of the app pairs outcome colors with words.
Evidence
score_cls = "win" if node["score_pct"] >= baseline else "loss"
...
html.Span(f"{node['score_pct']:.0f}%",
          className=f"rep-node-score {score_cls}"),

Baseline is tree["score_pct"] passed from update_repertoire (openings.py:212), i.e. dynamic, so the number alone cannot reveal its side of the threshold. The ⚠ "leaking points" flag fires only on the stricter `underperforming` test, so merely-below-baseline nodes have no non-color cue — exactly as described. Coach board PGN can carry two conflicting results: the user's Result header wrapped around the coach chapter's result token in the movetext

pages/game_detail.py:437 (with coach_match_core.py:162-169 and _game_pgn at 233-256) · reviewer: coach-review-matching
What it is
CoachChapter.movetext is exported via `chess.pgn.StringExporter(headers=False, variations=True, comments=True)`, which appends the coach game's result token (often '*' — coach Chapters are analysis boards that frequently lack a set result) at the end of the movetext. `_board_section` then builds the Coach view PGN as `_game_pgn(game, coach_chapter.movetext)`, which prepends the USER's headers including `("Result", game.get("Result"))`. The resulting PGN can say `[Result "1-0"]` in the header while the movetext terminates with `*` (or even the opposite decisive result if the coach mis-set it), and the pgn-viewer renders the movetext's terminator as the game outcome in the move list.
Why it matters
ADR 0001 says the user's Study version of a disputed fact is what displays; the Coach tab can show a different result than the Game tab for the same Game, purely as an export artifact. It is also simply confusing to see '*' after a game the user won.
How to fix
Strip the trailing result token from CoachChapter.movetext at parse time (or in _game_pgn) — e.g. drop a final '1-0'/'0-1'/'1/2-1/2'/'*' token — since _game_pgn already supplies the authoritative Result header from the user's Game.
Expected improvement
The Coach board view always shows the same outcome as the rest of the Game detail page, honoring the source-of-truth rule.
Evidence
exporter = chess.pgn.StringExporter(headers=False, variations=True, comments=True)
... movetext=game.accept(exporter).strip()
... data_attrs["data-pgn-coach"] = _game_pgn(game, coach_chapter.movetext)
... ("Result", game.get("Result")),

lpv-init.js: re-clicking the already-active view button re-mounts the viewer and resets the replay position

assets/lpv-init.js:88-116 · reviewer: client-js-lpv-seam
What it is
The click handler has no early return for the already-active button: clicking "Game" (or "My Analysis"/"Coach") while it is active falls through to `renderBoard(card, data, view)`, which by design rebuilds the mount from scratch. A double-click or an accidental re-click therefore throws away the user's current position in the move list and any board state, snapping back to the start of the game.
Why it matters
Losing your place mid-review of a long game over a stray click is a small but repeatable annoyance on the page where Daniel actually studies his games; deliberate view *switches* resetting position is the documented design ("switching views is just a fresh mount"), but a no-op click resetting it is not.
How to fix
First line of the click handler: `if (btn.classList.contains("active")) { return; }`.
Expected improvement
Idempotent clicks; replay position survives accidental re-clicks of the current tab.
Evidence
btn.addEventListener("click", function () {
  Array.prototype.forEach.call(switches, function (s) { s.classList.remove("active"); });
  btn.classList.add("active");
  ... renderBoard(card, data, view);

_TAG_RE matches URL fragments in comments, producing phantom Tags

pgn_stats_core.py:231, 283-287 · reviewer: pgn-parse-lesson-tag-extraction
What it is
_TAG_RE is `r"#([a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*)"` and extract_lessons_and_tags runs `.findall` over the whole comment text with no boundary or context guard. The leading-letter requirement correctly excludes SAN mate suffixes ('Qxf7#' — next char is whitespace) and '#1', but a URL anchor in a comment matches: a comment like 'compare https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucena_position#Endgame' yields the phantom Tag 'endgame' — which is even a CANONICAL_TAGS entry, so it lands in the canonical section of tag_counts and in recurring-weakness signals. Any '#word' fragment (docs anchors, lichess forum links) becomes a Tag.
Why it matters
Tags drive the Lessons page taxonomy and recurring_weaknesses; a pasted reference link silently tags a Game with a weakness it doesn't have, and per ADR 0002 there is no in-app way to remove it — Daniel would have to notice and edit the Lichess comment.
How to fix
Require the '#' to be at start-of-string or preceded by whitespace/punctuation that can't be part of a URL, e.g. `(?:(?<=\s)|^)#([a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*)` with re.MULTILINE, or strip URLs (`https?://\S+`) from the text before tag extraction.
Expected improvement
Comments containing links stop injecting phantom Tags into the taxonomy and weakness detection.
Evidence
_TAG_RE = re.compile(r"#([a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*)")  ...  for tag in _TAG_RE.findall(text):
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed by reading pgn_stats_core.py lines 225-290 and executing the regex. _TAG_RE (line 231) is exactly r"#([a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*)" and extract_lessons_and_tags calls .findall on the full comment text (line 283) after stripping only [%...] Lichess directives (line 275) — URLs are not stripped. Ran the regex on 'https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucena_position#Endgame' → ['Endgame'], lowercased to 'endgame', a CANONICAL_TAGS entry (line 240) that lands in the canonical section of tag_counts (line 1588). 'Qxf7#' correctly yields no match, as the finding states. Line citations are accurate. No test covers URLs in comments; not a duplicate of issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86. Severity low is right: requires Daniel to paste a '#word'-bearing link into a study comment, and the fix (strip https?://\S+ before extraction, or a lookbehind boundary) is small. Minor correction to the suggested fix: the proposed (?:(?<=\s)|^)# needs re.MULTILINE only if comments are multi-line and a tag starts a non-first line; the URL-strip approach is simpler and safer.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/pgn_stats_core.py lines 220-304 and confirmed the code matches the finding exactly: _TAG_RE = re.compile(r"#([a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*)") at line 231, unguarded .findall over each comment at lines 283-287 (only [%...] directives are stripped first, line 275). Reproduced empirically: re.findall on 'compare https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucena_position#Endgame and #tactics' returns ['Endgame', 'tactics'] — the URL fragment becomes the phantom canonical tag 'endgame'. No mitigation exists: docs/decisions/0002 says hashtags anywhere in comments become tags (so the phantom flows into the canonical taxonomy and recurring-weakness signals), tests/test_pgn_stats_core.py has no URL-in-comment case, and per ADR 0002 there is no app-side edit to remove a bad tag — Daniel must notice and edit the Lichess comment. Severity 'low' is right: it requires pasting a URL with a fragment into a study comment, which is plausible but occasional, and the effect is one wrong tag per such comment, correctable on Lichess. One correction to the proposed fix: the suggested `(?:(?<=\s)|^)#...` regex would also reject legitimate tags preceded by punctuation, e.g. '(#tactics)' or 'see:#endgame'; the safer alternative the finding also offers — stripping `https?://\S+` from the text before extraction — is the better of the two fixes.

has_my_analysis discards user-drawn [%cal]/[%csl] shapes as 'machine annotations', so arrow-only analysis reads as no analysis

pgn_stats_core.py:233-235, 312-317 · reviewer: pgn-parse-lesson-tag-extraction
What it is
The directive stripper's comment (lines 233-234) lumps `[%cal ...]` and `[%csl ...]` in with `[%clk ...]` as 'machine annotations', and has_my_analysis strips all `[%...]` directives before deciding whether Daniel 'added something to the Chapter himself'. But on Lichess, [%cal] (arrows) and [%csl] (circles) in a Study chapter are produced by the user drawing shapes on the board — they are exactly the kind of hand analysis the docstring says should count ('a comment of his own'). A chapter Daniel annotated purely with arrows/circles (no prose, no variations) returns has_my_analysis=False, so the Game-detail view never offers the 'My Analysis' board even though his shapes exist in the Movetext and the vendored pgn-viewer could render them. [%clk]/[%eval] are the genuinely machine-generated ones.
Why it matters
Shape-only annotation is a common Lichess Study habit; those chapters' analysis is invisible in the app — the annotated view is withheld precisely for the games where the annotation is purely visual.
How to fix
In has_my_analysis, treat a comment as 'his own' if, after stripping only the machine directives ([%eval], [%clk]), it contains prose OR a [%cal]/[%csl] directive — e.g. test the raw comment against a `\[%(cal|csl) ` pattern before the blanket strip.
Expected improvement
Arrow/circle-annotated chapters correctly surface the My Analysis board.
Evidence
# Lichess embeds machine annotations in comments: [%clk 1:30:00], [%cal ...],
# [%csl ...]. Strip them before looking for Lessons/Tags.
...
text = _LICHESS_DIRECTIVE_RE.sub("", raw).strip()
if text and not _LESSON_RE.match(text):
    return True

.dockerignore excludes uscf_cache.json and analysis_cache.json but not games.pgn, so the local PGN cache is baked into the image

.dockerignore:1-16 · reviewer: deploy-config
What it is
The Dockerfile does `COPY . .` and relies on .dockerignore to keep local caches out of the image. .dockerignore lists `uscf_cache.json` and `analysis_cache.json` but not `games.pgn`, and a 173 KB `games.pgn` (the local cache of the last successful Sync, last written 2026-07-08) sits in the repo root. .gitignore explicitly says 'Never commit game data' and ignores `*.pgn`, but the Docker build ships it anyway. `.coverage` (53 KB, present in the root) and `.ruff_cache` are also not excluded and get copied in.
Why it matters
In production on Fly this file is dead weight only, because fly.toml sets `CACHE_PATH=/data/games.pgn`. But `docker-compose.yml` sets no CACHE_PATH, so config.py's cwd-relative default resolves to the baked-in `/app/games.pgn`: anyone running `make docker-up` boots from Daniel's stale personal sync cache instead of an empty state, and any published image distributes his game data — the exact leak .gitignore was written to prevent (ADR 0001 says the PGN is a disposable cache, not data to ship).
How to fix
Add `games.pgn` (or `*.pgn` with the same `!tests/data/demo-games.pgn` exception already present), `.coverage`, `htmlcov`, and `.ruff_cache` to .dockerignore.
Expected improvement
Images no longer contain personal game data or stale caches; compose runs boot clean; image is slightly smaller.
Evidence

```
uscf_cache.json
analysis_cache.json
```
(no games.pgn line), while .gitignore says:
```
# source of truth — ADR 0001). Never commit game data.
games.pgn
*.pgn
```
and Dockerfile line 5 is `COPY . .`.

Demo seed pseudonyms are trivially reversible via public USCF crosstables (real events, dates, rounds, Elos kept)

tests/data/demo-games.pgn:1-30 · reviewer: data-handling
What it is
config.py:47 states the committed demo file 'must never hold real opponent data', and scripts/anonymize_pgn.py replaces opponent names and member IDs with synthetic ones. But the anonymizer deliberately leaves every quasi-identifier intact: real Event names ('2nd Annual Thanksgiving Open (U1600)', 'ACC vs ANC'), real venues ('Army Navy Club, Washington DC', 'Sterling, VA'), real Dates and Round numbers, and real Elo ratings (`[WhiteElo "1097"]`), while the player's own identity is kept real by design ('Daniel Gentile'). USCF MSA crosstables for these exact events are public, so mapping 'Alex Archer, round 1, 2025.06.20, ACC Friday Ladder, 1097' back to the real opponent is a one-lookup exercise. Each synthetic name is therefore a reversible pseudonym, and the committed file ties re-identifiable real people to coach commentary and `Lesson:` annotations.
Why it matters
The repo is a public resume showcase. The anonymization guarantee the repo makes to itself ('never commit a user's game data', 'must never hold real opponent data') is only nominally met: anyone motivated can attach real names to every game, including annotated blunders and coach remarks about games against those people. The residual facts are public USCF records, so this is linkage rather than disclosure of secrets — hence medium, not high.
How to fix
Extend scripts/anonymize_pgn.py to also perturb the quasi-identifiers in the demo seed: synthesize Event/Site names (a pool like the name pool), shift all Dates by a constant random offset, and optionally jitter Elos by a few points. Keep Rounds/results as-is since they carry the chess meaning.
Expected improvement
The committed demo file becomes genuinely non-linkable to real opponents instead of pseudonymized-with-a-public-lookup-table, honoring the stated 'never real opponent data' guarantee.
Evidence
demo-games.pgn: `[Event "2nd Annual Thanksgiving Open (U1600)"]`, `[Site "Army Navy Club, Washington DC"]`, `[Date "2025.06.20"] [Round "1"]`, `[White "Alex Archer"] [WhiteElo "1097"]` alongside `[Black "Daniel Gentile"]`; anonymize_pgn.py docstring: 'leaving the chess itself ... byte-for-byte intact'
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/tests/data/demo-games.pgn (headers), scripts/anonymize_pgn.py (full), and config.py:40-55. All cited evidence is real and current: the file contains 63 games with real Event names ([Event "2nd Annual Thanksgiving Open (U1600)"] at line 666, [Event "ACC vs ANC"] at line 1230), real venues ([Site "Army Navy Club, Washington DC"] line 1231, [Site "Sterling, VA"] line 1357), real Dates/Rounds, and real opponent Elos ([White "Alex Archer"][WhiteElo "1097"], round 1, 2025.06.20, ACC Friday Ladder — this specific example IS at lines 1-30 as cited; the other quoted tags are deeper in the file, so the line cite only covers part of the evidence). anonymize_pgn.py confirms by inspection that it replaces ONLY names, FideId member IDs, study/chapter IDs, and non-self annotator handles — Event, Site, Date, Round, and Elo tags pass through untouched — while [Black "Daniel Gentile"] is deliberately kept real (SELF_NAME, script lines 26-31). config.py's DEMO_CACHE_PATH comment (lines ~44-46, finding said :47 — off by a line at most) does state the tracked file "must never hold real opponent data". So the linkage attack is as described: Daniel's real name + real event/date/round/result/rating uniquely keys each opponent into public USCF MSA crosstables, making each pseudonym reversible in one lookup, and the file attaches coach commentary and Lesson annotations to those games. Not a duplicate of issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86 (the GPL/AI disclosures are unrelated; no cleanup PR touched anonymization scope). Caveats for the report: the anonymizer's docstring only promises to replace "identifying values" and deliberately keeps the chess byte-for-byte, so this is a known design trade-off rather than a bug in the script — the finding is that the trade-off breaks config.py's stated guarantee. Also the recoverable facts (who played whom in a rated event) are already public USCF records; the incremental exposure is tying re-identified opponents to annotated blunders/coach remarks, which the finding correctly prices at medium rather than high. Suggested fix (perturb Event/Site/Date) is reasonable; note dates likely can't be shifted arbitrarily without breaking rating-history/date-window matching semantics in tests that consume the seed, so verify test fixtures before shifting.

Not excluded by issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86. Ambiguous coach Chapters are indistinguishable from teaching extras and surface nowhere (unmatched_chapters has zero consumers)

coach_match_core.py:112-118, 256-267 · reviewer: coach-review-matching
What it is
match_coach_chapters lumps two very different outcomes into one bucket: (a) coach extras that genuinely match no Game (intended to be dropped) and (b) real coach reviews rejected because of ambiguity — a Chapter fitting two Games, or one Game claimed by two Chapters (`if len(urls) != 1 or len(game_claimants[urls[0]]) != 1: continue`). Both land in `unmatched_chapters`, and a repo-wide grep shows `unmatched_chapters` is read by nothing outside the module and its tests — not by Reconciliation (pages/reconciliation.py contains no coach references), not by data.py, not by any page. The CoachMatchResult docstring promises the extras are "kept ... rather than silently discarded — ... available for inspection", but no surface inspects them. Concretely: two of the user's Games sharing the first 20 plies (deep opening theory the user repeats, entirely plausible over ~60 OTB games) make BOTH coach reviews vanish with no signal anywhere; sync_coach's `failure` field only reports fetch errors, never match ambiguity.
Why it matters
The house rule (ADR 0001/0007 spirit, restated in this module's own docstring) is that disagreements and ambiguity surface in Reconciliation rather than disappearing. Here a coach review the user paid for can silently never render — no Coach tab, no note in the Lessons feed, no Reconciliation row — and the user has no way to discover why, or that anything was dropped at all. The docstring's 'available for inspection' claim is currently false in practice.
How to fix
Distinguish ambiguous-but-plausible Chapters (had >=1 candidate Game, or claimed a contested Game) from zero-candidate extras in CoachMatchResult — e.g. an `ambiguous_chapters` tuple alongside `unmatched_chapters` — and render the ambiguous ones as a section in pages/reconciliation.py, mirroring how USCF ambiguity surfaces there. Zero-candidate extras can keep being dropped silently as designed.
Expected improvement
Ambiguity becomes visible and actionable (the user can rename/split the colliding Chapters on Lichess), matching the module's own documented contract instead of silently eating coach content.
Evidence
if len(urls) != 1 or len(game_claimants[urls[0]]) != 1:
            continue  # ambiguity in either direction → no match, not a guess
... docstring: "kept as ``unmatched_chapters`` rather than silently discarded ... available for inspection" — grep -rn unmatched_chapters --include=*.py (excluding tests) matches only coach_match_core.py itself.

AI-summary cache fingerprint excludes the model and system prompt, so changing either serves stale summaries forever

ai_summary.py:121-126, 140-146 · reviewer: engine-analysis
What it is
The cache key is `_fingerprint(prompt)` — a sha256 of the assembled user prompt only. That correctly covers every Game fact the summary can restate (the prompt IS the facts), but it does not include `model` or `_SYSTEM`. If DEFAULT_MODEL is bumped (e.g. off claude-haiku-4-5 when it is deprecated) or the system instruction is reworded (tone, length, the 'no move numbers' rule), every previously summarized Game keeps hitting the cache and is never regenerated under the new model/instructions — only Games whose facts changed pick up the new behavior, giving a permanently mixed-style corpus.
Why it matters
A model upgrade or prompt fix silently applies only to new/changed Games; the visible summaries stay inconsistent with no signal that anything is stale, and the only remedy is knowing to hand-delete analysis_cache.json.
How to fix
Fold model and the system prompt into the fingerprint, e.g. `hashlib.sha256(f"{model}\n{_SYSTEM}\n{prompt}".encode()).hexdigest()` in summarize (pass model into _fingerprint).
Expected improvement
Bumping the model or editing the system instruction transparently regenerates all summaries on the next Sync; the cache stays truly disposable.
Evidence
prompt = build_prompt(analysis)
    fingerprint = _fingerprint(prompt)
...
def _fingerprint(prompt: str) -> str:
    ...
    return hashlib.sha256(prompt.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
Verifier notes (2)

Confirmed as described: summarize() computes fingerprint = _fingerprint(prompt) at line 122, and _fingerprint (lines 140-146) hashes only the assembled user prompt (sha256 of prompt.encode). Neither `model` (parameter, default DEFAULT_MODEL="claude-haiku-4-5" at line 47) nor `_SYSTEM` (lines 55-62) participates in the cache key, so bumping the model or rewording the system instruction serves stale cached summaries for any Game whose facts (prompt) are unchanged. Cited line ranges are accurate (121-126 for the summarize side; 140-146 for _fingerprint). The proposed fix is sound. Mitigating context, correctly reflected in the low severity: ADR 0004 explicitly documents analysis_cache.json as disposable, so deleting the cache is a sanctioned remedy — the real gap is that nothing signals staleness or invalidates automatically on a model/prompt change. This is not one of the excluded/known items and does not conflict with any documented intentional design (the "cached by Game identity" docstring describes fact-identity, not model/instruction identity).
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/ai_summary.py in full, grepped analysis_cache.py and docs/decisions/0004. The factual claim is exactly right: summarize() keys the cache on _fingerprint(prompt) (lines 121-126), and _fingerprint (lines 140-146) is sha256 of the assembled user prompt only — neither `model` nor `_SYSTEM` participates, and analysis_cache.py stores just {"fp", "text"} per chapter with no version field or model tag, so a DEFAULT_MODEL bump or _SYSTEM rewording never invalidates existing entries. Documented password-hash CLI form puts the plaintext password in shell history and process list

user_config.py:30-32, 119-122 · reviewer: data-handling
What it is
user_config supports two hashing invocations: `python -m user_config hash '<password>'` (argv) and a getpass prompt when the argument is omitted (_hash_cli, lines 187-192). But every place that teaches the operator the command recommends the argv form: the module docstring ('mint one with:: python -m user_config hash 'my password''), the UserConfigError raised for a plaintext password ('Mint one with: python -m user_config hash '<pw>''), and the usage string. A password passed as a shell argument lands in the shell history file and is visible in `ps` output for the duration of the process.
Why it matters
The whole point of the surrounding machinery is that plaintext passwords are never stored ('passwords must be stored as a password_hash', enforced at parse). Steering operators to type the plaintext on the command line quietly persists it in ~/.zsh_history — the same class of leak the parser loudly rejects in config.
How to fix
Flip the documentation: make the docstring, the UserConfigError message, and the usage line recommend the argument-less `python -m user_config hash` (getpass prompt), keeping the argv form as an undocumented convenience or removing it.
Expected improvement
The documented credential-minting path no longer writes plaintext passwords to shell history or exposes them in the process table.
Evidence
user_config.py:31 `python -m user_config hash 'my password'` (docstring); :121 "Mint one with: python -m user_config hash '<pw>'"; :190-191 the safe `getpass.getpass("Password: ")` path already exists

game_detail.py _game_pgn: header values are not PGN-escaped — a quote in an opponent/event name corrupts the generated PGN

pages/game_detail.py:233-256 · reviewer: client-js-lpv-seam
What it is
_game_pgn builds tag pairs with `f'[{k} "{v}"]\n'` and no escaping of the value. The PGN spec requires `\"` for embedded quotes (and `\\` for backslashes) inside a tag value. Opponent names, Event names, and Round strings come straight from Lichess Study chapter data; a value containing a double-quote (e.g. an event named `2025 "Summer" Open` or a nicknamed opponent) produces a malformed tag pair like `[Event "2025 "Summer" Open"]`. The HTML-attribute round-trip itself is safe (Dash/React uses setAttribute, and lpv-init.js reads it back with getAttribute), so the breakage point is the PGN text handed to LichessPgnViewer, which will fail or mis-parse the headers.
Why it matters
One oddly-named event or opponent silently breaks (or degrades) the board for that Game with no error surfaced — and because the same helper feeds data-pgn-game, data-pgn-analysis, and data-pgn-coach, all three board views break together.
How to fix
Escape the value before interpolation: `str(v).replace("\\", "\\\\").replace('"', '\\"')` inside the header join in _game_pgn.
Expected improvement
PGN headers stay well-formed for any name Lichess allows; board rendering no longer depends on players/events avoiding quote characters.
Evidence
head = "".join(f'[{k} "{v}"]\n' for k, v in headers if str(v or "").strip())
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Verified in /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/pages/game_detail.py. Line 255 is exactly the cited evidence: head = "".join(f'[{k} "{v}"]\n' for k, v in headers if str(v or "").strip()) — no escaping of embedded quotes or backslashes. Header values at lines 247-254 include Event, Round, and Opponent (via White/Black at 244-246), all sourced from Lichess Study chapter data, so a double-quote in any of them yields a malformed tag pair per the PGN spec (which requires \" and \\ inside tag values). The helper feeds all three viewer payloads as claimed: data-pgn-game (line 402), data-pgn-analysis (416), data-pgn-coach (437), and assets/lpv-init.js reads them back via getAttribute (lines 75-77), so the HTML round-trip is safe and the breakage point is indeed the PGN handed to lichess-pgn-viewer. Cited line range 233-256 is correct. Not covered by excluded issues/PRs (checked: PRs #82-#86 were docs/cleanup; this is a data-handling bug, not visual polish). Severity low is appropriate: requires an unusually named event/opponent, and failure degrades one Game's board views rather than the app. Suggested fix (escape backslash then quote before interpolation) is correct; escaping only in _game_pgn is the right place since it is the only tag-pair builder.

Store and UserRecord dataclass reprs embed secrets (lichess_token, password_hash, anthropic_api_key)

data.py:115-132 · reviewer: multiuser-tenant-isolation
What it is
Store is a @dataclass whose auto-generated repr includes `token`, `anthropic_api_key`, and `uscf_member_id`; only `sync_lock` was marked `field(..., repr=False)`, showing repr content was considered but the secret fields were left in. UserRecord (user_config.py:53-62) likewise includes `password_hash` and `lichess_token` in its frozen-dataclass repr. I verified no current log statement prints either object (the only user-adjacent logs are data.py:234 and data.py:538, which log counts and usernames), and UserConfigError messages carry only the username/field name — so this is latent, not an active leak.
Why it matters
Any future `logger.debug("store=%r", store)`, an f-string in an error message, a pytest assertion diff on a UserRecord, or an exception-reporting tool that reprs locals will dump a live Lichess API token and scrypt password hash into logs/transcripts. How to fix
Mark the secret fields `field(repr=False)` on Store (`token`, `anthropic_api_key`) and UserRecord (`password_hash`, `lichess_token`), mirroring what was already done for `sync_lock`.
Expected improvement
Accidentally repr-ing a store or user record in a log line or traceback can no longer disclose credentials.
Evidence

Error handling & robustness (8)

highConfirmedverifier suggests: medium backend/http-clients effort: small

uscf_client._get_json lets non-JSON 200 bodies and mid-body transport errors escape the typed UscfError contract, breaking sync_uscf's never-raises guarantee

uscf_client.py:229-244 · reviewer: http-clients
What it is
_get_json only converts requests.Timeout and requests.ConnectionError into UscfUnreachableError. Two other realistic failure classes escape as raw requests exceptions: (1) a 200 response whose body is not JSON — `return response.json()` raises requests.JSONDecodeError, which subclasses RequestException/ValueError, not UscfError; the API is Cloudflare-fronted and undocumented, so a 200 HTML interstitial or maintenance page is plausible; (2) a connection dropped mid-body (requests.exceptions.ChunkedEncodingError) or ContentDecodingError, which subclass RequestException but not ConnectionError, raised inside `requests.get(...)` while it downloads the body. sync.py's sync_uscf catches only `except UscfError` (sync.py:389) and its docstring promises "Never raises: USCF data is enrichment, never a dependency (ADR 0003)". Any of these exceptions blows straight through sync_uscf, then through data.py's refresh (which catches only `(SyncError, RuntimeError)`, data.py:537) and app.py:191/250, crashing the whole Sync.
Why it matters
This is a direct violation of ADR 0003's core invariant: a USCF hiccup (Cloudflare serving a 200 HTML page, or a reset connection mid-download) takes down the entire Sync — Lichess games included — instead of degrading to the cached USCF snapshot that _uscf_from_cache was built for. Over months of daily syncs against an unofficial API this failure mode is likely, and the degraded path already exists but is unreachable for these exception types.
How to fix
In _get_json, broaden the transport catch to `except requests.RequestException as exc: raise UscfUnreachableError(...)` (Timeout/ConnectionError are subclasses, so message specialization can stay), and wrap `response.json()` in try/except (requests.JSONDecodeError or ValueError) raising `UscfError(f"USCF returned a non-JSON body for {what}.")`.
Expected improvement
sync_uscf's documented never-raises contract holds for every transport/body failure; USCF outages of any shape degrade to the cache instead of crashing the Sync.
Evidence
except (requests.Timeout, requests.ConnectionError) as exc:
    raise UscfUnreachableError(...)
...
return response.json()  # requests.JSONDecodeError is not a UscfError

sync.py:389: except UscfError as exc:  # docstring: "Never raises" (ADR 0003)
Verifier notes (2)

All cited evidence is real and current: (1) _get_json (uscf_client.py:229-244) catches only (requests.Timeout, requests.ConnectionError) at line 233 and calls `return response.json()` unguarded at line 244 — requests.JSONDecodeError (subclass of ValueError/RequestException, not UscfError) escapes on a 200 non-JSON body; ChunkedEncodingError/ContentDecodingError (RequestException subclasses, not ConnectionError) raised while requests.get downloads the body also escape. (2) sync_uscf's docstring at sync.py:374 says "Never raises: USCF data is enrichment, never a dependency (ADR 0003)" and the guard at sync.py:389 is `except UscfError` only; the cache-fallback path _uscf_from_cache exists but is unreachable for these exception types. (3) Upstream catches are `except (SyncError, RuntimeError)` at data.py:537 and app.py:191/250 — no ValueError/RequestException handling anywhere on the path, so the exception crashes the whole Sync including the Lichess portion, directly violating ADR 0003. No corrections needed: line numbers, exception-hierarchy claims, and the proposed fix (broaden to requests.RequestException, wrap response.json()) are all accurate. That is still an ADR 0003 violation (a USCF hiccup fails the entire Sync, fresh Lichess data included, instead of degrading to the USCF cache), but it is recoverable via retry, not a crash. lichess_client.fetch_study_pgn maps only Timeout/ConnectionError to LichessError, so mid-download failures defeat sync_studies' per-Study isolation

lichess_client.py:72-82 · reviewer: http-clients
What it is
The try block around `requests.get(...)` catches only `(requests.Timeout, requests.ConnectionError)`. Since the call is not streamed, the full PGN body (potentially large — every Chapter of a Study) is downloaded inside `requests.get`, and a connection reset mid-body raises requests.exceptions.ChunkedEncodingError; TooManyRedirects and ContentDecodingError are other RequestException subclasses that escape untyped. sync.py's sync_studies loop (sync.py:130-134) and sync_coach (sync.py:578-583) catch only `except LichessError`, whose whole purpose is one-Study-fails-others-survive; an escaping raw requests exception aborts the entire loop, skips the SyncError/partial-result machinery, and propagates past data.py's `except (SyncError, RuntimeError)` (data.py:537) into the Dash callback.
Why it matters
The module's docstring claims LichessError is "Base class for anything that goes wrong talking to Lichess", and sync.py's per-Study degrade design ("One Study failing never loses the Games of the Studies that succeeded") depends on that being true. A single flaky download of one Study crashes the whole Sync — including the offline PGN-cache fallback path in data.py that only engages on SyncError.
How to fix
Broaden the catch to `except requests.RequestException as exc: raise LichessUnreachableError(...)` — Timeout and ConnectionError are subclasses, so the single clause covers all transport failures while preserving the current message.
Expected improvement
Any transport failure on one Study degrades to a per-Study failure entry (or a clean SyncError → cache fallback when all fail) instead of an unhandled exception in the callback.
Evidence
except (requests.Timeout, requests.ConnectionError) as exc:
    raise LichessUnreachableError(
        f"Could not reach Lichess to fetch Study {study_id!r}: {exc}"
    ) from exc

sync.py:132: except LichessError as exc:  # per-Study isolation depends on this

mediumConfirmedverifier suggests: low backend/http-clients effort: small

No 429 handling or backoff in lichess_client — sync_studies keeps hammering Lichess after being rate-limited

lichess_client.py:89-92 · reviewer: http-clients
What it is
A 429 from Lichess falls into the generic `if response.status_code != 200: raise LichessError(...)` branch with no special handling: no Retry-After/60-second wait, no retry, and no signal to the caller to stop. sync_studies (sync.py:129-134) and sync_coach (sync.py:578-583) then treat it as a routine per-Study failure and immediately fire the next `fetch_study_pgn` in the loop, so once Lichess rate-limits the client, every remaining designated Study is requested back-to-back into the same rate-limit window — the exact behavior Lichess's API guidelines say to avoid (they ask clients to wait a full minute after a 429 and may throttle or block tokens that don't).
Why it matters
Besides losing all remaining Studies of that Sync (each 429s in turn, and if all fail the Sync falls back to cache), continuing to send requests after a 429 risks Lichess throttling or banning the API token, which would break the source-of-truth path (ADR 0001) far longer than one Sync.
How to fix
In fetch_study_pgn, detect status 429 and either (a) sleep min(Retry-After, 60s) once and retry the single request, or (b) raise a distinct `LichessRateLimitedError(LichessError)` that sync_studies/sync_coach catch to abort the remaining loop iterations immediately (marking the rest as rate-limited failures) instead of continuing to hit the API.
Expected improvement
A rate-limited Sync either recovers within one Sync (retry after the cooldown) or stops politely, protecting the token and turning an all-Studies failure into at most a partial one.
Evidence
if response.status_code != 200:
    raise LichessError(
        f"Lichess returned HTTP {response.status_code} for Study {study_id!r}."
    )

Token-ban risk from a few bounded requests per manual Sync is remote. sync_coach: a partial fetch overwrites the full coach cache and drops the unreachable Study's Chapters from the current result

sync.py:576-593 · reviewer: coach-review-matching
What it is
sync_coach fetches each configured coach Study independently and collects failures, but the success path fires whenever `pgn_texts` is non-empty: it joins ONLY the Studies that fetched, writes that partial merge over the single shared cache file (`_write_cache(cache_path, merged)`), and matches against it. Two consequences when one of two coach Studies is down: (1) that Study's Chapters disappear from this Sync's coach content even though the previous Sync's cache still holds them — the cached-fallback branch (lines 595-608) only runs when EVERY Study failed; (2) the cache is permanently shrunk to the partial content, so a later total outage falls back to a cache that is missing a whole Study. The docstring's promise that 'coach content survives a brief outage' only holds for full outages.
Why it matters
With multiple coach Studies configured (the parameter is a list, and the merge logic exists precisely for that case), a routine single-Study hiccup silently loses part of the coach content twice over: now, and again on the next full outage via the degraded cache. The USCF cache lifecycle this mirrors (ADR 0003) never destroys good cached data on a partial failure.
How to fix
Cache per Study (e.g. coach-<study_id>.pgn) and, on a per-Study fetch failure, substitute that Study's cached PGN into the merge before matching; only record `from_cache=True` granularity as needed. Alternatively, keep one cache file but merge the cached text for the failed Studies' Chapters (parseable by ChapterURL prefix) before overwriting.
Expected improvement
A single unreachable coach Study degrades to that Study's cached content instead of deleting it from both the current view and the cache.
Evidence
if pgn_texts:
        merged = "\n\n".join(pgn_texts)
        if cache_path:
            _write_cache(cache_path, merged)
        return CoachSyncResult(
            result=match_coach_study(games_df, merged), ...
Verifier notes (2)
