The cached-fallback branch (595-608) is reachable only when pgn_texts is empty, i.e. every configured Study failed. So with 2 coach Studies and 1 down: that Study's Chapters vanish from this Sync even though the cache held them, and the cache is shrunk to the partial content, degrading a future full-outage fallback. Multi-Study configs are real: coach_study_ids is a list plumbed from user config (data.py:116, 241, 331, 511). One correction to the finding's framing: the docstring (566-569) actually says "if EVERY coach Study is unreachable, the cached coach PGN is used" — so the code matches its own docstring; only the looser summary phrase "coach content survives a brief outage" is overstated, not broken. The behavior is still a genuine partial-failure data-loss gap (contrast with ADR 0003's spirit of enrichment degrading gracefully), not an already-fixed or excluded item (not covered by #80/#40/PRs 82-86). Cited line range 576-593 is slightly narrow — the fallback branch is 595-608 — but the evidence snippet is verbatim from the current file. Proposed fix (per-Study cache files, or merging cached text for failed Studies) is sound; per-Study files (coach-<study_id>.pgn) is the cleaner option. Medium severity seems right: silent partial content loss, but enrichment-only and self-heals on the next fully-successful fetch.

Nuance the finding overstates slightly: the damage is self-healing (next successful fetch of the failed Study fully restores content and cache) and coach data is enrichment-only, so low would also be defensible; keeping medium since it silently violates a documented invariant and degrades the cache for future full outages. Proposed per-Study-cache fix is sound and fits the existing atomic _write_cache pattern.

lpv-init.js: failed viewer import is silent and cached forever — dead blank board with no fallback

assets/lpv-init.js:30-37, 48-65 · reviewer: client-js-lpv-seam
What it is
loadLpv() memoizes the dynamic import promise: `lpvPromise = import("/assets/lichess-pgn-viewer.min.js").then(...)`. If the import rejects (asset missing after a bad deploy, network hiccup on first paint, CSP blocking module scripts), the rejected promise is cached in lpvPromise for the lifetime of the page, so every later view switch reuses the failure and never retries. renderBoard() chains `.then(function (LichessPgnViewer) {...})` with no `.catch()` anywhere, so the only symptom is an unhandled-rejection console error; the `.lpv` mount div stays empty with no user-visible message, and the Game / My Analysis / Coach buttons appear to work (they toggle .active) while doing nothing.
Why it matters
The board is the centerpiece of the Game-detail page and this is a resume-showcase app: a reviewer on a flaky connection or a deploy that drops the vendored asset gets a permanently blank card with zero explanation, and even recovering connectivity doesn't fix it without a full reload because the rejection is memoized.
How to fix
Add a `.catch` in renderBoard (or on lpvPromise) that (a) resets `lpvPromise = null` so the next interaction retries the import, and (b) writes a small fallback into the mount, e.g. mount.textContent = "Board failed to load — open this game on Lichess instead." (the Open-on-Lichess button already exists alongside).
Expected improvement
Transient load failures self-heal on the next click, and permanent ones show an explanatory message instead of a silent dead board.
Evidence
lpvPromise = import("/assets/lichess-pgn-viewer.min.js").then(function (m) {
  return m.default;
});  ...  loadLpv().then(function (LichessPgnViewer) { ... });  // no .catch anywhere in the file

load_games_from_text never inspects game.errors — a malformed chapter is silently truncated into a plausible-looking row

pgn_stats_core.py:385-441 · reviewer: pgn-parse-lesson-tag-extraction
What it is
The parse loop only guards against `chess.pgn.read_game` returning None (line 385-387), which python-chess uses to signal end-of-stream. A chapter with a corrupt movetext (illegal SAN, mangled token) does NOT return None: python-chess's GameBuilder catches the exception, appends it to `game.errors`, logs at ERROR level, and skips the rest of that variation — so the loop receives a partially-parsed game and builds a normal row from it. Plies/FullMoves/Moves/Movetext are silently truncated at the bad token; extract_lessons_and_tags misses every comment after the truncation point. Nothing in the module (grep confirms zero references to `.errors` on the game object) checks or surfaces this. One bad chapter neither drops nor kills the Sync — good — but it produces a wrong row that looks valid.
Why it matters
ADR 0001's posture is that data problems surface (in Reconciliation) rather than being silently corrected or hidden. A truncated game skews game-length stats, repertoire-tree depth, and can drop a Lesson written on move 35 of a chapter whose move 20 got mangled — with no signal anywhere in the UI or the sync log that the row is partial.
How to fix
After read_game, check `game.errors`; when non-empty, log the chapter name/URL at WARNING with the error list, and consider carrying a ParseErrors/Partial flag on the row so Reconciliation (or at least the sync summary) can surface it.
Expected improvement
Corrupted chapters become visible instead of quietly contaminating stats; debugging a 'missing Lesson' report becomes a log lookup instead of a parser archaeology session.
Evidence
game = chess.pgn.read_game(f)
if game is None:
    break
idx += 1
h = _norm_headers(game.headers)

UscfCache/AnalysisCache only validate the top-level JSON type; wrong-typed nested sections raise AttributeError, breaking sync_uscf's never-raises contract

sync.py:193-195, 308-314 · reviewer: sync-store
What it is
Both disposable caches promise that "every filesystem misfortune ... degrades to 'no cache', never to an error", but _read() only checks `isinstance(data, dict)` at the top level. Every accessor then assumes nested types: UscfCache.get_current does `self._data.get("current", {}).get(key)` — a cache file like {"current": []} (truncation repaired by hand, or a partial hand edit of this gitignored-but-user-visible JSON) raises AttributeError; dismissals() does `list(self._data.get("dismissals", []))` which raises TypeError on an int; AnalysisCache.get_summary has the identical pattern (`self._data.get("summaries", {}).get(chapter_url)`, analysis_cache.py:56). sync_uscf catches only UscfError, so an AttributeError from _uscf_from_cache propagates out of the function documented "Never raises" — up through _sync_uscf_into_store it either crashes initialize() at startup (app exits) or trips refresh()'s blanket handler after _swap, triggering the half-updated-store failure mode described in the atomic-swap finding.
Why it matters
A cache that exists precisely to make corruption harmless can instead take down startup or degrade a Sync, and the corruption class (right top-level type, wrong nested type) is exactly what a truncated/hand-touched JSON file produces. The blast radius is small but the contract violation feeds the more serious half-swap bug.
How to fix
Validate shape in _read (drop any of "current"/"immutable"/"aged"/"summaries" that is not a dict and "dismissals"/"seen_achievements" that is not a list), or wrap each accessor's lookup in an isinstance check the way get_aged already does (`entry.get("value") if isinstance(entry, dict) else None`).
Expected improvement
Any malformed cache file degrades to empty-cache with a warning, as both modules' docstrings already promise.
Evidence
sync.py get_current: "return self._data.get(\"current\", {}).get(key)"; _read: "return data if isinstance(data, dict) else {}"; sync_uscf docstring: "Never raises: USCF data is enrichment" but only "except UscfError as exc:" is caught; analysis_cache.py:56: "entry = self._data.get(\"summaries\", {}).get(chapter_url)"
Verifier notes (2)

ai_summary has no backoff on Anthropic 429/overload, so one rate-limit turns the rest of a batch into empty summaries for that Sync

ai_summary.py:157-172 · reviewer: http-clients
What it is
_call_anthropic does a single POST and `response.raise_for_status()`; summarize's `except Exception` correctly degrades any failure to "" per ADR 0004. But data.py calls summarize per Game in a loop (data.py:347), and a 429 or 529 (overloaded) from the API is not retried and not distinguished from permanent failures — every subsequent un-cached Game in that Sync immediately fires another request into the same rate-limit window and also degrades to "". The summaries are only recovered on the next full Sync (cache misses re-bill nothing extra since failures aren't cached, so correctness holds).
Why it matters
For a first Sync over many analyzed Games (the exact case where summaries are all uncached), a single rate-limit spike silently blanks most AI summaries for the session and wastes a request per remaining Game. It is within the letter of ADR 0004 but a cheap robustness win.
How to fix
In _call_anthropic, on status 429/529 sleep per the Retry-After header (bounded, e.g. once) before one retry; alternatively let summarize raise a distinguishable RateLimited signal that the data.py loop uses to stop attempting further summaries this Sync.
Expected improvement
Transient Anthropic rate limits cost one delayed request instead of blanking every remaining Game's summary until the next Sync.
Evidence
response.raise_for_status()
...
except Exception as exc:  # any failure degrades to "" — never a dependency
    logger.warning("AI summary unavailable for %s (degrading): %s", ...)
    return ""

The suggested fix (bounded Retry-After sleep on 429/529, or a distinguishable RateLimited signal to stop the loop) is proportionate; the loop-stop variant is the cheaper of the two since it avoids sleeping inside a Sync.

apply_rating_lens recomputes Sync-time-invariant lens bases via iterrows on every chart callback

uscf_core.py:1276-1315 · reviewer: perf-datapath
What it is
Every filter-driven callback calls filters.get_filtered(), which ends in uscf_core.apply_rating_lens(). That function copies the filtered frame (`out = df.copy()`), rebuilds three lookup dicts from scratch — `live_by_section`, `records_by_url`, and (under the Live lens) `opponent_pre`, a flat dict built by iterating every StandingEntry of every cached crosstable — and then runs a Python `for _, game in out.iterrows()` loop that computes `_official_basis` (a linear scan of the official series) and `_live_basis` per row. The per-Game basis values depend only on the Game's matched record, its date, and the USCF series — none of which change between Syncs — yet they are recomputed for every callback. The Trends page registers 11 callbacks on FILTER_INPUTS (pages/trends.py lines 234-629), plus filters.update_filter_summary (filters.py:290-305), so one filter tweak triggers ~12 sequential executions of this loop on the app's single Gunicorn worker (single worker is by design, so the callbacks queue rather than parallelize). The code even contains a comment acknowledging the pressure ('get_filtered runs this for every filter-driven callback, so per-row dict rebuilding multiplies fast', uscf_core.py:1278-1279) but still rebuilds the dicts and iterates rows each call.
Why it matters
With a few hundred Games, iterrows over a wide mixed-dtype frame costs on the order of 50-100 ms per call; multiplied by ~12 queued callbacks per interaction on one worker, each filter or lens change on the Trends page burns roughly 0.5-1 s of serial server CPU before any figure is even built. This is the single hottest repeated cost in the interaction path and it grows linearly with both game count and standings size.
How to fix
Compute the lens bases once per Sync instead of once per callback: in data._sync_uscf_into_store (after enrich_games), attach `OfficialBasisNum`, `LiveBasisNum`, and `OpponentLiveBasisNum` columns using the same _official_basis/_live_basis logic, then reduce apply_rating_lens to a vectorized column selection (`out['PlayerRatingNum'] = out['LiveBasisNum'].fillna(out['OfficialBasisNum'])` style, plus the string display columns). Alternatively (smaller change), memoize get_filtered with functools.lru_cache keyed by the filter-value tuple, lens, and a per-store sync generation counter, so the 12 callbacks of one interaction share a single computation; invalidate on _swap.
Expected improvement
Filter/lens interactions on multi-chart pages drop from ~0.5-1 s of serial per-row Python work to a few milliseconds of vectorized column ops (or a single computation shared by all callbacks), and the cost stops growing with standings size.
Evidence
uscf_core.py:1289-1299: `for _, game in out.iterrows():\n        record = records_by_url.get(game["ChapterURL"])\n        official_value = _official_basis(record, game, official_series)` — preceded by `opponent_pre = { (event_id, section_name, entry.member_id): entry.pre_rating ... for entry in entries } if lens == LIVE_LENS else {}` rebuilt per call; filters.py:63-85 shows every callback funnels through this via get_filtered.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read uscf_core.py:1241-1402, filters.py:40-110 and 285-310, and grepped pages/trends.py. All cited code is real and current: apply_rating_lens copies the frame, rebuilds live_by_section/records_by_url/opponent_pre per call, and runs iterrows with a per-row linear scan of official_series (_supplement_in_effect); the quoted comment is verbatim at uscf_core.py:1278-1279; get_filtered ends in apply_rating_lens (filters.py:78-85). Corrections: trends.py has 10 FILTER_INPUTS callbacks (the 11 count included the import line), so ~11 executions per interaction with update_filter_summary, not ~12. Impact overstated: dataset is ~63 games (demo) and iterrows at a few hundred rows costs ~5-20 ms per call, not 50-100 ms, so an interaction costs tens-to-~200 ms serial CPU, not 0.5-1 s. Proposed Sync-time precompute fix is sound and consistent with ADRs 0003/0006 and the lens-only-in-get_filtered rule. Not a duplicate of excluded issues/PRs. Real inefficiency, but low severity at actual data scale.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/uscf_core.py:1241-1402, filters.py (whole file), grepped pages/trends.py, data.py, and counted the real dataset. Mechanics CONFIRMED: apply_rating_lens (uscf_core.py:1276-1316) does df.copy(), rebuilds live_by_section/records_by_url/opponent_pre per call, and runs iterrows with _official_basis doing a linear scan of official_series per row (uscf_core.py:1361-1391). filters.get_filtered (filters.py:78-85) funnels every filter-driven callback through it, and trends.py has 10 FILTER_INPUTS chart callbacks (not 11: lines 234, 355, 379, 409, 429, 452, 480, 564, 587, 621) plus update_filter_summary = ~11 per interaction on the single worker. However, the IMPACT is materially overstated: games.pgn contains exactly 63 games, official_series is monthly supplements (tens of points), and standings are a handful of small crosstables. I benchmarked iterrows on a 40-column mixed-dtype frame: ~1.0 ms at 63 rows, ~3.8 ms at 300 rows — so apply_rating_lens costs low-single-digit ms per call, and one interaction burns tens of ms total, not the claimed 50-100 ms/call and 0.5-1 s/interaction (off by ~10-20x). Figure construction and network round-trips dominate the interaction path, not this loop. This is a personal dashboard / resume showcase whose data grows by a few games per month, so the linear-growth concern is decades away from mattering. The precompute-at-Sync fix is sound in principle (bases are Sync-invariant); the alternative lru_cache fix as written would fail — filter values arrive as lists (unhashable), so it needs tuple normalization. Downgrade to low: real redundant work, honestly acknowledged in the code's own comment, but not a user-perceivable cost at any realistic scale for this app.

Eager per-user Sync at module import blocks Gunicorn worker boot for the whole multi-user roster

app.py:89-93, 176-190 · reviewer: multiuser-tenant-isolation
What it is
In multi-user mode build_app() runs `for username in users: data.sync_user(username)` serially, and build_app is invoked at module import time (`_app, server = build_app(...)` at app.py:180) — i.e. inside Gunicorn's worker boot, before it can serve /health. Each sync_user does a full pipeline per user: Lichess Study export, USCF scrape of ratings.uschess.org, engine-analysis enrichment, and one Anthropic Haiku call per not-yet-cached analyzed Game (_summaries_for, data.py:336-350). The lazy path exists (ensure_synced in the before_request hook, app.py:152) but never fires because sync_user marks initialized=True first.
Why it matters
Boot time grows linearly with users and with un-cached AI summaries; a fresh deploy (empty analysis_cache.json) with a handful of users can take minutes of external HTTP inside worker startup. Gunicorn kills workers that exceed its boot timeout (default 30s), and Fly.io health checks fail the deploy — with exactly one worker by design (ADR 0006), a slow third-party (USCF scrape or Anthropic) turns into a failed release. There is no concurrency bug here (it runs before any request), purely a boot-availability risk that gets worse with each added user.
How to fix
Pick one: (a) drop the eager loop and rely on the already-implemented ensure_synced lazy path (first request per user pays the Sync, everyone else is unaffected); (b) keep eager Sync but run it on a background thread post-bind so /health answers immediately (activate() is not needed there since sync_user takes the store by name, not via the thread-local); or (c) at minimum document/raise the Gunicorn --timeout in fly.toml to cover worst-case roster boot.
Expected improvement
Deploys stop being hostage to N users x (Lichess + USCF + Anthropic) latency inside worker boot; /health responds as soon as the worker binds.
Evidence
app.py:92-93 `for username in users:\n            data.sync_user(username)` inside build_app, which runs at module scope: app.py:180 `_app, server = build_app(`; per-game AI calls during that Sync: data.py:346-349 `ai_summary.summarize(analysis, api_key=store.anthropic_api_key, cache=cache)`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/app.py, data.py (lines 215-400, 520-554), gunicorn.conf.py, fly.toml. Core mechanics confirmed: app.py:92-93 runs `for username in users: data.sync_user(username)` serially inside build_app, and build_app is called at module scope (app.py:178, within the cited 176-190) — i.e. during Gunicorn worker boot, before the /health route (registered at app.py:130) can answer. Each sync goes through data.py _sync_store (Lichess export, USCF scrape, analysis enrichment) and _summaries_for at data.py:336-350 makes one ai_summary.summarize call per un-cached analyzed Game (evidence line 347, finding cited 346-349 — accurate). The lazy path claim also checks out, and is even slightly stronger than stated: _sync_store sets store.initialized = True at data.py:258 BEFORE syncing, so ensure_synced (data.py:541-546, wired at app.py:152) never fires after the eager loop — and never retries even if the eager sync failed (sync_user catches SyncError at data.py:535-538 and serves an empty store). Two corrections that reduce practical severity: (1) Gunicorn's timeout is NOT the 30s default — gunicorn.conf.py:19 sets timeout = 120, so the finding's proposed fix (c) is already half done; a worker only dies if the whole roster boot exceeds 120s (plausible on a fresh deploy with several users and a cold analysis cache, but not "default 30s"). (2) fly.toml defines no USERS — its comment says multi-user per-user caches apply "if ever enabled" — so the multi-user eager-boot path is latent, not active in the current single-user Fly deployment (single-user boot also syncs eagerly at import, but that is one sync, not a linear roster). The code path and the boot-availability risk are real as described, but with timeout=120 already configured and multi-user not deployed, medium overstates it; suggest low. Not a duplicate of issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read app.py (full), data.py:215-269/336-350/480-559, gunicorn.conf.py, fly.toml. Mechanism confirmed: serial per-user sync_user loop at app.py:92-93 runs at module import (app.py:176-190) inside Gunicorn worker boot, with one Anthropic call per uncached analyzed Game (data.py:346-349); _sync_store sets initialized=True first (data.py:258), so ensure_synced (app.py:152) never fires after eager boot, even on failure — the lazy-path-is-dead claim is accurate. Corrections that deflate severity: (1) gunicorn.conf.py:19 already sets timeout=120, not the default 30s the finding assumes — fix (c) is essentially already applied; (2) fly.toml mounts a persistent volume at /data for CACHE_PATH/ANALYSIS_CACHE_PATH/DATA_DIR, so the "fresh deploy with empty analysis cache" scenario applies only to the first-ever deploy, not every release; (3) the shipped fly.toml is single-user (no USERS configured — multi-user is "if ever enabled"), so the linear-in-roster loop is not exercised in the actual deployment; (4) eager Sync is a documented deliberate choice (data.py register_users docstring: "eagerly at build, or lazily on first access"; build_app comment), not an accidental bug; (5) sync_user swallows SyncError, so failing upstreams degrade fast — only slow upstreams block. Residual risk is real (first multi-user deploy with many uncached analyzed games can exceed 120s and boot grows linearly with users), so exists=true, but as a latent boot-availability risk in a currently-undeployed mode: low, not medium. Proposed fixes (a)/(b) are technically sound; (a) conflicts with the documented eager-boot intent and would make the first request per user slow instead.

apply_filters makes an unconditional full-frame copy before masking, doubling per-callback copies

pgn_stats_core.py:516-539 · reviewer: perf-datapath
What it is
apply_filters starts with `out = df.copy()` and then applies up to 8 sequential boolean-index operations (`out = out[out["Color"].isin(colors)]` etc.), each of which already materializes a new DataFrame. The upfront copy is redundant: boolean indexing never mutates the source, so the store frame is never at risk. In the common default state (all filters at 'everything'), the function copies the entire frame just to hand it to apply_rating_lens, which immediately copies it again (uscf_core.py:1276) — two full copies of the store frame per callback, times ~12 callbacks per interaction on the Trends page.
Why it matters
The frame carries wide object columns (Analysis GameAnalysis objects, Tags lists, TagSources dicts, Summary strings), so each copy is not free; the redundant copy plus the chain of intermediate frames adds fixed overhead to every one of the ~12 callbacks a single filter interaction fires. Small individually, but it sits on the hottest path in the app and compounds with the apply_rating_lens copy.
How to fix
Drop the initial `out = df.copy()` and instead accumulate one combined boolean mask (start with `mask = pd.Series(True, index=df.index)`, AND in each active condition) and index once at the end: `return df[mask]`. This yields exactly one materialized result frame per call, and zero-cost passthrough logic can return df itself when no filter is active (callers already treat results as immutable per pages/AGENTS.md).
Expected improvement
One full-frame copy and up to 7 intermediate frame materializations eliminated per callback; with 12 callbacks per interaction this removes the majority of redundant allocation on the filter hot path.
Evidence
pgn_stats_core.py:516-518: `out = df.copy()\n    if colors:\n        out = out[out["Color"].isin(colors)]` — followed by seven more `out = out[...]` re-materializations.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/pgn_stats_core.py:498-539, /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/uscf_core.py:1273-1287, and /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/filters.py:27-78. All cited evidence is real and current: apply_filters opens with `out = df.copy()` at line 516, followed by eight sequential `out = out[...]` boolean-index re-materializations (517-538), and filters.get_filtered (line 67) hands the result straight to apply_rating_lens (line 78), which copies again at uscf_core.py:1276. FILTER_INPUTS-driven callbacks per page are plentiful (trends.py alone has at least 4 visible in a partial grep; the ~12 figure is plausible but I did not count exhaustively — treat it as approximate). Two corrections/nuances: (1) the double-copy only occurs when USCF data exists — apply_rating_lens returns df unchanged at 1273-1274 when both rating series are empty (ADR 0003 no-USCF path), so in that degraded mode there is exactly one copy, not two; (2) the docstring says "return a filtered copy", so the upfront copy looks deliberate as a defensive-immutability guarantee — the proposed mask-based fix is sound (pages/AGENTS.md mandates treating DataFrames as immutable, and boolean indexing already yields new frames) but should also update that docstring wording. Not covered by excluded issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86. Severity low is right: fixed overhead on the hottest path, no correctness impact.

Facts confirmed: apply_filters does `out = df.copy()` at line 516 and then up to ~10 boolean-index re-materializations (lines 517-538); each `out = out[...]` already produces a new frame, so the upfront copy is redundant whenever any filter is active. get_filtered then hands the result to apply_rating_lens, which copies again at uscf_core.py:1276 before writing rating columns (that second copy IS necessary — it mutates). Corrections/context tempering impact: the dataset is a personal OTB game archive (likely hundreds of rows, not tens of thousands), and apply_rating_lens's per-row iterrows() loop (uscf_core.py:1291) almost certainly dominates the copy cost on the same hot path — so the wall-clock win is small. Also the docstring says "return a filtered copy", so the fix should update that one line. Real but marginal; low severity is the ceiling — arguably info-grade given data size.

USCF name-fallback pass renormalizes every record name once per candidate chapter (O(chapters x records) regex work)

uscf_core.py:1038-1050 · reviewer: perf-datapath
What it is
_name_pass loops `for _, game in df.iterrows()` over every unmatched chapter and, inside that, `for i, record in enumerate(records)` over every record, calling _names_match for each pair. _names_match (uscf_core.py:1069-1070) calls _normalize_name on BOTH names, and _normalize_name runs `re.sub(r"[^\w\s]", "", name.lower())` plus a split/join. So each record's opponent name is regex-normalized once per unmatched chapter, and each chapter's opponent name once per record — O(C x R) regex passes when C x R pairs exist, at Sync time.
Why it matters
This is Sync-path only, so it never blocks a chart callback, but at a few hundred chapters times a few hundred career game records the pass performs on the order of 10^5 redundant regex substitutions per Sync (and per multi-user boot Sync), adding avoidable hundreds of milliseconds to a path the user watches a spinner for. It also grows quadratically as the archive grows.
How to fix
Precompute `normalized_records = [(_normalize_name(r.opponent_name), r) for r in records if r.rating_system in _OTB_RATING_SYSTEMS]` once before the chapter loop, and normalize each chapter's opponent name once per chapter (it is loop-invariant across records). Pass the pre-normalized strings into a comparison helper instead of re-deriving them per pair.
Expected improvement
Name-pass normalization drops from O(C x R) to O(C + R) regex operations — roughly a 100x reduction in regex work for the fallback pass at current scale, shaving a visible slice off each Sync.
Evidence
uscf_core.py:1038-1045: `for _, game in df.iterrows(): ... for i, record in enumerate(records): ... if (_names_match(str(game["Opponent"]), record)`; uscf_core.py:1069-1070: `chapter_name = _normalize_name(chapter_opponent)\n    record_name = _normalize_name(record.opponent_name)` executed per pair.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Verified in /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/uscf_core.py. _name_pass (lines 1038-1050) does nest `for _, game in df.iterrows()` over `for i, record in enumerate(records)` and calls _names_match per pair (line 1045); _names_match (lines 1069-1070) calls _normalize_name on both names each call, and _normalize_name (line 1084) runs `re.sub(r"[^\w\s]", "", name.lower())` per invocation. So the O(C x R) redundant normalization exists exactly as cited, and the proposed precompute fix is valid (note the chapter loop already filters early via `continue` on line 1040-1041, so the chapter name could also be normalized once per chapter after those guards). Corrections to impact scope: (1) the inner loop only runs for chapters that survive line 1040's filter — no ChapterURL, already matched by the id pass, or having an opponent id all skip it — and only over records not in `used` and in _OTB_RATING_SYSTEMS (line 1043 continue), so C and R are the residual unmatched subsets after the primary id pass, typically far smaller than total chapters x total career records; the ~10^5-regex / "hundreds of milliseconds" estimate assumes the id pass largely failed, which is not the common case. (2) Python's re module caches the compiled pattern, so the per-call cost is a cached-pattern sub plus lower/split/join, not recompilation. Sync-path only, correctness unaffected. Real but very minor; suggest info rather than low, though low is defensible.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/uscf_core.py:1000-1109 and the caller chain (match_games -> _name_pass at uscf_core.py:983; match_games invoked only from data.py:293 inside refresh(), i.e. the Sync path). The code is exactly as described: _name_pass (lines 1038-1050) nests `for i, record in enumerate(records)` inside `for _, game in df.iterrows()`, and _names_match (1069-1070) calls _normalize_name on both names per pair; _normalize_name (1084) runs re.sub + split/join with no lru_cache or precompute anywhere. Both normalizations are loop-redundant: record.opponent_name is invariant across chapters, and the chapter's Opponent is invariant across the inner loop. Line numbers and evidence in the finding are accurate. Corrections/materiality caveats: (1) the outer loop skips chapters already ID-matched or carrying an opponent_id, and the inner loop skips used/non-OTB records, so C and R are the *residuals*, typically much smaller than "few hundred x few hundred" for this single-player dashboard — the "hundreds of milliseconds" estimate is overstated; realistic cost is likely single-digit to tens of ms, invisible next to the USCF HTTP fetches in the same Sync. (2) A cheaper fix also exists: reorder the condition so the O(1) `record.player_outcome == game["Outcome"]` check short-circuits before _names_match, or just @lru_cache _normalize_name — the proposed precompute is also correct and semantics-preserving (_names_match only ever operates on the normalized strings). Quadratic growth is real but Sync-only and never blocks a callback, consistent with ADR 0006's single-store refresh design. Severity low stands (it is the floor of a real finding); do not raise it.

lpv-init.js: app-wide MutationObserver runs an undebounced full-document scan on every DOM mutation on every page

assets/lpv-init.js:131-135 · reviewer: client-js-lpv-seam
What it is
The observer watches `document.documentElement` with `{ childList: true, subtree: true }` and calls scan() -> `document.querySelectorAll(".game-board-card")` on every mutation batch, on every page of the app, forever — it is never disconnected and there is no debounce. Pages full of Plotly graphs (dashboard, trends) generate mutation storms during redraws, hover interactions, and the very `window.dispatchEvent(new Event("resize"))` this file fires at line 105, each triggering a document-wide selector query that can match nothing.
Why it matters
Wasted main-thread work on the nine pages that have no board, scaling with chart interactivity; it is the kind of always-on cost that shows up in a Lighthouse pass of a showcase project even though each individual call is cheap.
How to fix
Debounce scan() behind requestAnimationFrame (coalesce the batch: `if (scheduled) return; scheduled = true; requestAnimationFrame(function () { scheduled = false; scan(); })`), and/or bail out fast by checking mutation targets before querying.
Expected improvement
One scan per frame at most instead of one per mutation batch, eliminating background selector churn on chart-heavy pages.
Evidence
var observer = new MutationObserver(function () {
  scan();
});
observer.observe(document.documentElement, { childList: true, subtree: true });
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read assets/lpv-init.js in full. Lines 131-135 match the evidence exactly: MutationObserver on document.documentElement with {childList:true, subtree:true} calling scan() -> document.querySelectorAll(".game-board-card") with no debounce and never disconnected; line 105 fires the resize event as claimed. Not an intentional design per AGENTS.md/ADRs (the header comment only explains SPA rescanning, doesn't bless the undebounced form) and not covered by excluded issues/PRs. Two wording corrections: the observer fires only on childList (node add/remove) mutations, not literally every DOM mutation (attribute/text changes are unobserved — Plotly hover still adds/removes tooltip nodes, so the claim survives in practice); and each scan is a single cheap class-selector query plus a WeakSet-guarded loop, so per-call cost is tiny. Severity "low" is appropriate; the suggested requestAnimationFrame coalescing fix is correct.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read assets/lpv-init.js in full. Confirmed: observer at lines 132-135 watches document.documentElement {childList:true, subtree:true}, calls scan() -> document.querySelectorAll(".game-board-card") (line 121), never disconnected, no debounce; header comment lines 10-11 acknowledges the rescan-on-every-mutation design. Corrections: (a) MutationObserver already coalesces mutations into per-task batches, so the title's "on every DOM mutation" overstates — it's once per batch, as the description itself says; (b) the resize dispatch at line 105 doesn't mutate the DOM directly, only Plotly's redraw response does. Actual cost is one fast class-selector query per mutation batch (~tens of microseconds), which will not register in a Lighthouse pass — the "why it matters" claim is inflated. Proposed rAF-coalescing fix is correct and safe (initCard is WeakSet-idempotent, one-frame delay is harmless). Real but hygiene-level: suggest downgrading low -> info. Not covered by exclusions #40/#80 or PRs #82-#86.

What it is

sync.py duplicates the multi-Study fetch loop between sync_studies and sync_coach, and re-implements _cache_mtime inline in load_from_cache

sync.py:129-134, 578-583 · reviewer: duplication-deadcode
What it is
Two copies of the same fetch-and-collect-failures loop: sync_studies (sync.py:129-134) `for study_id in study_ids: try: pgn_texts.append(fetch_study_pgn(study_id, token=token)) except LichessError as exc: logger.warning("Could not fetch Study %r: %s", ...); failures.append((study_id, str(exc)))` and sync_coach (sync.py:578-583) with an identical body (only the log prefix says "coach Study"). Both then join with `"\n\n".join(pgn_texts)` and `"; ".join(f"{sid}: {reason}" ...)`. Separately, load_from_cache (sync.py:646) inlines `datetime.fromtimestamp(os.path.getmtime(cache_path), tz=timezone.utc)` although _cache_mtime (sync.py:623-627) exists for exactly that.
Why it matters
The per-Study degrade behavior (one Study failing never loses the others) is a core Sync guarantee; two copies of the loop mean a future change — e.g. retries or a different exception taxonomy — can land in one path and silently miss the coach path. The mtime duplication is a helper that already exists going unused at one of its two natural call sites.
How to fix
Extract `_fetch_studies(study_ids, token) -> tuple[list[str], list[tuple[str, str]]]` and call it from both sync_studies and sync_coach (pass a label for the log message). Replace load_from_cache's inline mtime expression with `_cache_mtime(cache_path)`.
Expected improvement
One implementation of the partial-failure fetch contract; ~10 fewer duplicated lines.
Evidence
sync.py:131 `pgn_texts.append(fetch_study_pgn(study_id, token=token))` / :134 `failures.append((study_id, str(exc)))` duplicated at sync.py:580-583; sync.py:646 `cached_at = datetime.fromtimestamp(os.path.getmtime(cache_path), tz=timezone.utc)` vs _cache_mtime at sync.py:627
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read sync.py lines 120-150 and 560-660. All three claims check out in current code: (1) sync_studies' fetch loop at lines 129-134 and sync_coach's at 578-583 are byte-identical except the log prefix ("Study" vs "coach Study"); both build pgn_texts/failures the same way, both join with "\n\n".join and "; ".join(f"{sid}: ...") (140/137 vs 586/592-596). (2) load_from_cache at line 646 inlines datetime.fromtimestamp(os.path.getmtime(cache_path), tz=timezone.utc) while _cache_mtime (lines 623-627) does exactly that and is used at line 605. Two caveats on scope/fix: the duplicated portion is only the ~6-line loop plus join idioms — the post-loop handling deliberately diverges (sync_studies raises SyncError when all fail; sync_coach never raises and falls back to its cache per ADR 0003), so extraction is limited to _fetch_studies as proposed. And _cache_mtime returns datetime | None while load_from_cache's signature promises a non-None datetime, so the suggested swap needs a cast/assert or signature tweak to stay mypy-clean. Severity low is right; not covered by PRs #82-#86 (verified code is present at HEAD f8d96f1) and not part of excluded issues #40/#80.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed both claims by reading /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/sync.py. (2) load_from_cache at ~646 inlines datetime.fromtimestamp(os.path.getmtime(cache_path), tz=timezone.utc) while _cache_mtime (~623-627) exists. Line numbers in the finding are accurate. Materiality caveats that keep this at low, not moot: (a) both failure paths ARE independently tested (tests/test_sync.py TestPartialFailure asserts per-Study degrade; tests/test_coach_sync.py has a partial-fetch test), so a divergent future change would likely be caught — the "silently miss the coach path" risk is partially mitigated; (b) downstream handling genuinely differs (sync_studies raises SyncError on total failure, sync_coach falls back to cache and never raises), so only the ~6-line loop is extractable, limiting the payoff; (c) the proposed _cache_mtime fix for load_from_cache is slightly off: _cache_mtime returns datetime | None, but load_from_cache's return type is a non-optional datetime (the earlier open() already guarantees the file exists), so the swap needs an assert or type narrowing — the inline expression is arguably deliberate there. The core duplication finding stands; severity low is correct.

events.py formats the start–end date range with the same collapse rule in two places

pages/events.py:95-100, 289-293 · reviewer: duplication-deadcode
What it is
_event_dates (pages/events.py:95-100) renders a Rated Event's window as `start if start == end or not end else f"{start} – {end}"`. _unplayed_card (pages/events.py:289-293) re-implements the identical single-day-collapse rule for UscfEvent's date objects: `event.start_date.isoformat() if event.start_date == event.end_date or not event.end_date else f"{event.start_date} – {event.end_date}"`. Same display rule, two copies in one file, differing only in dict-vs-dataclass input.
Why it matters
The one-date-for-single-day-events rule is a display convention; when it changes (e.g. locale-style dates in the #40 redesign) one of the two copies will be missed, and the played vs. unplayed event cards will format dates differently.
How to fix
Extract one module-level helper, e.g. `_date_range(start: str, end: str) -> str`, and call it from both (converting the dataclass dates with .isoformat() at the call site).
Expected improvement
One date-range formatting rule for the Events page.
Evidence
events.py:100 `return start if start == end or not end else f"{start} – {end}"` vs events.py:291-293 `dates = (event.start_date.isoformat() if event.start_date == event.end_date or not event.end_date else f"{event.start_date} – {event.end_date}")`
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/pages/events.py lines 85-110 and 280-300. Both copies exist exactly as cited: _event_dates (lines 95-100) returns `start if start == end or not end else f"{start} – {end}"` for dict input, and _unplayed_card (lines 289-293) re-implements the same single-day collapse for UscfEvent date objects, including the same empty-start guard (`if not start: return ""` vs `dates = ""` / `if event.start_date:`). Evidence quotes match the current file verbatim. Minor line-cite correction: the second copy spans 289-293 (the finding's header says 289-293 in the description but 289-293 vs "289-293" — the JSON's line field says 289-293 for the second range, which is accurate; the quoted evidence range 291-293 omits the guard at 289-290). One nuance the finding glosses over: the two copies are not byte-identical in output semantics — _event_dates works on already-formatted strings while _unplayed_card f-strings date objects (relying on date.__str__ == isoformat), so a shared `_date_range(start: str, end: str | None) -> str` helper with .isoformat() at the call site (as proposed) is the right fix. Chapter-id extraction from a ChapterURL is implemented independently in components.py and data.py

components.py:351 · reviewer: duplication-deadcode
What it is
The rule for deriving a Game's chapter id from its ChapterURL — strip trailing slash, take the last path segment — exists twice: components.game_detail_path (components.py:351, `f"/game/{chapter_url.rstrip('/').rsplit('/', 1)[-1]}"`) and data.get_coach_notes (data.py:840, `chapter_id = match.chapter_url.rstrip("/").rsplit("/", 1)[-1]`). A third spot depends on the same convention from the other direction: game_detail._find_game matches with `df["ChapterURL"].str.endswith(f"/{chapter_id}")` (pages/game_detail.py:50).
Why it matters
ChapterURL is the permanent Game identity (ADR 0001), and the id-segment convention is what makes deep links (/game/<id>) resolve. With the parsing rule scattered, a URL-shape change (e.g. Lichess adding a trailing path element) would have to be fixed in multiple places or deep links silently break in one path but not another.
How to fix
Add a single `chapter_id(chapter_url: str) -> str` helper (components.py already hosts game_detail_path; or pgn_stats_core if you want it Dash-free) and use it in game_detail_path and data.get_coach_notes.
Expected improvement
One place encodes the ChapterURL→id convention that Game identity and deep-linking rest on.
Evidence
components.py:351 `return f"/game/{chapter_url.rstrip('/').rsplit('/', 1)[-1]}"` vs data.py:840 `chapter_id = match.chapter_url.rstrip("/").rsplit("/", 1)[-1]`
Verifier notes (2)

The parsing rule is genuinely duplicated in two places with a third implicit dependent, as the finding says. Proposed fix (extract _awaiting_hint(what_appears) called from both sites) is correct and harmless. Severity "low" is right: pure maintainability/copy-drift risk, no functional impact today.

Architecture (1)

lowConfirmed frontend effort: small

Four pages guard on DataFrame column presence, violating the columns-always-exist contract

pages/events.py:342 · reviewer: pages-contracts
What it is
pages/AGENTS.md states 'Enrichment columns always exist — never guard on "is USCF configured" by checking for a column'. Four pages check anyway: events.py:342 `if "UscfEventId" in df_f.columns:` gates the per-event performance ratings; opponents.py:135 `matched = games[games["UscfOpponentId"] != ""] if "UscfOpponentId" in games.columns else games.iloc[0:0]`; games.py:115-129 wraps LessonIndicator, TagsDisplay, USCF status, and ChapterURL each in `if "<col>" in df_f.columns:`; lessons.py:54 `has_lessons = df[df["Lessons"].map(bool)] if "Lessons" in df.columns else df`. Since Sync guarantees these columns (unmatched = off state), the guards are dead code — but worse, they convert any future schema regression into silent feature disappearance (the games table would quietly drop its USCF and Lesson columns; events would quietly stop showing performance ratings) instead of a loud failure.
Why it matters
This is exactly the drift the contract was written to prevent: presence checks re-encode 'is USCF configured' logic in pages, and they mask bugs — a Sync change that dropped an enrichment column would pass smoke tests while features vanish from the UI.
How to fix
Delete the presence checks and index the columns directly (events.py, opponents.py, lessons.py); in games.py assign the derived columns unconditionally. If a defensive posture is wanted, assert the schema once in data.py, not per-page.
Expected improvement
Pages match the documented invariant, ~10 lines of dead branching removed, and schema regressions fail loudly at the store boundary instead of silently degrading the UI.
Evidence
events.py: `if "UscfEventId" in df_f.columns:` · opponents.py: `if "UscfOpponentId" in games.columns \\ else games.iloc[0:0]` · games.py: `if "Lessons" in df_f.columns:` / `if "UscfMatched" in df_f.columns:` · lessons.py: `if "Lessons" in df.columns else df`
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read pages/AGENTS.md (lines 52-53: "Enrichment columns always exist — never guard on 'is USCF configured' by checking for a column") and all four cited sites. Every guard exists exactly as quoted: events.py:342 `if "UscfEventId" in df_f.columns:` gates per-event performance ratings; opponents.py:135 `if "UscfOpponentId" in games.columns else games.iloc[0:0]`; games.py:115/117/121/129 guard Lessons, Tags, UscfMatched, ChapterURL; lessons.py:54 `if "Lessons" in df.columns else df`. Failure mode is accurately described: a schema regression would silently drop UI features instead of failing loudly. Not covered by issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86 (checked recent commit descriptions; the dead-code passes did not touch these guards). Severity low is right — dead-code-plus-masking, no current user-visible bug.

Not covered by issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86 (checked recent commit subjects; the cleanup passes did not touch these guards).

Testing gaps (5)

mediumConfirmed tests effort: trivial

Open-redirect guard auth._safe_next has zero test coverage — the post-login `next` flow is entirely untested

tests/test_auth.py:52-124 · reviewer: tests-quality
What it is
auth.py's login flow reads a `next` form/query parameter and redirects to it after a successful login, with `_safe_next()` (auth.py:143-148) as the only defense against an open redirect: it accepts paths starting with `/` but rejects `//host` and absolute URLs. test_auth.py (230 lines) never sends a `next` value in any request — `grep -n next tests/test_auth.py` returns nothing. Neither the happy path (login lands on the requested page), the `//evil.example` refusal, nor the `https://evil.example` refusal is exercised anywhere in the suite.
Why it matters
This is the one security-sensitive string-parsing function in the auth module, and the exact kind of code that regresses silently: a future edit like `raw.startswith('/')` without the `//` check would reintroduce a classic open redirect (phishing vector on the login page) and every existing test would stay green. The rest of auth.py is well tested through the real Flask test client, which makes this hole stand out.
How to fix
Add a TestNextRedirect class to tests/test_auth.py using the existing `client` fixture: (1) POST /login with data={'username': 'daniel', 'password': 'hunter2', 'next': '/trends'} and assert the 302 Location is '/trends'; (2) same with next='//evil.example' and next='https://evil.example/x' asserting Location falls back to '/'; (3) GET /login?next=/trends and assert the hidden input carries the escaped value.
Expected improvement
The only open-redirect defense in the codebase becomes regression-protected; four cheap tests close the largest untested branch in auth.py.
Evidence
auth.py: `def _safe_next(raw: str) -> str: ... if raw.startswith("/") and not raw.startswith("//"): return raw` — and in tests/test_auth.py `grep "next"` yields no matches; `_login()` posts only `{"username": ..., "password": ...}`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed. auth.py lines 119-148 match the finding exactly: POST /login redirects to _safe_next(request.form.get("next","")), GET pre-fills the hidden next input, and _safe_next (143-148) is the only open-redirect guard, with the quoted startswith("/")/startswith("//") logic. grep for "next" in tests/test_auth.py (230 lines) returns zero matches; no other test file touches _safe_next or the next parameter (other grep hits are Python next() iterator calls). Not covered by excluded PRs #82-#86 or issues #80/#40. Cited file/lines are accurate. Suggested fix is sound; worth also adding a backslash case (next='/\\evil.example') since some browsers treat /\ as scheme-relative and the current guard would pass it through — a latent weakness the new tests should pin down.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Verified. auth.py:126 and :132 feed request `next` through _safe_next (auth.py:143-148), which is exactly as quoted: accepts paths starting with "/" but not "//", else returns "/". grep for "next"/"_safe_next" across the entire tests/ directory (not just test_auth.py) returns zero matches; _login() in tests/test_auth.py:52 posts only username/password. So neither the accept branch (raw.startswith("/") true path) nor either rejection case is ever executed in the suite — the True branch of the guard literally never runs under test. The proposed fix is sound and drops straight into the existing app/client fixtures. Two refinements: (1) the file/line anchor "tests/test_auth.py:52-124" is loose — the gap is the absence of any TestNextRedirect-style class, best anchored near _login() at line 52 or after TestLogin (lines 86-116); (2) materiality nuance: the before_request gate (auth.py:117) redirects to login WITHOUT appending ?next=, so the app itself never generates a next link — the parameter is only reachable via externally crafted URLs. That makes the "happy path lands on /trends" test less important, but it makes the guard tests MORE important, since attacker-crafted ?next= links are precisely the open-redirect phishing vector the guard exists for. Not excluded by issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86 (the coverage-gate PR added a line-coverage gate, which does not force branch/behavioral coverage here). Medium severity is fair for an untested security guard.
mediumConfirmed tests effort: small

Engine mate-score parsing ([%eval #N] → ±_MATE_CP) has no asserting test anywhere in the suite

tests/test_engine_analysis_core.py:60-99 · reviewer: tests-quality
What it is

Why it matters
Mate evals are common in real OTB blunder-heavy games (Daniel's demo seed has 20 of them), and this is exactly the branch where a python-chess API change or a refactor of _node_cp (e.g. dropping the mate_score kwarg, which makes .score() return None for mates) would silently mark every mate-bearing ply eval-less — degrading or corrupting critical-moment detection, accuracy, and the error profile with all current tests green. Qd8 was best. }`, then assert via analyze_game(): eval_after == -100.0 pawns (i.e. _MATE_CP folded), win_pct_after < 1, the move classifies as a blunder, and it becomes the critical moment. Add one case with a malformed directive (e.g. `[%eval xyz]`) asserting the ply degrades to eval-less rather than raising.

The mate branch of eval parsing — currently exercised only incidentally with zero assertions — becomes pinned; regressions in _node_cp/mate handling fail loudly instead of silently zeroing analysis on mate-bearing games.

_real_round's ambiguous-forfeit refusal (ADR 0007 'match, never guess') is untested — only the single-forfeit case is covered

tests/test_uscf_core.py:1878-1930 · reviewer: tests-quality
What it is
uscf_core._real_round (uscf_core.py:582-590) attaches a real round number to an unmatched forfeit Game only when exactly one forfeit-outcome round exists against that opponent: `if len(forfeit_rounds) == 1: # ambiguity → no guess`. TestAttachRoundNumbers covers the single-forfeit case (`assert list(forfeit["UscfRound"]) == [4]`, line 1902) and the no-crosstable case, but there is no test where two forfeit rounds against the same opponent exist — the branch that must refuse (return None) per ADR 0007. The zero-forfeit-rounds and missing-opponent-id (`if not opponent_id: return None`) sub-branches are likewise unasserted.
Why it matters
This is a designed refusal branch of the 'match, never guess' policy, and the natural bug — someone 'simplifying' to `if forfeit_rounds: return forfeit_rounds[0]` — would guess a round on ambiguity, exactly what ADR 0007 forbids, with no test failing. The matching engine's other refusal branches (ambiguous name candidates, two missing IDs) are all explicitly tested, so this one is an inconsistency in an otherwise disciplined pattern.
How to fix
In TestAttachRoundNumbers, build a standings dict with two RoundOutcome entries in _FORFEIT_OUTCOMES against the same opponent id (e.g. an Unpaired and a Forfeit in two sections), an unmatched forfeit Game against that opponent, and assert `pd.isna(attached['UscfRound']).all()` for it.
Expected improvement
The last unguarded refusal branch of the matching policy gets a regression test, matching the coverage discipline of the name-pass ambiguity tests.
Evidence
uscf_core.py:588 `if len(forfeit_rounds) == 1:  # ambiguity → no guess`; test_uscf_core.py:1902 asserts only the one-forfeit case `assert list(forfeit["UscfRound"]) == [4]` — no test constructs multiple forfeit rounds.

The other ADR 0007 refusal branches are explicitly tested (e.g. matched-game candidate consumption and ambiguous name-fallback tests elsewhere in the file), so this is a genuine gap in an otherwise consistent pattern. Proposed fix is sound; note that `attach_round_numbers` keys my_rounds by (event_id, section, opponent_id) while the forfeit lookup scans across all sections, so the two-sections construction in how_to_fix is the right way to build the ambiguity. Severity low is correct — no runtime bug today, purely a missing regression guard.

refresh()'s empty-result branch (Sync succeeds but returns zero games) is untested

tests/test_data.py:787-866 · reviewer: tests-quality
What it is
data.refresh() has a dedicated branch for a Sync that reaches Lichess but yields no games: `if result.df.empty: return RefreshOutcome(status="error", error=f"No games found...")` (data.py:443-447), which must return before `_swap` so current data survives. TestRefresh covers new games, no-change, exception-during-Sync, concurrent Sync, and refresh-before-initialize, but no test stubs the study to return an empty/blank PGN on refresh. `grep -rn 'No games found' tests/` returns nothing — the equivalent initialize() branch is tested (test_empty_studies_raise_clear_error) but the refresh path, whose contract is different (error outcome + data untouched instead of raising), is not.
Why it matters
This is the branch that protects a healthy dashboard from a user accidentally emptying their Study (or a Lichess export hiccup returning headers-only PGN): the atomic-swap guarantee says current data must remain. A regression that moved the emptiness check after _swap, or let it raise, would wipe the store on a bad refresh and no existing test would notice.
How to fix
Add to TestRefresh: initialize with sample_pgn_text, then `with stub_studies(study1="")` call data.refresh(); assert outcome.status == 'error', 'No games found' in outcome.error, data.get_df() is unchanged (same object or same length 7), and data.synced_at() did not advance.
Expected improvement
The remaining untested failure branch of refresh() — the one guarding against data loss on an emptied Study — becomes pinned.
Evidence
data.py:443-447 `if result.df.empty: return RefreshOutcome(status="error", error=f"No games found in designated Studies: {store.study_ids}")`; `grep -rn 'No games found' tests/` → no matches.

lichess_client's generic non-200 branch (429/5xx → LichessError) is untested

tests/test_lichess_client.py:53-116 · reviewer: tests-quality
What it is
fetch_study_pgn raises bare LichessError for any non-200/non-404 status (lichess_client.py:89-92: `if response.status_code != 200: raise LichessError(...)`). test_lichess_client.py covers 200, 404, Timeout, and ConnectionError, but never a 429 (Lichess rate limit, a realistic response for study export) or 5xx. Downstream, sync._fetch's per-Study degradation catches base `LichessError` (sync.py:132), so the contract that a 429 is a LichessError subclass instance — not an uncaught exception type — is what keeps a rate-limited Sync from crashing the app; that contract has no test at either layer.
Why it matters
The uscf_client tests explicitly cover the analogous branch ('A 5xx ... is a UscfError, not a crash', test_uscf_client.py:231), so the Lichess side is the asymmetric gap. If someone changed the branch to raise requests.HTTPError via raise_for_status(), sync's `except LichessError` would stop catching it, a Lichess 429 would take down startup/refresh, and no test would fail.
How to fix
Add one test mirroring the USCF client's: mock requests.get to return _response(429, "") (and/or 503) and assert pytest.raises(LichessError) with the status code named in the message; optionally assert it is not a StudyNotFoundError so callers can distinguish.
Expected improvement
Parity with the USCF client's error-branch coverage; the exception-type contract sync.py relies on for per-Study degradation is protected.
Evidence
lichess_client.py:89-92 `if response.status_code != 200: raise LichessError(f"Lichess returned HTTP {response.status_code}...")`; test file has only test_returns_pgn_text..., test_unknown_study_id_raises_not_found (404), timeout, and connection-error cases.

Config & dependencies (5)

mediumConfirmed deploy effort: small

All dependencies are unpinned floor constraints with no lock file, so every Docker build and CI run resolves a different, unreproducible set

requirements.txt:1-8 · reviewer: deploy-config
What it is
requirements.txt (which the Dockerfile installs) and pyproject.toml both use only `>=` floors — `dash>=4.0.0`, `pandas>=2.0.0`, `numpy>=1.24.0`, etc. — with no upper bounds and no lock file (no pip-tools/uv lock, no `pip freeze` snapshot). Every `docker build`, `fly deploy`, and CI run resolves whatever is newest on PyPI at that moment.
Why it matters
A routine redeploy can silently pull a breaking major release (numpy 1.24 → 3.x is permitted by `numpy>=1.24.0`; pandas and dash likewise) and take the production app down with no code change to bisect. It also means CI green today does not certify the image built tomorrow — the coverage/typecheck gates validate a different dependency set than the one deployed. For a resume-showcase repo, a reviewer running `make install` months from now may hit an environment the code was never tested against.
How to fix
Generate a pinned lock (e.g. `pip-compile requirements.in` or `uv pip compile`) and have the Dockerfile and CI install from the pinned file, keeping the loose floors in pyproject.toml as the abstract dependency declaration. Refresh the pins deliberately via PRs.
Expected improvement
Reproducible images and CI runs; dependency upgrades become explicit, reviewable diffs instead of deploy-time surprises.
Evidence
requirements.txt:
```
dash>=4.0.0
dash-bootstrap-components>=2.0.0
plotly>=5.18.0
pandas>=2.0.0
numpy>=1.24.0
```
Dockerfile: `RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt`
Verifier notes (2)

No lock file anywhere in repo root (no uv.lock, poetry.lock, requirements.in, *.lock, no pip freeze snapshot). Dockerfile line 4 runs `pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt` as claimed; CI (.github/workflows/ci.yml lines 23/42/61) also installs directly from the loose files, so CI and the deployed image can resolve different dependency sets over time. Evidence quoted in the finding is real and in context. Not a duplicate of excluded items: PRs #82-#86 added a coverage gate and shared mypy scope but did not pin dependencies; issues #80/#40 are polish/design, not dependency reproducibility. Suggested fix (compile a pinned lock, install from it in Dockerfile/CI, keep floors in pyproject.toml as abstract deps) is appropriate. Severity medium is fair for a resume-showcase app with periodic redeploys.

Makefile `lint` runs ruff with --fix while CI runs check-only, so the local target mutates files and diverges from the gate

Makefile:40-41 · reviewer: deploy-config
What it is
`make lint` executes `ruff check . --fix`, which silently rewrites source files, whereas CI's lint job runs plain `ruff check .`. A developer whose habit is 'make lint passed, push' can push the pre-fix files (fixes applied locally but not staged/committed are easy to miss in an otherwise clean run) and have CI fail on violations that `make lint` already auto-repaired — or worse, commit mechanical changes they never reviewed.
Why it matters
The repo's own recent work (PR #84) went out of its way to make Makefile and CI share one mypy scope and one coverage gate 'so the two can't drift'; the lint target is the one remaining pair that behaves differently locally vs in CI, and it is also the only Make target with side effects on the working tree.
How to fix
Make `lint` check-only (`$(RUFF) check .`) to mirror CI, and add a separate explicit `fix` or `format` target for the mutating variant.
Expected improvement
Local and CI lint agree; no surprise working-tree mutations from a target named 'lint'.
Evidence
Makefile: `lint: install-dev  ## Lint with ruff\n\t$(RUFF) check . --fix` vs ci.yml: `- name: Run ruff\n  run: ruff check .`
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/Makefile lines 40-41: `lint: install-dev` runs `$(RUFF) check . --fix` — exactly as claimed, and it is the only Make target that mutates the working tree. CI (.github/workflows/ci.yml lines 25-26) runs plain `ruff check .`. Cited lines and evidence are accurate. Not covered by excluded PRs #82-#86: PR #84 unified the mypy scope and coverage gate but left the lint target's --fix divergence in place (still present at HEAD f8d96f1). Proposed fix (check-only lint plus a separate `fix`/`format` target) is reasonable. Severity low is appropriate — worst case is a locally-green/CI-red surprise or an unreviewed auto-fix commit, not a correctness bug.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/Makefile (full) and .github/workflows/ci.yml lint job. Confirmed exactly as described: Makefile lines 40-41 are `lint: install-dev` / `$(RUFF) check . --fix`, while CI runs plain `ruff check .` (ci.yml line 26). There is no separate `fix`/`format` target in the Makefile, and no doc (AGENTS.md/README/CONTEXT.md) documents the --fix behavior as intentional, so it is not a documented invariant. The materiality framing holds: commit 6fc2d24 (PR #84) deliberately unified the mypy scope and coverage gate between Makefile and CI (test target uses the same --cov-fail-under=92 as CI), leaving lint as the only local/CI divergence and the only Make target that mutates the working tree. One nuance slightly softens impact: since --fix runs locally, `make lint` passing means violations were auto-repaired, so a developer who commits everything afterward would not fail CI — the failure mode requires pushing without staging the auto-fixed files, or committing unreviewed mechanical edits. That keeps severity at low, not medium. Proposed fix (check-only lint + explicit `fix` target) is correct and harmless; `.PHONY` line would need the new target added.

config.py DEBUG re-implements parse_bool inline three lines below other settings that use it

config.py:98 · reviewer: duplication-deadcode
What it is
config.py defines parse_bool (line 24-26, `raw.strip().lower() in ("1", "true", "yes")`) and uses it for DEMO_MODE (line 75), but DEBUG at line 98 hand-rolls the same check without the strip: `os.environ.get("DEBUG", "").lower() in ("1", "true", "yes")`. Besides the duplication, `DEBUG="true "` (trailing whitespace) parses as False while `DEMO_MODE="true "` parses as True — an inconsistency between the two boolean settings.
Why it matters
Two parsing rules for the same concept in a 100-line config module is exactly the drift the parse_* helpers exist to prevent; the whitespace inconsistency is a (tiny) real behavioral difference.
How to fix
Change line 98 to `DEBUG: bool = parse_bool(os.environ.get("DEBUG", ""))`.
Expected improvement
Consistent boolean env parsing across all settings.
Evidence
config.py:26 `return raw.strip().lower() in ("1", "true", "yes")` vs config.py:98 `DEBUG: bool = os.environ.get("DEBUG", "").lower() in ("1", "true", "yes")`

README Project Structure tree still lists docs/adr/ after the MADR migration to docs/decisions/

fly.toml still sets WEB_CONCURRENCY, which ADR 0006 explicitly says was removed

fly.toml:10 · reviewer: docs-drift
What it is
ADR 0006 states: "`WEB_CONCURRENCY` used to let an env var override the worker count; it was removed so nobody can trip the constraint by accident." But fly.toml [env] still ships `WEB_CONCURRENCY = "1"`. The variable is currently inert (gunicorn.conf.py hardcodes `workers = 1`, and an explicit config-file setting overrides gunicorn's WEB_CONCURRENCY-derived default), so this is doc/config drift rather than a live bug — the ADR's factual claim about the codebase is contradicted by the deploy config it describes.
Why it matters
The single-worker constraint is documented as load-bearing for both the Sync swap and per-user isolation. A leftover WEB_CONCURRENCY line invites exactly the accident the ADR says was made impossible: someone bumps it to "4" in fly.toml expecting it to work, and when it silently doesn't (or if gunicorn.conf.py's hardcoding is ever relaxed, when it silently does), the mental model from the ADR is wrong either way.
How to fix
Delete the `WEB_CONCURRENCY = "1"` line from fly.toml [env], completing the removal ADR 0006 records.
Expected improvement
The deploy config matches the ADR's stated invariant; no dangling knob suggests the worker count is configurable.
Evidence
fly.toml line 10: `WEB_CONCURRENCY   = "1"` vs docs/decisions/0006-single-worker-in-memory-store.md: "`WEB_CONCURRENCY` used to let an env var override the worker count; it was removed so nobody can trip the constraint by accident." gunicorn.conf.py line 17 hardcodes `workers = 1`.

Not a duplicate of issues #80/#40 or PRs #82-#86 (those PRs added ADR 0006 content but left the deploy configs untouched). Severity low is appropriate — pure doc/config drift, no runtime effect today.
