_extract_comments claims 'document order' but walks mainline-deep-first, so sideline comments are emitted after all later mainline comments

coach_match_core.py:187-204 · reviewer: coach-review-matching
What it is
The docstring promises comments 'in document order', and CoachChapter.comments repeats the claim ('the coach's prose, in document order'). The walk recurses `for child in node.variations: walk(child, ply + 1)` — python-chess puts the mainline continuation at variations[0], so the entire mainline is exhausted before any sideline is visited. In PGN document order a variation's comments appear immediately after the move they branch from; here a coach comment inside a variation at move 5 is emitted after a mainline comment at move 40. Today this is masked because the only cross-module consumer, data.get_coach_notes (data.py:854), re-sorts by move_number — but that stable sort also cannot restore document order among same-move comments (a sideline comment on move 12 lands after every mainline-continuation comment tagged move 12), and any future consumer trusting the field docstring inherits the scrambled order. Ply attribution itself is correct (all variations of a node are moves at ply+1), and move_number=(ply+1)//2 is right for both colors.
Why it matters
The dataclass contract is the API here (the module is deliberately framework-agnostic); a documented ordering guarantee that the code does not provide is a latent bug for the next consumer, and already produces subtly wrong interleaving for multiple notes on the same move in the Coach's Notes feed.
How to fix
Either fix the docstrings to say 'mainline-first depth-first order, tagged by ply', or produce true document order by visiting each node's comment, then its sidelines (variations[1:]) recursively, then continuing along variations[0] iteratively.
Expected improvement
The API contract matches behavior; same-move coach notes render in the order the coach wrote them.
Evidence
"""Every prose comment in the Chapter tree, engine directives stripped,
    in document order. ..."""
    ...
        for child in node.variations:
            walk(child, ply + 1)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/coach_match_core.py lines 130-220 and data.py lines 830-862. All cited evidence is real and current. The docstring of _extract_comments (lines 188-190) says "in document order" and the CoachChapter.comments field comment (line 92, not quoted in the finding's line range but claimed and confirmed) repeats "the coach's prose, in document order". The walk (lines 193-201) recurses `for child in node.variations: walk(child, ply + 1)`, which fully exhausts variations[0]'s subtree (the entire remaining mainline plus its nested sidelines) before visiting variations[1:]. True PGN document order interleaves a sideline immediately after the mainline move it branches from, so the traversal is mainline-deep-first, not document order — the finding's mechanics are correct. Ply attribution is indeed correct (every child of a node is at ply+1). The masking claim also checks out: data.py:854 stable-sorts by move_number, which repairs cross-move ordering but cannot restore intra-move-number document order (sideline comment tagged move N lands after mainline comments tagged move N regardless of source position). Minor corrections: (1) the field-docstring claim lives at line 92, outside the cited 187-204 range; (2) practical impact is very small — after the move_number re-sort the only observable scramble is among multiple comments sharing a move_number, and no other consumer of .comments exists today (grep confirms only data.get_coach_notes iterates it). Severity low is right; it's a docs/contract-accuracy issue, and the proposed fix options are both valid.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/coach_match_core.py lines 120-220 and data.py lines 810-862, plus grepped all consumers and tests. Confirmed: _extract_comments (lines 187-204) recurses `for child in node.variations: walk(child, ply+1)` — python-chess puts the mainline continuation at variations[0], so the entire mainline subtree is exhausted before any sideline branching from it is visited. That is NOT PGN document order (where a sideline's comments appear immediately after the move they branch from), yet the docstring (lines 188-190) and the CoachComment field comment on line 92 ("the coach's prose, in document order") both promise it, and comments_for() (line 124-127) exposes the same tuple as public API. Mitigation check: the only cross-module consumer is data.get_coach_notes (data.py:841, stable re-sort at 854), which masks cross-move scrambling but preserves the wrong relative order for multiple comments tagged the same move_number (mainline-continuation comment before an earlier-in-document sideline comment). No test pins ordering (test_coach_match_core.py asserts counts, not order). Ply/move_number attribution is correct as the finding states. Not covered by issues #40/#80 or PRs #82-#86. Impact is essentially a contract-accuracy/docs issue with a marginal same-move ordering artifact in the Coach's Notes feed; severity low is right, and the cheapest fix is the docstring correction (both line 92 and 188-190), with the true-document-order walk (comment, then variations[1:], then continue along variations[0]) as the alternative if the guarantee is worth keeping.
lowConfirmed backend effort: trivial

activate() docstring contradicts _current(): unknown users get a fresh registered store, not the default store

data.py:147-169 · reviewer: multiuser-tenant-isolation
What it is
activate()'s docstring says "``None`` (or an unknown user) falls back to the default store", but the code sets `_active.user = username if username else _DEFAULT_USER` — any non-empty unknown name is kept as-is, and _current() then lazily creates a brand-new empty Store and permanently inserts it into _registry (`_registry[key] = store`). So an unknown user gets a fresh empty store, not the default store, and the registry grows by one entry per distinct unknown key. Today the web path cannot reach this: the auth gate re-validates membership on every request (`if session.get(_SESSION_KEY) in users: return None` at auth.py:115) before _activate_request_user runs, so a stale session for a removed user is bounced to /login rather than activated. The lazy-insert path is only reachable by future in-process callers that activate unvalidated names.
Why it matters
The current behavior is actually the safer one — an unknown key isolating to an empty store beats silently serving the default store's data — but the docstring documents the dangerous behavior, so a future maintainer reading it (e.g. when adding an API token path or background job that bypasses auth.current_user()) will believe unknown names are harmless fallbacks. The silent unbounded _registry insert also means any such future caller leaks a Store per unique bad key with no log line.
How to fix
Fix the activate() docstring to state the real contract (unknown user -> isolated empty store, registered on first accessor touch), and consider logging a warning in _current() when it materializes a store for a key absent from the registry, since in the gated app that indicates a caller bypassed validation.
Expected improvement
The documented contract matches the code, and any future path that activates unvalidated usernames announces itself in the logs instead of silently minting stores.
Evidence
data.py:149-154 docstring `"None (or an unknown user) falls back to the default store"` vs data.py:154 `_active.user = username if username else _DEFAULT_USER` and data.py:165-168 `store = _registry.get(key)\n    if store is None:\n        store = Store()\n        _registry[key] = store`; gate check auth.py:115 `if session.get(_SESSION_KEY) in users:`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/data.py lines 130-185 and auth.py lines 100-129. All cited evidence is real and accurately quoted: the activate() docstring (data.py:150) says "``None`` (or an unknown user) falls back to the default store", but line 154 is `_active.user = username if username else _DEFAULT_USER`, so any non-empty unknown name is kept as-is; _current() (data.py:161-169) then lazily creates a fresh Store and permanently inserts it into _registry (`_registry[key] = store` at line 168) — a distinct empty store per unknown key, not the default store. The finding's own caveat is also correct: the web path is gated by auth.py:115 (`if session.get(_SESSION_KEY) in users: return None`), which re-validates membership before activation, so the mismatch is unreachable via HTTP today and only matters for future in-process callers. Note _current()'s own docstring (lines 162-163) already documents the actual behavior ("unknown users get a fresh, empty store"), so the contradiction is between activate()'s docstring and the rest of the module — a pure docs fix on activate() plus an optional warning log, exactly as the finding proposes. Line range 147-169 is accurate. Severity low is right; no duplicate in the excluded issues/PRs (checked against #80/#40/#82-#86 descriptions — none touch data.py store semantics).
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/data.py:120-199 and auth.py:95-134. Confirmed: activate() docstring (data.py:150) claims unknown users fall back to the default store, but data.py:154 keeps any non-empty name and _current() (data.py:164-168) lazily creates and registers a fresh empty Store per unknown key. auth.py:115 gate check confirmed — web path cannot reach this with an unvalidated name, so impact is limited to future in-process callers, as the finding says. Correction/addition: _current()'s own docstring (data.py:162-163) already documents the real behavior ("unknown users get a fresh, empty store"), so the lazy-create is intentional and the defect is purely the stale/contradictory activate() docstring — two docstrings five lines apart disagree. Severity low is right; fix (reword activate() docstring, optionally warn on lazy materialization) is appropriate.

Appendix A — Refuted findings

Reported by a reviewer, then rejected by the adversarial verifiers. Kept for transparency.

mediumRefuted backend effort: small

ensure_synced/sync_user run the full Sync without the store's sync_lock — check-then-act race duplicates first-request Syncs

data.py:541-546, 253-259 · reviewer: sync-store
What it is
Store.sync_lock is documented as "Guards against doubled Syncs", but only refresh() acquires it. The multi-user lazy path — app.py's before_request hook calling data.ensure_synced(user), which does `if store is not None and not store.initialized: sync_user(username)` — has no locking at all, and _sync_store() sets `store.initialized = True` only after the check. A first page load in Dash fires many parallel callback POSTs; in any threaded server every one of those threads sees initialized=False and each launches a complete Sync of the same store concurrently: N duplicate Lichess/USCF fetch storms, N interleaved store.df rebinds (compounding the non-atomic-swap window above), and N redundant Anthropic-billed summary passes racing on the same analysis_cache.json. The same unguarded _sync_store can also run concurrently with a lock-holding refresh() for that store. Under the deployed gunicorn config (sync worker, 1 thread) requests are serialized so this is currently latent in production, but data.py's own model explicitly assumes threading ("The active user is a thread-local set per request"), and the dev server is threaded.
Why it matters
The one concurrency guard the store has does not cover the multi-user code path it was built alongside (issue #72). Any move to gunicorn threads>1 — or simply developing against the Dash dev server with a multi-user config — produces duplicate paid Anthropic calls, hammers the USCF API the project explicitly tries to be polite to, and interleaves partial df states across threads.
How to fix
Acquire store.sync_lock inside _sync_store (or in ensure_synced around the initialized check-and-sync), re-checking store.initialized after acquiring; keep refresh()'s non-blocking acquire semantics by having ensure_synced skip (not block) when the lock is held.
Expected improvement
Exactly one Sync per store regardless of request concurrency; the initialized flag and sync_lock actually enforce what their comments claim.
Evidence
data.py: "def ensure_synced(username: str) -> None:\n    ...\n    if store is not None and not store.initialized:\n        sync_user(username)" and _sync_store: "store.initialized = True\n    try:\n        result = sync_studies(" — no sync_lock use anywhere except refresh(): "if not store.sync_lock.acquire(blocking=False):"
Verifier notes (3)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/data.py (lines 120-146, 250-290, 414-473, 520-547), app.py (before_request at 147-152), gunicorn.conf.py, and Dockerfile. Confirmed: sync_lock is acquired only in refresh() (acquire at line 431, release at 466). ensure_synced (lines 541-546) does an unguarded `if store is not None and not store.initialized: sync_user(username)` check-then-act, and _sync_store (line 258) sets store.initialized = True with no lock — so under any threaded server, N parallel first-load requests each see initialized=False and each run a full Sync (Lichess + USCF + analysis + coach passes), and an unguarded _sync_store can also run concurrently with a lock-holding refresh() on the same store. Cited line numbers are exact. Corrections/nuance: (1) the lock's docstring (line 131) says "Guards against doubled Syncs (button mashing)" — i.e. it was scoped to the Sync-button path, so the finding's phrasing that it "does not cover the multi-user code path it was built alongside" slightly overstates the documented intent, but the gap is real; (2) production impact is confirmed latent: gunicorn.conf.py sets workers=1 with no threads setting (default sync worker, 1 thread), so requests are serialized in the deployed config; the race is live only under the Dash dev server (threaded Flask) or any future threads>1 config, exactly as the finding says. The proposed fix (acquire sync_lock in _sync_store or around ensure_synced's check, re-check initialized after acquiring, skip rather than block when held) is sound. Severity medium is appropriate: real check-then-act bug with paid-API duplication consequences, but currently latent in the deployed configuration.
  • REFUTE (impact lens, high confidence): Read data.py (Store fields 100-133, _sync_store 253-276, refresh 414-466, sync_user/ensure_synced 523-546), app.py in full, gunicorn.conf.py, and docs/decisions/0006. The code-level mechanics are accurately described: ensure_synced does an unlocked check-then-act, _sync_store never touches sync_lock, and only refresh() (data.py:431/466) acquires it. But the failure scenario is unreachable in every wiring the repo actually has, which is why I refute on materiality. (1) app.py:89-93 registers users and then EAGERLY calls data.sync_user(username) for every user at build time, at module import — before gunicorn (or any server) accepts a single request. (2) _sync_store sets store.initialized = True as its FIRST statement (data.py:258), and sync_user swallows SyncError/RuntimeError after that flag is set — so even a user whose eager Sync fails ends up initialized=True. Therefore after boot, ensure_synced's `not store.initialized` check is false for every registered user, permanently: the before_request hook never triggers a Sync, and the "first page load fires N parallel duplicate Syncs" storm cannot happen. (3) The finding's dev-server escalation is factually wrong: main()'s build_app call (app.py:242-249) passes no users, so the threaded Dash dev server never installs the before_request hook or multi-user stores at all; the multi-user app only boots via the module-level block, which does the eager sync. (4) Concurrent _sync_store vs refresh() also has no live window — refresh() is only reachable via a callback after boot, when all eager syncs have completed. (5) ADR 0006 + gunicorn.conf.py hardcode one sync worker (WEB_CONCURRENCY override deliberately removed) and document single-threaded request handling as a load-bearing correctness constraint, so "move to threads>1" is an explicitly rejected configuration, not a plausible drift. Minor correction to the finding's evidence: the sync_lock comment (data.py:131) reads "Guards against doubled Syncs (button mashing)" — it scopes the lock to the refresh-button path it actually covers, so the docs do not overpromise as claimed. Residual truth: register_users' docstring (data.py:495-496) advertises a lazy "on first access" mode that, if a future caller ever used it on a threaded server, would need the lock ensure_synced lacks — a one-line hardening (acquire sync_lock in _sync_store, re-check initialized) is cheap and reasonable, but today this is defensive-code polish, not a bug. If kept at all, downgrade to info-level hardening.
  • REFUTE (existence lens, high confidence, tiebreaker): Read data.py (100-133, 253-276, 414-466, 483-546), app.py in full, gunicorn.conf.py, and grepped all callers of register_users/sync_user/ensure_synced. The cited code is real — ensure_synced's check-then-act is unlocked and _sync_store never takes sync_lock — but the described failure is unreachable in the current code: (1) app.py:92-93 eagerly runs data.sync_user() for every configured user at module import, before any request is served; (2) _sync_store sets store.initialized=True as its first statement (data.py:258) and sync_user swallows SyncError/RuntimeError, so after boot every registered user is permanently initialized=True and the before_request ensure_synced never triggers a Sync; (3) the finding's dev-server claim is wrong — main() (app.py:242-249) passes no users, so the threaded Dash dev server never runs the multi-user hook at all; (4) refresh() is only reachable via callbacks after boot, so no _sync_store/refresh overlap window exists; (5) gunicorn.conf.py hardcodes 1 sync worker/1 thread as an ADR 0006 correctness constraint, making threads>1 a rejected config, not plausible drift; (6) grep confirms app.py is the sole caller — no lazy-path consumer exists anywhere. Residual value: register_users' docstring advertises a lazy "on first access" mode that a future caller could use unsafely; taking sync_lock in _sync_store with an initialized re-check is cheap hardening. That is info-level defensive polish, not a bug as described. Minor correction: data.py:131's lock comment says "button mashing" — scoped to the path it covers, so the docs do not overpromise. This settles the prior verifier split in favor of refutation on materiality.
lowRefutedverifier suggests: info frontend effort: small

lpv-init.js: WeakSet mount-guard skips re-init when the same route re-renders with a different game (/game/A -> /game/B)

assets/lpv-init.js:23, 68-80 · reviewer: client-js-lpv-seam
What it is
initCard guards with `mounted.has(card)` on the `.game-board-card` wrapper and captures the PGNs into a closure (`var data = { game: mount.getAttribute("data-pgn-game") ... }`) exactly once. This is correct for the common navigation path (game_detail -> another page -> a different game_detail), because the intermediate page destroys the card node and Dash builds a fresh one, so the WeakSet entry is garbage-collected. But when the URL changes directly from /game/A to /game/B on the same path_template (address-bar edit of a deep link today; any future in-page game-to-game link, e.g. "other games vs this opponent"), React reconciles the structurally-identical page layout and can reuse the existing card DOM node, only updating attributes. Then mounted.has(card) is true, initCard returns early, the closure still holds game A's PGNs, and the visible board keeps showing game A while the surrounding metadata shows game B. (React's attribute update also lands on the original `.lpv` node the viewer already detached, so the new data-pgn-* payload is written to a node no longer in the document.)
Why it matters
The page docstring advertises the route as deep-linkable, and the failure mode is the worst kind — wrong data displayed with full confidence (game B's header over game A's moves). It is also a latent trap: the first PR that adds a game-to-game link (a natural feature for head-to-head) triggers it in normal UI flow.
How to fix
Key mounted-ness by content rather than node identity: stash the chapter id (or a hash of data-pgn-game) on the card, e.g. store `card.dataset.lpvMounted = data.game` at init and in scan() re-init when the current mount's data-pgn-game attribute differs — or have game_detail.py put the chapter_id on the card and compare that.
Expected improvement
Same-route param navigation re-mounts the viewer with the new game's PGN; the deep-link contract holds and future game-to-game links are safe by default.
Evidence
var mounted = new WeakSet();  ...  if (!mount || mounted.has(card)) { return; }
mounted.add(card);
var data = { game: mount.getAttribute("data-pgn-game") || "", ... };
Verifier notes (3)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read /Users/danielgentile/Projects/chess-dashboard/assets/lpv-init.js in full. The cited code is real and current: `var mounted = new WeakSet()` (line 23), `if (!mount || mounted.has(card)) return; mounted.add(card);` and the once-only closure capture of data-pgn-* attributes (lines 68-80). initCard never re-reads attributes after first mount, so a same-document /game/A -> /game/B transition where React reuses the card node would indeed keep showing game A's board; the file's own comment (lines 18-22) confirms the viewer replaces the .lpv node, supporting the detached-node claim. Two corrections. (1) The claimed reachable-today trigger is wrong: editing the address bar to a different deep link causes a full browser document load, which resets all JS state including the WeakSet — no bug there. (2) I verified no in-page game-to-game navigation exists today: game_detail.py (lines 116, 462, 476, 502) links only to /reconciliation, /games, and external Lichess/USCF URLs; the only /game/<id> links live in components.py (coach_note_card line 293, game_detail_path line 347, row_click_to_game line 411) and are rendered on other pages (lessons.py, games tables), so every current path to a second game destroys the card in between and the WeakSet entry with it. Back/forward history also cannot produce a direct A->B popstate without an A->B link having existed. So this is a genuinely latent trap (first PR adding a game-to-game link, e.g. head-to-head, triggers it), but it has zero user-reachable trigger in the current app — severity should drop from low to info. The proposed fix (key mounted-ness by data-pgn-game content on card.dataset instead of node identity) is sound; note the fix must also handle React writing new attributes to the detached original .lpv node, so comparing against the live mount's attribute only works if Dash/React re-renders the .lpv child (which recreates it) — stashing the chapter id on the card wrapper from game_detail.py, as the finding's alternative suggests, is the more robust variant. The React node-reuse behavior itself is plausible per standard reconciliation but was not demonstrated in a live browser.
  • REFUTE (impact lens, medium confidence): Read assets/lpv-init.js in full, pages/game_detail.py in full, and grepped all /game/ link producers (components.py lesson_card, coach_note_card, _game_card, row_click_to_game). Code quotes and line numbers in the finding are accurate, and the React node-reuse mechanism is plausible. But the finding is moot in the current code: (1) its only "today" trigger — address-bar edit from /game/A to /game/B — is a full browser page load, which resets the WeakSet and rescans, not a client-side Dash transition; (2) no in-app game-to-game link exists anywhere (game_detail renders links only to /games, /reconciliation, and external sites; all /game/<id> links live on Lessons/Games/Opponents pages), so every reachable A-to-B path passes through an intermediate page that destroys the card node, the path the finding concedes works; (3) back/forward history can never hold adjacent A/B entries without such a link. The WeakSet design is a deliberate, commented fix for a prior infinite-re-init browser hang (lpv-init.js lines 18-22). What remains is a latent trap for a hypothetical future game-to-game link; the proposed content-keyed guard (card.dataset.lpvMounted = data.game) is a sound cheap hardening if that feature is ever added, but nothing user-reachable is wrong today. At most an info-level hardening note, not a bug.
  • REFUTE (existence lens, high confidence, tiebreaker): Read assets/lpv-init.js in full (WeakSet guard line 23; `if (!mount || mounted.has(card)) return; mounted.add(card);` and the once-only data-pgn-* closure capture at lines 68-80 — code quotes in the finding are accurate). Grepped all /game/<id> link producers: components.py lines 293/351/415 (coach_note_card, game_detail_path, row-click helper), consumed only by pages/lessons.py, pages/events.py, pages/openings.py, and games tables. pages/game_detail.py itself links only to /games (lines 462, 476) and external sites — there is NO game-to-game link anywhere in the app today. The finding fails on its trigger, not its mechanics: (1) its sole "reachable today" scenario — editing the address bar from /game/A to /game/B — is a full browser document load, which discards all JS state including the WeakSet and re-runs scan(), so the board renders game B correctly; (2) every in-app path from one game to another necessarily passes through an intermediate page (Games/Lessons/Events/Openings), which destroys the card node — the path the finding itself concedes is safe; (3) browser history can never hold adjacent /game/A → /game/B entries without such a link existing, so back/forward cannot trigger it either. The WeakSet-on-card design is also a deliberate, commented fix for a prior infinite-re-init browser hang (lpv-init.js lines 18-22). What survives is a latent trap only: the first PR adding a direct game-to-game link (e.g. head-to-head) would hit stale-closure behavior IF React reuses the card node — plausible per reconciliation semantics but undemonstrated here. The proposed content-keyed guard (stash chapter id / data-pgn-game on card.dataset) is sound cheap hardening for that future; note the comparison must use a value on the card wrapper, not the .lpv node, since the viewer replaces .lpv and React may write new attributes to the detached original. As a bug in the current code as described, it does not exist — at most an info-level hardening note.

Appendix C — Method & coverage

Scoped reviewers each owned a subsystem × dimension slice, briefed on the project's intentional invariants so designs aren't reported as bugs — only violations of them. A completeness critic audited coverage and spawned extra reviewers (4 gap reviewer(s)). Findings were semantically deduplicated, then adversarially verified: two independent verifiers per finding (an existence lens that re-reads the code, an impact lens that hunts for mitigations and severity inflation), plus a tiebreaker on splits. Every finding cites file:line and a verbatim evidence snippet.
